The Ismā'īliyya Sect: Names and Hierarchical Structure
Describes the Ismā'īliyya sect, its seven names, and its hierarchical imamate structure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seven names of the Ismā'īliyya sect and their inner hierarchy of spiritual leadership.

Core Idea
The Ismā'īliyya prioritize inner meaning over outer, and have a seven-tiered hierarchy of prophets and imams.

The Ismā'īliyya are a Shī'ī sect known by many names, each reflecting a distinctive belief. This passage introduces their seven titles and explains their complex hierarchy of spiritual leaders, from the nāṭiq (speaker-prophet) down to the mukallib (one who argues like a hunting dog). As you read, notice how their interpretation of scripture leads to a systematic ranking of religious authority.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
The passage is dense with sect-specific terminology.
2
Identify the seven titles
List the seven names given: al-Bāṭiniyya, al-Qarāmiṭa, al-Ḥazmiyya, al-Sab'iyya, and their derivations. Notice how each title reflects a core belief.
The term 'Sab'iyya' comes from their belief in seven prophetic cycles.
3
Understand the hierarchical ranks
The passage describes a hierarchy: imam, ḥujja, dhū miṣṣa, abwāb (with grades). Map out the sequence and the role of each rank.
The mukallib is likened to a hunting dog who argues and persuades.
4
Reflect on the justification for bāṭin
They use Quran 57:13 to support their view that the inner meaning is intended and the outer leads to difficulty. Consider how this shapes their entire approach.
They trace this view to earlier sects al-Manṣūriyya and al-Janāḥiyya.
5
Connect to broader Islamic heresiography
Think about how this sect fits into the landscape of Shī'ī groups. The hierarchical structure is unique and differs from mainstream Shī'ism.
This passage is a classic example of how heresiographers categorize sects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإسماعيلية : ولقبوا بسبعة ألقاب بالباطنية لقولهم بباطن الكتاب دون ظاهره فإنهم قالوا : للقرآن ظاهر وباطن والمراد منه باطنه وظاهره المعلوم من اللغة ونسبة الباطن إلى الظاهر كنسبة اللب إلى القشر، والمتمسك بظاهره معذب بالمشقة في الاكتساب وباطنه مؤد إلى ترك العمل بظاهر وتمسكوا في ذلك بقوله تعالى فضرب بينهم بسور له باب باطنه فيه الرحمة وظاهره من قبله العذاب ﴾ [ الحديد : ١٣] وهذا القول أخذوه من المنصورية والجناحية (و) لقبوا ( بالقرامطة لأن أولهم ) الذي دعا الناس إلى مذهبهم رجل يقال له ( حمدان قرمط وهي إحدى قرى واسط، وبالحزمية لإباحتهم المحرمات والمحارم، وبالسبعية لأنهم زعموا أن النطقاء بالشرائع أي الرسل سبعة آدم ونوح وإبراهيم وموسى وعيسى ومحمد ومحمد المهدي سابع وبين كل اثنين ) من النطقاء ( سبعة أئمة يتممون شريعته ولا بد في كل سبعة بهم يقتدى وبهم يهتدى في الدين وهم متفاوتون في الرتب (إمام يؤدي عن الله ) وهو غاية الأدلة إلى دين الله ( وحجة يؤدى عنه ) أي عن الإمام ويحمل ويحتج به له ) وذو مصة يمص العلم من الحجة ) أي يأخذه منه، فهذه ثلاثة علمه ويحتج ( وأبواب وهم الدعاة فأكبر أي داع أكبر هو رابعهم ( يرفع درجات المؤمنين (و) داع ( مأذون يأخذ العهود على (الطالبين من أهل الظاهر فيدخلهم في ذمة الإمام ويفتح لهم باب العلم والمعرفة وهو خامسهم (ومكلب) قد ارتفعت درجته في الدين ولكن لم يؤذن له في الدعوة بل في الاحتجاج على الناس فهو ( يحتج ويرغب إلى الداعي ككلب الصائد ( حتى إذا احتج على أحد من أهل الظاهر وكسر عليه النطقاء من عصر
The Ismā'īliyya: and they were given seven titles: al-Bāṭiniyya because of their saying the inner meaning of the book without its outer meaning. For they said: The Quran has an outer and an inner, and the intended is its inner, while its outer is known from language. The relation of inner to outer is like the relation of kernel to shell. The one who holds to its outer is tormented with difficulty in acquisition, and its inner leads to abandoning work with the outer. And they adhered in that to His saying: 'Then a wall will be placed between them with a door, its inner side containing mercy, and its outer side from which is punishment.' (Quran 57:13) And this saying they took from al-Manṣūriyya and al-Janāḥiyya. And they were named al-Qarāmiṭa because their first [leader] who called people to their sect was a man called Ḥamdān Qarmaṭ, which is one of the villages of Wāsiṭ. And al-Ḥazmiyya due to their permitting forbidden things and marital relations. And al-Sab'iyya because they claimed that the speakers (nāṭiqūn) of the laws, i.e., the messengers, are seven: Adam, Noah, Abraham, Moses, Jesus, Muhammad, and Muhammad al-Mahdī as the seventh. And between every two of the nāṭiqūn there are seven imams who complete his law, and it is necessary in every seven that they be followed and guided in religion, and they are different in rank. [There is] an imam who conveys from God — he is the ultimate guide to God's religion; a proof (ḥujja) who conveys from him, i.e., from the imam, and conveys and argues for him; and a 'dhū miṣṣa' who sucks knowledge from the proof, i.e., takes it from him. So these are three. And 'abwāb' (gates) who are the callers (du'āt). The akbar (greater) caller is their fourth, he raises the degrees of the believers. And a ma'dhūn caller takes covenants from the seekers among the people of the outward, thus enters them into the guarantee of the imam and opens for them the door of knowledge and gnosis, and he is their fifth. And a mukallib who has advanced in rank in religion but has not been permitted for calling, but for arguing with people, so he argues and incites to the caller like the hunter's dog, until if he argues with one of the people of the outward and defeats him... the nāṭiqūn from the era?
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage describes the Ismā'īliyya sect in detail, noting their seven titles. They emphasize the inner (bāṭin) meaning of the Quran over the outer (ẓāhir). They justify this with a verse from Surah al-Hadid. They trace this view to earlier sects. They are also called Qarāmiṭa after their founder Ḥamdān Qarmaṭ. They permit forbidden acts. Their Sabb'iyya name comes from their belief in seven speaker-prophets (nāṭiqūn) and seven imams between each pair. They have a hierarchical system: the imam (leader from God), the ḥujja (proof), the dhū miṣṣa (one who draws knowledge), the abwāb (gates/callers) including the greater caller, the mā'dhūn, and the mukallib (like a hunting dog who argues and persuades). The text cuts off mid-sentence.

Key Terms
الإسماعيلية
الباطنية
القرامطة
الحزمية
السبعية
النطقاء
الحجة
ذو مصة
أبواب
مأذون
مكلب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ismā'īliyya merely accept allegorical interpretation while still practicing outer rituals.
Correction: They believe the outer meaning leads to difficulty and that the inner meaning requires abandoning outer practice entirely.

Checkpoint
How many speaker-prophets (nāṭiqūn) do the Ismā'īliyya believe in?
A) Five
B) Seven
C) Twelve
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The Ismā'īliyya are distinguished by their belief in seven prophetic eras and a seven-tiered hierarchy of spiritual leaders, emphasizing inner interpretation over outer practice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever justified neglecting an Islamic obligation by telling yourself the 'spiritual essence' matters more than the outward act? The Ismā'īliyya used that reasoning to abandon worship. Read their claim again: 'its inner leads to abandoning work with the outer.' Is there any area of your life where you have done the same? Commit to correcting it today.
?
The Ismā'īliyya created an elite hierarchy of 'callers' who controlled access to knowledge. Who are the people you trust to explain Islam to you? Do you ever rely on a teacher or scholar without verifying from the Quran and Sunnah yourself? What step will you take this week to become more directly connected to the sources?
?
They permitted what Allah forbade (al-Ḥazmiyya). Think of a sin you have come to accept because 'everyone does it' or because you found a loophole. Would you defend that sin in front of Allah? The Ismā'īliyya's error was taking inner interpretation too far. Are you using any personal interpretation to permit what is clearly prohibited? Repent and return to the straight path.

The Mufawwida: Delegating Creation to a Prophet
Author describes the Mufawwida sect's doctrine of delegation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the doctrine of the Mufawwida sect and why Sunni theologians consider it a heresy.

Core Idea
The Mufawwida gave prophetic figures creative power, undermining divine exclusivity.

The first sect discussed by the author is the Mufawwida, or 'Delegationists'. They claimed that God delegated the creation of the world to Muhammad, and some said to Ali. This section explains their view and why it violates the principle of tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Mufawwida
Read the Arabic and translation carefully to grasp the claim: God created Muhammad and delegated creation to him.
Notice the alternative version delegating to Ali.
2
Identify the problem
Consider why attributing creation to anyone but God is a violation of tawhid.
3
Reflect on the implication
If a prophet or imam is the creator, then God is no longer the sole creator, contradicting Quranic teaching.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المفوضة : قالوا الله فوض خلق الدنيا إلى محمد ) أي الله خلق محمداً وفوض إليه خلق الدنيا فهو الخلاق لها بما فيها وقيل : فوض ذلك إلى علي. ( البدائية : جوزوا البدء على الله تعالى أي جوزوا أن يريد الله شيئاً ثم يبدو له أي يظهر عليه ما لم يكن ظاهراً له ويلزمه أن لا يكون الرب عالماً بعواقب الأمور ( النصيرية والإسحاقية : قالوا : حل الله في علي ) فإن ظهور الروحاني في الجسد الجسماني مما لا ينكر إما في جانب الخير فكظهور جبريل بصورة البشر، وإما في جانب الشر فكظهور الشيطان في صورة الإنسان قالوا ولما كان علي أولاده أفضل من غيرهم وكانوا مؤيدين بتأييدات متعلقة بباطن الأسرار قلنا ظهر الحق تعالى بصورته ونطق بلسانهم وأخذ بأيديهم ومن هاهنا أطلقنا الآلهة على الأئمة ألا ترى أن النبي قاتل المشركين وعلياً قاتل المنافقين فإن النبي يحكم بالظاهر والله يتولى السرائر )
The Mufawwida said: God delegated the creation of the world to Muhammad – meaning God created Muhammad and delegated to him the creation of the world, so he is the creator of it and what it contains. And it is said: He delegated that to Ali. The Bada'iyya permitted change of will (bada') for God Almighty, meaning they permitted that God wills something and then it becomes apparent to Him – i.e., something appears to Him that was not apparent to Him – and this necessitates that the Lord is not knowledgeable of the outcomes of matters. The Nasiriyya and Is-haqiyya said: God dwelled in Ali. For the appearance of the spiritual in the physical body is not denied, either on the side of good, like the appearance of Jibril in human form, or on the side of evil, like the appearance of Satan in human form. They said: Since Ali and his children were better than others and were supported by supports related to the inner secrets, we said: The Truth Almighty appeared in his form, spoke with their tongues, and took them by the hands. From here we called the Imams gods. Do you not see that the Prophet fought the polytheists, and Ali fought the hypocrites? For the Prophet judges by the apparent, and God undertakes the secrets.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage classifies three early heretical sects and explains their key doctrines. The Mufawwida (Delegationists) held that God delegated the creation of the world to Muhammad, and some said to Ali. This removes absolute creative power from God. The Bada'iyya (Permission of Alteration) claimed that God can change His mind, implying He was ignorant of future outcomes – a clear anthropomorphic doctrine. The Nasiriyya and Is-haqiyya taught that God incarnated in Ali. The author shows they rationalize this by comparing it to angelic or satanic appearances in human form. They claimed that the divine manifested in Ali and his descendants, speaking through them, which is why they call Imams gods. They even appeal to the Prophet's outward judgment vs. God's hidden knowledge as support. Each doctrine is countered by core Sunni principles of divine transcendence and immutability.

Key Terms
المفوضة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God can delegate His creative power to a prophet or imam.
Correction: In Sunni Islam, creation is an exclusive attribute of Allah. No creature, however honored, shares in this attribute.

Checkpoint
What is the core belief of the Mufawwida?
A) God created the world directly
B) God delegated creation to Muhammad or Ali
C) God incarnated in Ali
D) God can change His will

Key Takeaway
The Mufawwida heresy lies in attributing creation to a creature, undermining the oneness of God as Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself unconsciously elevating a beloved scholar or spiritual guide to a place where you feel they have near-absolute authority over your understanding of truth? How will you correct that tendency starting today?
?
The Mufawwida claimed for the Prophet (peace be upon him) a role he himself never claimed. Are there any beliefs in your heart about the Prophet or the awliya' that could be an exaggeration? Write down one and ask Allah to purify it.
?
If you truly believe that only Allah creates and sustains, why do you sometimes fear or depend on human approval more than His? What one concrete change can you make this week to realign your dependence?

The Bada'iyya: Permitting Change of Will in God
Author describes the Bada'iyya sect's doctrine of bada' (alteration) in God's will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Bada'iyya doctrine of bada' and why it implies ignorance in God.

Core Idea
The Bada'iyya claimed God can change His mind, which implies He was unaware of the future.

The second sect is the Bada'iyya, who permitted 'bada'' (alteration) on God. They claimed that God may will something and then later it becomes apparent to Him, implying that He was not fully aware of outcomes. This section explains their view and its logical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Bada'iyya
Read the Arabic and translation to understand their claim about God's will changing.
The phrase 'بدا له' means it became apparent to Him.
2
Recognize the implication
If God can change His will because something new appears to Him, then He was not all-knowing. This is the heresy.
3
Consider the Sunni response
Sunni theology affirms that God is omniscient and unchanging in His knowledge and will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المفوضة : قالوا الله فوض خلق الدنيا إلى محمد ) أي الله خلق محمداً وفوض إليه خلق الدنيا فهو الخلاق لها بما فيها وقيل : فوض ذلك إلى علي. ( البدائية : جوزوا البدء على الله تعالى أي جوزوا أن يريد الله شيئاً ثم يبدو له أي يظهر عليه ما لم يكن ظاهراً له ويلزمه أن لا يكون الرب عالماً بعواقب الأمور ( النصيرية والإسحاقية : قالوا : حل الله في علي ) فإن ظهور الروحاني في الجسد الجسماني مما لا ينكر إما في جانب الخير فكظهور جبريل بصورة البشر، وإما في جانب الشر فكظهور الشيطان في صورة الإنسان قالوا ولما كان علي أولاده أفضل من غيرهم وكانوا مؤيدين بتأييدات متعلقة بباطن الأسرار قلنا ظهر الحق تعالى بصورته ونطق بلسانهم وأخذ بأيديهم ومن هاهنا أطلقنا الآلهة على الأئمة ألا ترى أن النبي قاتل المشركين وعلياً قاتل المنافقين فإن النبي يحكم بالظاهر والله يتولى السرائر )
The Mufawwida said: God delegated the creation of the world to Muhammad – meaning God created Muhammad and delegated to him the creation of the world, so he is the creator of it and what it contains. And it is said: He delegated that to Ali. The Bada'iyya permitted change of will (bada') for God Almighty, meaning they permitted that God wills something and then it becomes apparent to Him – i.e., something appears to Him that was not apparent to Him – and this necessitates that the Lord is not knowledgeable of the outcomes of matters. The Nasiriyya and Is-haqiyya said: God dwelled in Ali. For the appearance of the spiritual in the physical body is not denied, either on the side of good, like the appearance of Jibril in human form, or on the side of evil, like the appearance of Satan in human form. They said: Since Ali and his children were better than others and were supported by supports related to the inner secrets, we said: The Truth Almighty appeared in his form, spoke with their tongues, and took them by the hands. From here we called the Imams gods. Do you not see that the Prophet fought the polytheists, and Ali fought the hypocrites? For the Prophet judges by the apparent, and God undertakes the secrets.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage classifies three early heretical sects and explains their key doctrines. The Mufawwida (Delegationists) held that God delegated the creation of the world to Muhammad, and some said to Ali. This removes absolute creative power from God. The Bada'iyya (Permission of Alteration) claimed that God can change His mind, implying He was ignorant of future outcomes – a clear anthropomorphic doctrine. The Nasiriyya and Is-haqiyya taught that God incarnated in Ali. The author shows they rationalize this by comparing it to angelic or satanic appearances in human form. They claimed that the divine manifested in Ali and his descendants, speaking through them, which is why they call Imams gods. They even appeal to the Prophet's outward judgment vs. God's hidden knowledge as support. Each doctrine is countered by core Sunni principles of divine transcendence and immutability.

Key Terms
البدائية
البدء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God can change His will due to new circumstances.
Correction: Sunni Islam teaches that God's knowledge is eternal and unchanging; He knows all outcomes before they occur, so His will does not change due to new information.

Checkpoint
What does the Bada'iyya doctrine imply about God's knowledge?
A) God knows everything before it happens
B) God may not know future outcomes
C) God is all-powerful
D) God incarnates in humans

Key Takeaway
The Bada'iyya heresy is that it denies God's eternal omniscience by allowing change in His will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that God's will could change based on new information, would you still have complete trust in His promises and warnings? Examine why your certainty depends on His unchanging knowledge.
?
Have you ever acted as if God needed to 'change His mind' about something in your life — like a sin you thought He might overlook or a good deed you thought He wouldn't reward? What does this reveal about your understanding of His omniscience?
?
The Bada'iyya heresy reduces God to a being who learns over time. In what ways do you unconsciously treat God as if He is learning or adapting to your actions (e.g., through 'cutting deals' or bargaining in prayer)? How can you repent from this subtle diminishment of His majesty?

beginner
4 min
The Nasiriyya and Is-haqiyya: Incarnation of God in Ali
Author describes the Nasiriyya and Is-haqiyya sects' doctrine of divine incarnation in Ali and the Imams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the incarnationist doctrines of the Nasiriyya and Is-haqiyya and their rationalizations.

Core Idea
These sects claimed God incarnated in Ali and the Imams, making them divine.

The third sect described is the Nasiriyya and Is-haqiyya, who believed that God indwelled in Ali and his descendants. They attempted to justify this by analogies from angelic appearances and by distinguishing between apparent judging and hidden knowledge. This section exposes their heresy of incarnation (hulul).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Nasiriyya and Is-haqiyya
Read the Arabic and translation to understand their claim that God appeared in Ali.
They compare it to Jibril appearing in human form.
2
Analyze their justification
They argue that spiritual beings can appear physically, so God can appear in Ali. The author shows the fallacy.
3
Identify the consequence
They call the Imams 'gods' and claim God speaks through them, which is shirk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المفوضة : قالوا الله فوض خلق الدنيا إلى محمد ) أي الله خلق محمداً وفوض إليه خلق الدنيا فهو الخلاق لها بما فيها وقيل : فوض ذلك إلى علي. ( البدائية : جوزوا البدء على الله تعالى أي جوزوا أن يريد الله شيئاً ثم يبدو له أي يظهر عليه ما لم يكن ظاهراً له ويلزمه أن لا يكون الرب عالماً بعواقب الأمور ( النصيرية والإسحاقية : قالوا : حل الله في علي ) فإن ظهور الروحاني في الجسد الجسماني مما لا ينكر إما في جانب الخير فكظهور جبريل بصورة البشر، وإما في جانب الشر فكظهور الشيطان في صورة الإنسان قالوا ولما كان علي أولاده أفضل من غيرهم وكانوا مؤيدين بتأييدات متعلقة بباطن الأسرار قلنا ظهر الحق تعالى بصورته ونطق بلسانهم وأخذ بأيديهم ومن هاهنا أطلقنا الآلهة على الأئمة ألا ترى أن النبي قاتل المشركين وعلياً قاتل المنافقين فإن النبي يحكم بالظاهر والله يتولى السرائر )
The Mufawwida said: God delegated the creation of the world to Muhammad – meaning God created Muhammad and delegated to him the creation of the world, so he is the creator of it and what it contains. And it is said: He delegated that to Ali. The Bada'iyya permitted change of will (bada') for God Almighty, meaning they permitted that God wills something and then it becomes apparent to Him – i.e., something appears to Him that was not apparent to Him – and this necessitates that the Lord is not knowledgeable of the outcomes of matters. The Nasiriyya and Is-haqiyya said: God dwelled in Ali. For the appearance of the spiritual in the physical body is not denied, either on the side of good, like the appearance of Jibril in human form, or on the side of evil, like the appearance of Satan in human form. They said: Since Ali and his children were better than others and were supported by supports related to the inner secrets, we said: The Truth Almighty appeared in his form, spoke with their tongues, and took them by the hands. From here we called the Imams gods. Do you not see that the Prophet fought the polytheists, and Ali fought the hypocrites? For the Prophet judges by the apparent, and God undertakes the secrets.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage classifies three early heretical sects and explains their key doctrines. The Mufawwida (Delegationists) held that God delegated the creation of the world to Muhammad, and some said to Ali. This removes absolute creative power from God. The Bada'iyya (Permission of Alteration) claimed that God can change His mind, implying He was ignorant of future outcomes – a clear anthropomorphic doctrine. The Nasiriyya and Is-haqiyya taught that God incarnated in Ali. The author shows they rationalize this by comparing it to angelic or satanic appearances in human form. They claimed that the divine manifested in Ali and his descendants, speaking through them, which is why they call Imams gods. They even appeal to the Prophet's outward judgment vs. God's hidden knowledge as support. Each doctrine is countered by core Sunni principles of divine transcendence and immutability.

Key Terms
النصيرية
الإسحاقية
الحلول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God can incarnate in a human being.
Correction: Sunni Islam holds that God is transcendent and does not dwell in creation. Incarnation (hulul) is explicitly rejected.

Checkpoint
What justification did the Nasiriyya offer for their belief in God's dwelling in Ali?
A) They cited Quranic verses
B) They used the analogy of spiritual beings appearing in physical form
C) They claimed prophetic traditions
D) They argued from logic of creation

Key Takeaway
The Nasiriyya and Is-haqiyya sects commit shirk by claiming divine incarnation in the Imams.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at a religious leader or someone you deeply respect, do you ever catch yourself treating them as if they were perfect or infallible? How does the error of the Nasiriyya and Is-haqiyya warn you against crossing that line?
?
The sects used the example of Jibril appearing in human form to justify their belief. Think of a time you used a religious analogy to support an idea that deep down you knew was shaky. Are you willing to examine your own beliefs with the same honesty this passage demands?
?
If you were asked to defend the tawheed of Allah against someone who claims a human can be divine, what specific phrase from this lesson would you use? Would you be able to say it with conviction in a real conversation?

Names and Hierarchy of the Isma'ili Sect
Author enumerates seven names of the Isma'ili sect and describes their sevenfold hierarchy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seven names given to the Isma'ili sect and the sevenfold hierarchy of their leadership.

Core Idea
The Isma'ilis are defined by a complex system of seven names and a sevenfold rank of authority.

This passage from al-Iji's Mawaqif provides a detailed account of the Isma'ili sect, listing seven titles that reflect their beliefs and history. The author begins with al-Batiniyya, highlighting their esoteric interpretation of the Qur'an, and proceeds through al-Qaramita, al-Hazmiyya, al-Sab'iyya, al-Babakiyya, al-Muhammira, and al-Isma'iliyya. Embedded within the explanation of al-Sab'iyya is a description of their sevenfold hierarchy, from Imam to Mu'min, and the cosmic significance of the number seven.

Guided Path
1
Read the full Arabic passage
Begin by reading the Arabic text once, then read the translation. Notice the structure: first the names, then the hierarchy.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
List the seven names
Identify each name and the reason for it. Write them down in order: al-Batiniyya, al-Qaramita, al-Hazmiyya, al-Sab'iyya, al-Babakiyya, al-Muhammira, al-Isma'iliyya.
Note that al-Sab'iyya covers both the belief in seven messengers and the hierarchy.
3
Explore the hierarchy
Within the Sab'iyya name, find the seven ranks from Imam to Mu'min. Understand the specific role of each rank, especially the Mukallib.
Compare the ranks to the analogy of a hunting dog.
4
Connect the cosmic sevens
Notice how the author relates the hierarchy to the seven heavens, days, planets, etc. This shows the sect's symbolic numerology.
5
Reflect on the sect's identity
Consider how these names and hierarchy distinguish the Isma'ilis from other Muslim groups and why they were controversial.
Think about the charge of esotericism (batin).

أكبر هو رابعهم ( يرفع درجات المؤمنين (و) داع ( مأذون يأخذ العهود على (الطالبين من أهل الظاهر فيدخلهم في ذمة الإمام ويفتح لهم باب العلم والمعرفة وهو خامسهم (ومكلب) قد ارتفعت درجته في الدين ولكن لم يؤذن له في الدعوة بل في الاحتجاج على الناس فهو ( يحتج ويرغب إلى الداعي ككلب الصائد ( حتى إذا احتج على أحد من أهل الظاهر وكسر عليه مذهبه بحيث راب عنه وطلب الحق أداه المكلب إلى الداعي المأذون ليأخذ عليه العهود، قال الآمدي : وإنما سموا مثل هذا مكلباً لأن مثله مثل الجارح يحبس الصيد على كلب الصائد على ما قاله تعالى وما علمتم من الجوراح مكلبين ﴾ [المائدة : ٤ ] ، وهو سادسهم، ( ومؤمن يتبعه ) أي يتبع الداعي وهو الذي أخذ عليه العهد وآمن وأيقن بالعهد ودخل في ذمة الإمام وحزبه وهو سابعهم. قالوا ذلك ) الذي ذكرناه ) كالسماوات والأرض والبحار ( وأيام الأسبوع و ( الكواكب ( السيارة وهي المدبرات أمراً كل منها سبعة كما هو المشهور (و) لقبوا ( بالبابكية إذ اتبع طائفة الخرمي ) في الخروج (بآذربيجان وبالمحمرة للبسهم الحمرة في أيام بابك، أو تسميتهم) المخالفين لهم من المسلمين حميراً، وبالإسماعيلية لإثباتهم الإمامة لإسماعيل بن جعفر الصادق وهو أكبر أبنائه ، وقيل لانتساب زعيمهم إلى محمد ابن إسماعيل.
The Ismailiyya: They were given seven titles. (They are called) al-Batiniyya because of their saying that the inner meaning of the Book is intended instead of its apparent meaning. For they said: The Qur'an has an apparent (zahir) and an inner (batin) meaning; the intended meaning is its inner meaning, while its apparent meaning is what is known from language. The relation of the inner to the apparent is like that of the kernel to the shell. One who clings to its apparent is punished with hardship in acquisition, while its inner leads to abandoning practice of the apparent. They relied on that from His saying: 'Then a wall will be placed between them, with a door, inside which is mercy, and outside of which is punishment.' [Hadid:13]. They took this saying from the Mansuriyya and the Janahiyya. (And) they were called al-Qaramita because the first of them who called people to their sect was a man called Hamdan Qarmat, which is one of the villages of Wasit. And (they are called) al-Hazmiyya due to their permitting forbidden things and sacred things. And (they are called) al-Sab'iyya because they claimed that the speakers (nutaqa') of the laws, i.e., the messengers, are seven: Adam, Noah, Abraham, Moses, Jesus, Muhammad, and Muhammad al-Mahdi is the seventh. And between every two of the speakers there are seven imams who complete his law, and in every seven there must be those who are followed and by whom guidance is sought in religion. They differ in rank: An Imam who conveys from God – and he is the ultimate guide to God's religion. A Hujja who conveys from him – i.e., from the Imam, and he carries and argues for him. A Dhu Mista who sucks knowledge from the Hujja – i.e., he takes it from him. These are three? (unclear) and he argues. (Then) Abwab, and they are the da'is; the Akbar is the greater da'i, and he is the fourth? (he) raises the ranks of the believers. A Ma'dhun da'i who takes covenants from the seekers from the people of the apparent, so he enters them into the guarantee of the Imam and opens for them the door of knowledge and cognition, and he is the fifth. A Mukallib: his rank has risen in religion but he has not been given permission for da'wa but only for arguing against people. So he argues and incites towards the da'i like a hunting dog. Then when he argues against one of the people of the apparent and demolishes his doctrine so that he is shaken and seeks the truth, the Mukallib delivers him to the Ma'dhun da'i to take his covenant. Al-Amidi said: They called such a person Mukallib because his example is like a bird of prey that confines the game for the hunter's dog, according to His saying: 'Whatever you have taught of hunting animals (mukallibin).' [Ma'ida:4]. And he is the sixth. A Mu'min who follows him – i.e., follows the da'i, and he is the one on whom the covenant was taken, who believed and was certain of the covenant, and entered into the guarantee of the Imam and his party, and he is the seventh. They said that (which we mentioned) is like the heavens, the earth, the seas, the days of the week, and the planets (the moving stars) which manage affairs – each of them is seven, as is well known. (And) they were called al-Babakiyya because a group of al-Khurrami followed in the revolt in Azerbaijan. And (they are called) al-Muhammira for their wearing of red in the days of Babak, or their calling their Muslim opponents 'donkeys'. And (they are called) al-Isma'iliyya for their affirming the imamate of Isma'il ibn Ja'far al-Sadiq, who was his eldest son, and it is said due to the lineage of their leader to Muhammad ibn Isma'il.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of the Isma'ili sect, listing seven names and explaining their hierarchy. The author begins with the name al-Batiniyya, emphasizing their hermeneutical principle that the inner meaning (batin) of the Qur'an is the intended one, while the apparent meaning (zahir) is like a shell. They support this with a verse from Sura al-Hadid. The author traces this idea to earlier sects like al-Mansuriyya and al-Jahiziyya. The next name is al-Qaramita, derived from their founder Hamdan Qarmat. al-Hazmiyya refers to their licentiousness. The most detailed name is al-Sab'iyya, based on their belief in seven speakers (messengers) and seven imams between each pair. This leads to a description of a sevenfold hierarchy: the Imam, the Hujja (proof), the Dhu Mista (one who 'sucks' knowledge), the Abwab (doors/da'is), the Akbar (greater da'i), the Ma'dhun (authorized da'i), the Mukallib (the retriever/inviter), and the Mu'min (believer). The Mukallib is likened to a hunting dog that brings the prey to the master. The author then connects this to cosmic sevenfold structures like heavens, days, planets. Finally, other names are given: al-Babakiyya (followers of Babak), al-Muhammira (wearers of red), and al-Isma'iliyya (derived from Isma'il or his descendant). The passage shows the syncretic and hierarchical nature of the sect.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Isma'ilis are a unified sect with a single name.
Correction: They are known by multiple names (Batiniyya, Qaramita, etc.) reflecting different aspects, and they have a complex internal hierarchy.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Isma'ili sect is characterized by seven distinct names and a sevenfold leadership hierarchy, reflecting their esoteric and hierarchical worldview.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How does the Isma'ili belief that the inner meaning of the Qur'an leads to abandoning the apparent practice challenge your own approach to reading the Qur'an? Do you sometimes seek hidden meanings to avoid clear commands? This week, will you commit to acting on one clear command before seeking deeper interpretations?
?
The Isma'ili hierarchy shows a system where people are ranked in access to knowledge. In your own spiritual journey, do you ever feel that someone else has 'higher' knowledge and you are merely a follower? How does that affect your relationship with God? Are you content to be a 'mu'min' in the lowest rank, or do you strive to be a proof? What step will you take to seek understanding of the Qur'an directly, rather than relying on others?
?
Reflect on the Isma'ili name 'Mukallib' – likened to a hunting dog that brings prey to the master. Have you ever been used by others to argue or persuade, only to hand over the seeker to someone else? Does that make you feel like a tool? How can you ensure that your call to Islam is for God alone, not for a human hierarchy?

The Four Stages of Isma'ili Entrapment
Author describes the origin and four-stage method of Isma'ili entrapment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four-stage method used by the Isma'ili da'wa to subvert Islam from within, as explained by the author.

Core Idea
The Isma'ili method subverts Islam through gradual entrapment, not open confrontation.

This passage uncovers the systematic method of the Isma'ili da'wa, tracing its origins to the Magians who devised a cunning strategy to undermine Islamic law. The author describes four distinct stages that progressively ensnare the convert, from testing receptivity to binding with a covenant. Understanding this method sheds light on the historical threat of esoteric sects and their subversive tactics.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for overview
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get a sense of the historical context and the four-stage method.
Notice that the passage is a continuous narrative, not a theological argument.
2
Identify the four stages
Locate the four named stages: al-Dhawq, al-Ta'nis, al-Tashkik, and al-Rabt. Understand the purpose of each.
Each stage is separated by 'then' (ثم).
3
Analyze the political motive
Consider why the Magians devised this method: they could not fight Muslims openly, so they chose subversion through reinterpretation of law.
This is key to understanding the strategy as political rather than theological.
4
Reflect on the progression
Notice how each stage prepares the candidate for the next: from testing to attraction, then doubt, and finally binding.
The goal is to make the convert dependent on the da'i and secretive.

وآصل دعوتهم على إبطال الشرائع، لأن الغيارية وهم طائفة المجوس راموا عند شوكة الإسلام تأويل الشرائع على وجوه تعود إلى قواعد أسلافهم)، وذلك أنهم اجتمعوا فتذكروا ما كان عليه أسلافهم من الملك وقالوا لا سبيل لنا إلى دفع : المسلمين بالسيف لغلبتهم واستيلائهم على الممالك، لكنا نحتال بتأويل شرائعهم إلى ما يعود إلى قواعدنا ونستدرج به الضعفاء منهم، فإن ذلك يوجب اختلافهم واضطراب كلمتهم ( ورأسهم ) في ذلك حمدان قرمط وقيل عبد الله بن ميمون القداح، ولهم في الدعوة ) واستدراج الطعام ) مراتب : الذوق وهو تفرس حال المدعو هل هو قابل للدعوى أم لا، ولذلك منعوا إلقاء البذر في السبخة ) أي دعوة من ليس قابلا لها (و) منعوا ( التكلم في بيت فيه (سراج، أي في موضع فيه فقيه أو متكلم ( ثم التأنيس باستمالة كل أحد ) من المدعوين ) بما يميل إليه ) بهواه وطبعه ( من زهد وخلاعة ) فإن كان يميل إلى الزهد زينه في عينه وقبح نقيضه، وإن كان يميل إلى الخلاعة زينها وقبح نقيضها حتى يحصل له الأنس به ) ثم التشكيك في أركان الشريعة بمقطعات السور) بأن يقول : ما معنى الحروف المقطعة في أوائل السور ( وقضاء صوم الحائض دون قضاء صلاتها ) ؟ أي لم يجب أحدهما دون الآخر؟ (و) وجوب (الغسل من المني دون البول وعدد الركعات ) ؟ أي لم كان بعضها أربعاً وبعضها ثلاثاً وبعضها اثنين؟ إلى غير ذلك من الأمور التعبدية، وإنما يشككون في هذه الأشياء ويطوون الجواب عنها ( ليتعلق قلبهم بمراجعتهم فيها، ثم (الربط وهو أمران : الأول : (أخذ الميثاق منه بأن يقولوا قد جرت سنة الله بأخذ المواثيق والعهود ويستدلوا على ذلك بقوله تعالى : وإذا أخذنا من النبيين ميثاقهم ﴾ [الأحزاب : ٧]، ثم يأخذوا من كل أحد ميثاقه ) بحسب اعتقاده أن لا يفشي لهم سراً . و الثاني : ( حوالته على الإمام
And the origin of their call is the abrogation of the laws, because the Ghayariyya – and they are a group of the Magians – aimed, at the time of the strength of Islam, to interpret the laws in ways that return to the rules of their forefathers. That is because they gathered and recalled what their forefathers had of kingship and said: 'We have no way to repel the Muslims with the sword due to their dominance and seizure of the kingdoms, but we will cunningly interpret their laws to return to our rules and thereby entrap the weak among them, for that will cause their division and confusion of their unity.' Their leader in that was Hamdan Qarmat, and it is said 'Abdullah ibn Maymun al-Qaddah. They have in the call and the entrapment (istidraj) of food stages: al-Dhawq (tasting) – which is examining the condition of the invitee, whether he is receptive to the claim or not. For that reason they prohibited casting seed in salty ground – i.e., calling one who is not receptive. (And) they prohibited speaking in a house where there is a lamp – i.e., a place where there is a jurist or a theologian. Then al-Ta'nis (familiarization) by attracting each one of the invitees by what he inclines to, according to his desire and nature, whether asceticism or licentiousness. For if he inclines to asceticism, they beautify it in his eyes and make its opposite ugly, and if he inclines to licentiousness, they beautify it and make its opposite ugly until they gain his familiarity. Then al-Tashkik (skepticism) concerning the pillars of the Shari'a through the disconnected letters of the surahs, by saying: 'What is the meaning of the disconnected letters at the beginnings of the surahs?' and 'Why do women who menstruate have to make up fasts but not prayers?' – i.e., why must one be made up and not the other? – and 'Why is ritual washing (ghusl) required from semen but not from urine?' and 'Why are prayer cycles (rak'ats) sometimes four, sometimes three, sometimes two?' – to other such devotional matters. They only raise these doubts and withhold the answers in order that the heart of the invitee becomes attached to consulting them about them. Then al-Rabt (bonding) which consists of two things: First: taking a covenant from him by saying, 'The sunna of God has preceded in taking covenants and oaths,' and they cite His saying: 'And when We took from the prophets their covenant' [Ahzab:7]. Then they take from each one a covenant according to his belief that he will not divulge their secret. And second: referring him to the Imam...
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage is an analysis of the Isma'ili method of proselytism and subversion. The author traces the origin of their call to the Ghayariyya Magians who, facing Muslim dominance, devised a strategy to reinterpret Islamic law to undermine it from within. The leader Hamdan Qarmat or Abdullah ibn Maymun al-Qaddah initiated this. The method consists of four stages: 1) al-Dhawq (tasting) – testing the candidate's receptivity; they forbid preaching to those who are not ready. 2) al-Ta'nis (familiarization) – winning over the candidate by appealing to his personal inclinations, whether ascetic or libertine. 3) al-Tashkik (skepticism) – casting doubt on apparent Islamic practices by raising unanswerable questions about ritual details like disconnected letters, menstruation, ritual washing, and prayer cycles, to make the candidate dependent on the da'i for answers. 4) al-Rabt (bonding) – binding the convert with a covenant of secrecy, citing Quranic precedent, and then referring him to the Imam for further initiation. The passage shows the systematic nature of their da'wa. The text ends mid-sentence at the second part of rabt.

المجوس
الاستدراج
الذوق
التأنيس
التشكيك
الربط
الميثاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the Isma'ili method is a legitimate theological interpretation.
Correction: This passage reveals it as a political subversion strategy disguised as esoteric interpretation, aimed at undermining Islam.

D) To attract the candidate with asceticism

The Isma'ili method of entrapment involved four stages: tasting (testing), familiarization, skepticism, and bonding, aimed at undermining Islamic law from within.

?

?
The final stage required a covenant of secrecy. Are there any secrets or compromises in your life that you have hidden from others, fearing exposure? How does this lesson call you to bring them into the light of truth?

The Four Stages of Batiniyya Deception
Enumeration of the four stages of Batiniyya deception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four sequential stages of Batiniyya deception: problem-solving, tadlis, ta'sis, and khal'.

Core Idea
Batiniyya used a staged method of deception, not just persuasion.

The Batiniyya sect employed a systematic method to recruit and lead followers away from orthodox Islam. This passage, from a critical refutation, outlines four distinct stages that begin with problem-solving and end with stripping away religious beliefs. Understanding this method is key to recognizing the sect's deceptive tactics.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage describing the four stages
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the sequence marked by 'ثم' (then).
The stages are presented chronologically in the da'wa process.
2
Identify each stage and its purpose
List the four stages: solving problems / reaching the Imam, tadlis (deception by claiming authority), ta'sis (establishing premises), and khal' (stripping beliefs).
Tadlis and ta'sis are preparatory; khal' is the final stripping.
3
Understand khal' as the climax
Note that khal' involves first dropping bodily actions (physical worship) then stripping religious beliefs entirely.
This stage makes the follower receptive to antinomian teachings.
4
Reflect on the deceptive strategy
Consider how each stage builds on the previous one. The method is designed to gradually erode resistance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاتمة للمرصد الرابع أهله عليه من في حل ما أشكل عليه من الأمور التي ألقاها إليه فإنه العالم بها ولا يقدر عليها أحد حتى يترقى من درجته وينتهي إلى الإمام ) ثم التدليس وهو دعوى موافقة أكابر الدين والدنيا لهم حتى يزداد (ميله إلى ما دعاه إليه ) ثم التأسيس وهو تمهيد مقدمات يقبلها ) ويسلمها ( المدعو ) وتكون سائقة له إلى ما يدعوه إليه من الباطل ) ثم الخلع وهو الطمأنينة إلى إسقاط الأعمال البدنية ثم السلخ عن الاعتقادات الدينية ) ( وحينئذ ) أي وحين إذا آل حال المدعو إلى ذلك ) يأخذون في الإباحة والحث على ( استعجال اللذات وتأويل الشرائع ) كقولهم : الوضوء عبارة عن مولاة الإمام الأخذ والتيمم هو من المأذون عند غيبة الإمام الذي هو الحجة، والصلاة عبارة عن الناطق الذي هو الرسول بدليل قوله تعالى : إن الصلاة تنهى عن الفحشاء والمنكر [العنكبوت : ٤٥] ، والاحتلام عبارة عن إفشاء سر من أسرارهم إلى من ليس من بغير قصد منه والغسل تجديد العهد والزكاة تزكية النفس بمعرفة ما هم الدين، والكعبة النبي والباب ،علي والصفا هو النبي والمروة علي، والميقات الإيناس والتلبية إجابة الدعوة، والطواف بالبيت سبعاً موالاة الأئمة السبعة، والجثة راحة الأبدان عن التكاليف والنار مشقتها بمزاولة التكاليف إلى غير ذلك من خرافاتهم
Conclusion of the Fourth Observatory: His people [the Batiniyya] follow [this method] in solving what is problematic for him from matters that they cast to him, for he [the da'i] is the one who knows them, and no one else is able [to solve them] until he [the follower] ascends from his rank and reaches the Imam. Then [the second stage is] tadlis: which is claiming agreement of the great ones of religion and the world with them so that his inclination towards what they call him to increases. Then [the third stage is] ta'sis: which is preparing premises that the one called accepts and submits to, and they lead him to the falsehood to which they call him. Then [the fourth stage is] khal': which is tranquility in dropping bodily actions and then stripping away religious beliefs. And then—i.e. when the state of the one called reaches that—they begin to permit and urge hastening pleasures and allegorical interpretation of the laws, as their sayings: 'Wudu' is an expression of loyalty to the Imam; tayammum is [taking from] the authorized one in the absence of the Imam who is the proof; prayer is an expression of the speaking prophet (al-natiq), as evidence of His saying 'Indeed prayer forbids immorality and wrongdoing' [al-'Ankabut 45]; nocturnal emission is an expression of revealing a secret of their secrets to someone not of them without his intent; ghusl is renewing the covenant; zakat is purification of the soul by knowing what their religion is; the Ka'ba is the Prophet and the door is 'Ali; al-Safa is the Prophet and al-Marwa is 'Ali; the miqat is familiarizing and talbiya is answering the call; circling the House seven times is following the seven Imams; the Garden is resting bodies from duties and the Fire is their hardship in undertaking duties'; and other such nonsense of theirs.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the Batiniyya's step-by-step method of leading a follower into their sect, followed by examples of their allegorical interpretations (ta'wil) of Islamic rituals. The author enumerates four stages after the initial contact: first, the da'i solves problems for the follower, raising him to the Imam; second, tadlis (deception) where the da'i claims the support of religious and worldly authorities; third, ta'sis (foundation) where premises are fed to the follower; fourth, khal' (stripping) where the follower is made comfortable with abandoning physical acts of worship and then stripped of religious beliefs entirely. Once this state is reached, the Batiniyya permit and encourage immediate gratification of desires and reinterpret the sharia allegorically. The author then lists several examples of their ta'wil, such as interpreting wudu as loyalty to the Imam, prayer as the speaking prophet, the Ka'ba as Muhammad and the door as Ali, etc. The author condemns these as nonsense (khurafat). The passage is a critique of Batiniyya methodology and hermeneutics.

Key Terms
تدليس
تأسيس
خلع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Batiniyya method is simply intellectual persuasion or debate.
Correction: The method involves staged deception (tadlis), gradual foundation of premises (ta'sis), and finally stripping of beliefs (khal'), which is far more manipulative.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the fourth stage (al-khal‘) in the Batiniyya method?
A) Claiming agreement of great religious and worldly figures.
B) Preparing premises that the follower accepts.
C) The follower becomes comfortable with abandoning bodily actions and then being stripped of religious beliefs.
D) Allegorically interpreting the sharia.

Key Takeaway
The Batiniyya method progresses from solving problems to deception, foundation, and finally stripping away religious beliefs.

Batiniyya Allegorical Exegesis of Islamic Rituals
Examples of Batiniyya allegorical interpretations of Islamic rituals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Batiniyya allegorically reinterpreted Islamic rituals to justify antinomianism, and see examples of their ta'wil.

Core Idea
Batiniyya ta'wil turns ritual obligations into symbols for their own hierarchy.

After the follower has been stripped of orthodox beliefs through the four-stage method, the Batiniyya openly permit indulgence in pleasures and reinterpret Islamic laws allegorically. This passage provides several striking examples of their ta'wil, where acts of worship are explained away as references to the Batiniyya imams and concepts. Understanding these interpretations helps in recognizing the sect's radical hermeneutics.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on ta'wil examples
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note how familiar rituals are given alternative meanings.
The passage begins with 'وحينئذ' (and then) connecting to the previous method.
2
Identify the pattern in the interpretations
Notice that rituals are reinterpreted as references to Batiniyya figures: the Imam, the speaking prophet (natiq), Ali, etc.
The purpose is to replace outward worship with loyalty to the sect.
3
Analyze the examples chosen
Pick out a few examples like wudu, prayer, and circumambulation. What do they actually mean according to the Batiniyya?
This shows their anti-ritualistic stance.
4
Consider the author's condemnation
The author dismisses these as 'other such nonsense' (خرافاتهم). Reflect on why these interpretations are considered heretical.

Batiniyya Cosmological Emanation
Emanation from God to man in Batiniyya cosmology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Batiniyya emanationist cosmology, from God's command to the creation of man as the highest being.

Core Idea
The Batiniyya saw creation as a chain of emanations from God through Intellect and Soul.

This passage presents a blend of Neoplatonic philosophy and Islamic esoteric thought. The Batiniyya adopted the philosophers' emanation model to explain the origin of the universe, starting from God's command, through the Perfect Intellect, and then to the imperfect Soul, which longs for perfection. Understanding this chain is essential to grasp their later parallel with prophethood and imamate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the stages of emanation
Read the passage and list the sequence: God's command, Perfect Intellect, imperfect Soul, celestial bodies, elemental natures, compounds, and finally man.
Notice that each step is caused by the previous one through mediation or longing.
2
Note the role of the soul's longing
The imperfect Soul longs for the Perfect Intellect and this longing causes movement, which produces celestial bodies.
This movement is from imperfection to perfection.
3
Understand man's special status
Man is the highest being because he is ready to receive holy lights and connect to the higher world.
This sets up the parallel with the prophet in the next lesson.
4
Reflect on the philosophical borrowing
The passage begins by noting that the Batiniyya mixed their speech with the philosophers. Consider why they might adopt this model.
This shows their cosmology is not purely original but syncretic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وربما خلطوا كلامهم بكلام الفلاسفة)، فقالوا : إنه تعالى أبدع بالأمر العقل التام وبتوسطه أبدع النفس التي ليست تامة فاشتاقت النفس إلى العقل التام مستفيضة منه فاحتاجت إلى الحركة من النقصان إلى الكمال ولن تتم الحركة إلا بالتها، فحدثت الأجرام الفلكية وتحركت حركة دورية بتدبير النفس فحدثت بتوسطه الطبائع البسيطة العنصرية وبتوسط البسائط حدثت المركبات من المعادن والنباتات وأنواع الحيوانات وأفضلها الإنسان لاستعداده لفيض الأنوار القدسية عليه واتصاله بالعالم العلوي وحيث كان العالم العلوي مشتملاً على عقل كامل كلي ونفس ناقصة كلية تكون مصدراً للكائنات يكون في العالم السفلي عقل كامل يكون وسيلة إلى النجاة، وهو الرسول الناطق ونفس ناقصة تكون نسبتها إلى الناطق في تعريف طرق النجاة نسبة النفس الأولى إلى العقل الأول فيما يرجع إلى إيجاد الكائنات وهي الإمام الذي هو وصي الناطق وكما أن تحرك الأفلاك بتحريك العقل والنفس كذلك تحرك النفس إلى النجاة بتحريك الناطق والوصي وعلى هذا في كل عصر وزمان. قال الآمدي : هذا ما كان عليه قدماؤهم
And perhaps they mixed their speech with the speech of the philosophers, and they said: 'He, exalted, originated by the command the perfect intellect, and through its mediation He originated the soul which is not perfect. The soul longed for the perfect intellect, receiving emanation from it, so it needed movement from imperfection to perfection, and the movement is not completed except by it [the soul?]. Thus, celestial bodies came about and moved in a circular motion by the management of the soul, and through its mediation simple elemental natures came about, and through the mediation of the simples, compounds came about from minerals, plants, and kinds of animals, the best of which is man, for his readiness to receive the emanation of holy lights and his connection with the higher world. And since the higher world includes a perfect universal intellect and an imperfect universal soul that is the source of beings, in the lower world there is a perfect intellect that is a means to salvation, and he is the speaking messenger (al-rasul al-natiq), and an imperfect soul whose relation to the speaker in defining the ways of salvation is like the relation of the first soul to the first intellect with regard to the creation of beings, and that is the Imam who is the executor (wasi) of the speaker. And just as the spheres move by the moving of the intellect and soul, likewise the soul moves to salvation by the moving of the speaker and the executor, and thus in every age and time.' Al-Amidi said: 'This is what their predecessors were upon.'
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage presents the Batiniyya's philosophical cosmology, which they adopted from the philosophers (falasifa). It describes an emanationist scheme: God originates the Perfect Intellect by His command, and through it He originates an imperfect Soul. The Soul, longing for the Intellect, needs to move from imperfection to perfection. From this movement, celestial bodies arise and move circularly by the soul's management. From this, simple elemental natures and then compounds (minerals, plants, animals) are produced, with man as the highest due to his preparation to receive holy lights and connection to the higher world. The higher world contains a perfect universal intellect and an imperfect universal soul that is the source of beings. In the lower world, there is a parallel: a perfect intellect which is the speaking messenger (al-rasul al-natiq) and an imperfect soul which is the Imam (the executor, wasi). The relationship between the Imam and the prophet mirrors that of the first soul to the first intellect in creation. Just as the spheres move by the moving of the intellect and soul, the soul moves to salvation by the moving of the prophet and the imam, and this occurs in every age. Al-Amidi notes that this was the doctrine of their predecessors.

النفس
الأجرام الفلكية
الطبائع البسيطة
المركبات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Batiniyya cosmology is purely Islamic philosophy.
Correction: The passage states they mixed their speech with the philosophers, indicating borrowing from Neoplatonic emanationism.

Key Takeaway
The Batiniyya cosmology describes a descending chain of emanations from God through intellect, soul, celestial spheres, and elemental natures to man, who is the highest being due to his readiness for divine illumination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that you exist as the final link in a chain of emanations from God through intellect and soul, how would that change the way you see your purpose in life? What would your pursuit of 'holy lights' look like today, in a way that is not just academic?
?
The Batiniyya claim that the soul moves from imperfection to perfection out of longing for the intellect. What is it that you long for most deeply? Is it drawing you toward the perfect intellect (i.e., divine truth) or away from it? Be honest: what desire has the most control over your daily choices?
?
This cosmology places man above all other creations because of his 'readiness' (استعداد) to receive divine illumination. You are reading this on a screen, not in a state of prayer or reflection. If you died right now, would you be ready? What concrete step will you take in the next 24 hours to actually prepare for that connection?

Prophet and Imam in Batiniyya Cosmology
Parallel between cosmic hierarchy and prophetic-imamic chain in Batiniyya cosmology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Batiniyya parallel the cosmic hierarchy with the prophetic-imamic chain for salvation.

Core Idea
In Batiniyya thought, the prophet and imam mirror the intellect and soul in the lower world.

Having established the cosmic emanation, the Batiniyya then apply the same structure to the spiritual world. Just as the higher world has a perfect intellect and an imperfect soul that produces all beings, the lower world has a perfect intellect (the speaking prophet) and an imperfect soul (the imam) who guide souls to salvation. This passage explicitly draws the parallel and shows its practical implications for every age.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the parallel
Read the Arabic passage carefully and note the explicit comparison between the higher and lower worlds.
The text uses 'وحيث كان' to introduce the parallel.
2
Identify the lower world counterparts
The prophet is a perfect intellect, the imam is an imperfect soul. Find the terms used: الرسول الناطق and الوصي.
3
Understand the functional analogy
Just as the first soul relates to the first intellect in creation, the imam relates to the prophet in guiding to salvation.
This gives the imam a crucial role.
4
Note the eternal recurrence
The passage ends with 'في كل عصر وزمان', indicating that this pattern is perpetual.
Al-Amidi's comment confirms this as the doctrine of their predecessors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وربما خلطوا كلامهم بكلام الفلاسفة)، فقالوا : إنه تعالى أبدع بالأمر العقل التام وبتوسطه أبدع النفس التي ليست تامة فاشتاقت النفس إلى العقل التام مستفيضة منه فاحتاجت إلى الحركة من النقصان إلى الكمال ولن تتم الحركة إلا بالتها، فحدثت الأجرام الفلكية وتحركت حركة دورية بتدبير النفس فحدثت بتوسطه الطبائع البسيطة العنصرية وبتوسط البسائط حدثت المركبات من المعادن والنباتات وأنواع الحيوانات وأفضلها الإنسان لاستعداده لفيض الأنوار القدسية عليه واتصاله بالعالم العلوي وحيث كان العالم العلوي مشتملاً على عقل كامل كلي ونفس ناقصة كلية تكون مصدراً للكائنات يكون في العالم السفلي عقل كامل يكون وسيلة إلى النجاة، وهو الرسول الناطق ونفس ناقصة تكون نسبتها إلى الناطق في تعريف طرق النجاة نسبة النفس الأولى إلى العقل الأول فيما يرجع إلى إيجاد الكائنات وهي الإمام الذي هو وصي الناطق وكما أن تحرك الأفلاك بتحريك العقل والنفس كذلك تحرك النفس إلى النجاة بتحريك الناطق والوصي وعلى هذا في كل عصر وزمان. قال الآمدي : هذا ما كان عليه قدماؤهم
And perhaps they mixed their speech with the speech of the philosophers, and they said: 'He, exalted, originated by the command the perfect intellect, and through its mediation He originated the soul which is not perfect. The soul longed for the perfect intellect, receiving emanation from it, so it needed movement from imperfection to perfection, and the movement is not completed except by it [the soul?]. Thus, celestial bodies came about and moved in a circular motion by the management of the soul, and through its mediation simple elemental natures came about, and through the mediation of the simples, compounds came about from minerals, plants, and kinds of animals, the best of which is man, for his readiness to receive the emanation of holy lights and his connection with the higher world. And since the higher world includes a perfect universal intellect and an imperfect universal soul that is the source of beings, in the lower world there is a perfect intellect that is a means to salvation, and he is the speaking messenger (al-rasul al-natiq), and an imperfect soul whose relation to the speaker in defining the ways of salvation is like the relation of the first soul to the first intellect with regard to the creation of beings, and that is the Imam who is the executor (wasi) of the speaker. And just as the spheres move by the moving of the intellect and soul, likewise the soul moves to salvation by the moving of the speaker and the executor, and thus in every age and time.' Al-Amidi said: 'This is what their predecessors were upon.'
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage presents the Batiniyya's philosophical cosmology, which they adopted from the philosophers (falasifa). It describes an emanationist scheme: God originates the Perfect Intellect by His command, and through it He originates an imperfect Soul. The Soul, longing for the Intellect, needs to move from imperfection to perfection. From this movement, celestial bodies arise and move circularly by the soul's management. From this, simple elemental natures and then compounds (minerals, plants, animals) are produced, with man as the highest due to his preparation to receive holy lights and connection to the higher world. The higher world contains a perfect universal intellect and an imperfect universal soul that is the source of beings. In the lower world, there is a parallel: a perfect intellect which is the speaking messenger (al-rasul al-natiq) and an imperfect soul which is the Imam (the executor, wasi). The relationship between the Imam and the prophet mirrors that of the first soul to the first intellect in creation. Just as the spheres move by the moving of the intellect and soul, the soul moves to salvation by the moving of the prophet and the imam, and this occurs in every age. Al-Amidi notes that this was the doctrine of their predecessors.

Key Terms
الرسول الناطق
الوصي
العقل الكامل
النفس الناقصة
النجاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Batiniyya believed that prophets and imams are optional for salvation.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that the prophet and imam are necessary as means to salvation, just as the intellect and soul are necessary for creation.

Checkpoint
In the Batiniyya lower world parallel, what is the role of the imam (executor)?
A) He is the perfect intellect and means to salvation.
B) He is the imperfect soul whose relation to the prophet is like the first soul to the first intellect.
C) He is the celestial sphere that moves the stars.
D) He is the source of all beings in the lower world.

Key Takeaway
The Batiniyya taught that the prophet and imam are essential cosmic parallels to the intellect and soul, guiding souls to salvation in every age.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Batiniyya believed that in every age a prophet and imam are necessary to move souls toward salvation. As a Muslim who affirms that Prophet Muhammad is the final prophet, do you feel that your soul is being actively moved by his guidance, or have you allowed your spiritual life to become stagnant? What specific teaching of the Prophet will you implement this week to ensure your soul is moving toward salvation?
?
In this passage, the imam (executor) is described as an 'imperfect soul' that defines the ways of salvation. Who or what defines the 'ways of salvation' in your life? Is it the Qur'an and Sunnah through proper scholarship, or has your own desire or culture replaced that guidance? How can you submit more fully to the prophetic way, even when it demands difficulty?
?
The movement of the soul to salvation is compared to the movement of the spheres by the intellect and soul. If your soul is not moving toward salvation, what is holding it back? Is it pride, laziness, or attachment to this world? Identify one area where you have resisted the prophetic call and commit to a concrete change starting today.

Hasan al-Sabbah: Revival and Antinomian Outcome
Description of Hasan al-Sabbah's revival and its antinomian outcome.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Hasan al-Sabbah revived the Batiniyya call, his methods of control, and the antinomian conclusions drawn from his teachings.

Core Idea
Hasan al-Sabbah's revival led to the outright rejection of religious law.

This passage presents the historical figure Hasan al-Sabbah, who claimed to be the Proof (al-hujja) of the hidden Imam and revived the Batiniyya call. The author details his methods of preventing access to knowledge and the eventual antinomian outcome, showing the extreme trajectory of this sect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the flow from Hasan al-Sabbah's appearance to his methods and the resulting practices.
The author's tone is condemnatory and includes a prayer for refuge.
2
Identify the claim and method
What did Hasan al-Sabbah claim to be? What measures did he take to control knowledge and power?
3
Analyze the antinomian outcome
What did the group openly begin to do? How does the author describe their state? Why does he seek refuge?
The outcome is the logical extreme of Batiniyya thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحين ظهر الحسن بن محمد الصباح جدد الدعوة على أنه الحجة ) الذي يؤدي عن الإمام الذي لا يجوز خلو الزمان عنه ( وحاصل كلامه ما تقدم في الاحتياج إلى المعلم) ثم إنه منع العوام عن الخوض في العلوم والخواص عن النظر في الكتب المتقدمة كيلا يطلع على فضائحهم ثم إنهم تفلسفوا ولم يزالوا مستهزئين بالنواميس الدينية والأمور الشرعية وتحصنوا بالحصون وكثرت شوكتهم وخافت ملوك السوء منهم، فأظهروا إسقاط التكاليف وإباحة المحرمات وصاروا كالحيوانات العجماوات بلا ضابط ديني ولا وازع شرعي. نعوذ بالله من الشيطان وأتباعه .
And when al-Hasan ibn Muhammad al-Sabbah appeared, he renewed the call [claiming] that he is the Proof (al-hujja) who conveys from the Imam whose existence is necessary in every time. And the gist of his speech is what preceded regarding the need for a teacher. Then he prevented the common people from delving into the sciences and the elite from looking at earlier books, lest they become aware of their scandals. Then they philosophized and did not cease ridiculing religious laws and legal matters, and they fortified themselves in fortresses, their power increased, and evil kings feared them. So they openly displayed the dropping of duties and the making lawful of forbidden things, and they became like dumb animals, with no religious restraint and no legal deterrent. We seek refuge in Allah from Satan and his followers.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage describes the historical figure Hasan al-Sabbah, who revived the Batiniyya da'wa by claiming to be the 'Proof' (al-hujja) who acts as intermediary for the hidden Imam. The author notes that his message was essentially the same as the earlier Batiniyya argument for the necessity of a teacher. He then describes the methods: he prevented ordinary people from studying the sciences and the elite from reading earlier books to hide their scandals. The Batiniyya of his time became philosophizers, mocked religious laws, fortified themselves in strongholds, and gained power. Ultimately, they openly called for the abolition of religious duties and the permitting of forbidden acts, becoming like animals without any religious or legal restraint. The author ends with a prayer for refuge from them. This section shows the extreme antinomian outcome of the Batiniyya trajectory.

Key Terms
الحجة
الحسن بن محمد الصباح

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Hasan al-Sabbah's movement was purely political, but the passage shows its doctrinal shift to antinomianism and defiance of religious law.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that the Batiniyya openly abandoned duties and permitted forbidden acts, demonstrating a clear antinomian religious outcome, not just politics.

Checkpoint

B) The proof (al-hujja) who conveys from the Imam.

Key Takeaway
The logical endpoint of Batiniyya thought, as exemplified by Hasan al-Sabbah, is the complete abolition of religious law.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How does the fate of Hasan al-Sabbah's followers—who became like dumb animals—warn you against rationalizing away Allah's commands? What is one specific duty you have been neglecting that you will recommit to starting today?
?
This passage shows that intellectual pride led the elite to ridicule religious laws. Reflect on your own heart: are there any Islamic rulings that you secretly find outdated or burdensome? How will you humble yourself before Allah's law this week, perhaps by learning the wisdom behind a ruling you struggle with?
?
The Batiniyya ended up with 'no religious restraint and no legal deterrent.' In what areas of your daily life—speech, consumption, relationships—have you lost a sense of religious boundaries? What practical step can you take today to restore a 'religious deterrent' (الوازع الشرعي) in that area?

The Three Sects of the Zaydiyya: Jarudiyya, Sulaymaniyya, and Butriyya
Classification of Zaydiyya into three sects with their doctrinal positions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three main subsects of the Zaydiyya and their distinct views on imamate, the companions, and the awaited imam.

Core Idea
Zaydis split into three on nass, shura, and the status of early caliphs.

The Zaydiyya, followers of Zayd ibn Ali, are not a single doctrinal school. This passage from al-Mawaqif divides them into three subsects—al-Jarudiyya, al-Sulaymaniyya, and al-Butriyya—each with distinct positions on how the imam is designated and on the moral status of the early Companions. You will read the original classification and learn how these groups disagree on the very foundations of imamate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then the translation. Notice the author's clear enumeration of the three sects.
The passage begins with 'وأما الزيدية' and ends with 'إلا في مسائل قليلة'.
2
Identify the three sects and their namesakes
Find the names of the three sects and the individuals they are attributed to: Abu al-Jarud, Sulayman ibn Jarir, and Butr al-Thawmi.
The names are given at the start of each description.
3
Compare the Jarudiyya's nass versus the Sulaymaniyya's shura
Note the Jarudiyya believe in a textual designation (nass) by description for Ali, while the Sulaymaniyya hold that imamate is decided by consultation (shura) among the community.
This is a key doctrinal split between nass and shura.
4
Note the disagreement on the companions
The Jarudiyya excommunicate all companions who opposed Ali; the Sulaymaniyya excommunicate Uthman, Talha, al-Zubayr, and Aisha but accept Abu Bakr and Umar; the Butriyya suspend judgment on Uthman.
Takfir versus tawaqquf is another distinguishing feature.
5
Consider the author's closing remark
The passage concludes with a note on contemporary Zaydis: most are muqallidun, following Mu'tazili theology and Hanafi fiqh with few exceptions.
This shows that later Zaydis syncretized with other schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الزيدية ) وهم المنسوبون إلى زيد بن علي زين العابدين ( فثلاث فرق : الجارودية : أصحاب أبي الجارود الذي سماه الباقر سرحوباً وفسره بأنه شيطان يسكن البحر ( وقالوا بالنص) من النبي في الإمامة على علي وصفاً لا تسمية والصحابة كفروا بمخالفته وتركهم الاقتداء بعلي بعد النبي ) والإمامة بعد الحسن والحسين شورى في أولادهما فمن خرج منهم بالسيف وهو عالم شجاع فهو إمام ) كما مر واختلفوا في الإمام المنتظر أهو محمد بن عبد الله بن الحسين بن علي الذي قتل بالمدينة في أيام المنصور؟ فذهب طائفة منهم إلى ذلك (و) زعموا ( أنه لم يقتل أو ) هو محمد بن القاسم بن علي ( بن الحسين صاحب طالقان الذي أسر في أيام المعتصم وحمل إليه فحبسه في داره حتى مات فذهب طائفة أخرى إليه وأنكروا موته ( أو هو يحيى بن عمير صاحب الكوفة من أحفاد زيد بن علي دعا الناس إلى نفسه واجتمع عليه خلق كثير وقتل في أيام المستعين بالله فذهب إليه طائفة ثالثة وأنكروا قتله . ( السليمانية : هو سليمان بن جرير قالوا : الإمامة شورى فيما بين الخلق وإنما تنعقد برجلين من خيار المسلمين وتصح إمامة المفضول مع وجود الأفضل ( وأبو بكر وعمر إمامان وإن أخطأ الأمة في البيعة لهما مع وجود علي لكنه خطأ لم ينته إلى درجة الفسق وكفروا عثمان وطلحة والزبير وعائشة البتيرية هو بتير الثومي وافقوا السليمانية إلا أنهم توقفوا في عثمان ( هذه فرق الزيدية وأكثرهم في زماننا مقلدون يرجعون في الأصول إلى الاعتزال وفي الفروع إلى مذهب أبي حنيفة إلا في مسائل قليلة
And as for the Zaydiyya—they are those attributed to Zayd ibn 'Ali Zayn al-'Abidin—they are three sects: 1) al-Jarudiyya: the followers of Abu al-Jarud, whom al-Baqir called Sarhub and explained as a devil dwelling in the sea. They said that there is a text (nass) from the Prophet regarding the imamate upon 'Ali by description, not by name, and that the Companions disbelieved by opposing him and abandoning following 'Ali after the Prophet. And the imamate after al-Hasan and al-Husayn is a consultation (shura) among their children: whoever among them emerges with the sword while being knowledgeable and courageous, he is the imam—as has passed. And they differed concerning the awaited imam: is he Muhammad ibn 'Abdillah ibn al-Husayn ibn 'Ali who was killed in Medina during the days of al-Mansur? So a group of them inclined to that, and they claimed that he was not killed. Or is he Muhammad ibn al-Qasim ibn 'Ali (ibn al-Husayn) the master of Taliqan, who was captured in the days of al-Mu'tasim and brought to him and imprisoned in his house until he died? So another group inclined to him and denied his death. Or is he Yahya ibn 'Umayr the master of Kufa, from the descendants of Zayd ibn 'Ali, who called people to himself and many people gathered around him and he was killed in the days of al-Musta'in bi-llah? So a third group inclined to him and denied his killing. 2) al-Sulaymaniyya: they are [followers of] Sulayman ibn Jarir. They said: the imamate is a consultation among the people, and it is only concluded by two of the best Muslims, and the imamate of the less excellent is valid even when the more excellent exists. They said that Abu Bakr and 'Umar are imams, even if the community made a mistake in giving allegiance to them when 'Ali existed—but it is a mistake that does not reach the level of sinfulness. They pronounced takfir of 'Uthman, Talha, al-Zubayr, and 'A'isha. 3) al-Butriyya: [followers of] Butr al-Thawmi. They agreed with the Sulaymaniyya except that they suspended judgment regarding 'Uthman. These are the sects of the Zaydiyya. Most of them in our time are followers of tradition (muqallidun); they rely in principles (usul) upon Mu'tazilism and in branches (furu') upon the school of Abu Hanifa, except in a few issues.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the Zaydiyya, a Shi'a sect, into three main factions: al-Jarudiyya, al-Sulaymaniyya, and al-Butriyya. The author first identifies the Zaydiyya as followers of Zayd ibn 'Ali, then describes each sub-sect's views on the imamate and the early caliphs. Al-Jarudiyya: They believe there is a textual designation (nass) from the Prophet for 'Ali by description (sifa) but not by name. They consider the Companions who opposed 'Ali as disbelievers. After al-Hasan and al-Husayn, the imamate is decided by shura among their descendants, with the condition that the candidate emerges with the sword and is knowledgeable and courageous. They differ on who the awaited imam is, with three possibilities: Muhammad ibn 'Abdillah, Muhammad ibn al-Qasim, or Yahya ibn 'Umayr. Al-Sulaymaniyya: They hold that the imamate is a matter of consultation among the people and can be established by two righteous Muslims. They accept the imamate of the less excellent (mafdul) over the more excellent (afdal). They consider Abu Bakr and 'Umar as imams, though the community erred in choosing them over 'Ali—but the error does not reach sin. They excommunicate 'Uthman, Talha, al-Zubayr, and 'A'isha. Al-Butriyya: they agree with the Sulaymaniyya but suspend judgment on 'Uthman. The author concludes by noting that most contemporary Zaydiyya are taqlid followers, adopting Mu'tazili theology and Hanafi jurisprudence, with few exceptions.

Key Terms
الزيدية
الجارودية
السليمانية
البتيرية
النص
الإمامة
الشورى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Zaydis share identical views on imamate and the companions.
Correction: The Zaydiyya are divided into three main subsects (Jarudiyya, Sulaymaniyya, Butriyya) with significant differences on nass, shura, and the status of early caliphs.

Checkpoint

A) It is invalid when a more excellent person exists.
B) It is valid.
C) It is valid only if the less excellent has a sword.
D) They suspend judgment.

Key Takeaway
The Zaydiyya are not a unified sect: their three main subsects differ fundamentally over how the imam is chosen and how to evaluate the early Companions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage ends by noting that most Zaydis are muqallidun, blindly following others in principles and branches. Are you, in your own religious practice, simply imitating a scholar or madhhab without understanding the evidence? What specific step will you take this week to move from taqlid to tahqiq?
?
The Zaydi sects differed over who the awaited imam is, each insisting their candidate is not dead. Examine your own heart: do you hold any belief not because it is true, but because it gives you comfort or a sense of identity? Are you willing to submit to the truth even if it shatters your expectations?

Sects and Disagreements
