Imamiyya Doctrine: Clear Text on 'Ali and Condemnation of Companions
Imamiyya claim of clear text on Ali and its consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Imamiyya belief in a clear textual designation (al-nass al-jali) for 'Ali's imamate and how this led them to declare the Companions disbelievers and revile them.

Core Idea
The Imamiyya built their entire imamate doctrine on a single claim: that the Prophet explicitly designated 'Ali.

This passage from al-Mawaqif presents the Imamiyya sect's foundational belief about the imamate. It is a claim with massive consequences: they assert that the Prophet made a clear, unambiguous statement appointing 'Ali as his successor. On this basis, they rejected the legitimacy of the first three caliphs and went so far as to declare many Companions disbelievers. Let's examine this claim and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of al-nass al-jali
Read the Arabic phrase 'النص الجلي' and understand that it means an explicit, clear textual designation from the Prophet, leaving no room for interpretation.
This is contrasted with 'al-nass al-khafi' (implicit text).
2
Note the consequences: takfir of Companions
The passage says they declared the Companions disbelievers ('كفروا الصحابة') and reviled them. Think about why this follows from their belief in clear nass.
3
Trace the line to Ja'far al-Sadiq
They traced the imamate from 'Ali down to Ja'far al-Sadiq. This sets the stage for the second part of the passage about later imams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الإمامية فقالوا : بالنص الجلي على إمامة علي وكفروا الصحابة ووقعوا فيهم وساقوا الإمامة إلى جعفر الصادق واختلفوا في المنصوص عليه بعده والذي استقر عليه رأيهم أنه ابنه موسى الكاظم وبعده علي بن موسى الرضاء وبعده محمد بن علي التقي وبعده علي بن محمد التقي وبعده الحسن به علي الزكي وبعده محمد بن الحسن وهو الإمام المنتظر، ولهم في كل من المراتب التي بعد جعفر اختلافات أوردها الإمام في آخر المحصل، وكانت الإمامية أولاً على مذهب أئمتهم حتى
And as for the Imamiyya, they said: there is a clear text (al-nass al-jali) upon the imamate of 'Ali, and they declared the Companions disbelievers and reviled them. They traced the imamate to Ja'far al-Sadiq, and they differed regarding who was designated after him. What their view settled upon is that it is his son Musa al-Kazim, and after him 'Ali ibn Musa al-Rida, and after him Muhammad ibn 'Ali al-Taqi, and after him 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Taqi, and after him al-Hasan ibn 'Ali al-Zaki, and after him Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, who is the awaited Imam (al-imam al-muntazar). They have differences in each of the ranks after Ja'far, which the Imam [al-Razi] mentioned at the end of al-Muhassal. And the Imamiyya were at first upon the school of their imams until...
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage presents the Imamiyya (Twelver Shi'a) doctrine on the imamate. They assert that there is a clear and explicit textual designation (al-nass al-jali) from the Prophet for 'Ali's imamate, and on that basis they declare the early caliphs and other Companions who opposed 'Ali to be disbelievers and they revile them. They trace the line of imams from 'Ali through his sons Hasan and Husayn up to Ja'far al-Sadiq. After Ja'far, there were disagreements among the Imamiyya on who the next imam was, but eventually the settled view became that it was his son Musa al-Kazim, followed by a specific list of seven imams: 'Ali al-Rida, Muhammad al-Taqi, 'Ali al-Taqi, Hasan al-Zaki, and finally Muhammad al-Hasan, who is the awaited Imam (al-Mahdi). The author notes that there were differences concerning each succession after Ja'far, which were recorded by Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi in his work al-Muhassal. The passage cuts off at the word 'until' (hatta), indicating continuation on the next page, possibly describing their later development.

Key Terms
النص الجلي
الإمامة
تكفير الصحابة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Imamiyya believe in a general designation of 'Ali without condemning the Companions.
Correction: The passage clearly states they declared the Companions disbelievers and reviled them as a direct consequence of the clear nass.

Checkpoint
What did the Imamiyya claim regarding the Prophet's designation of 'Ali?
A) It was an implicit suggestion
B) It was a clear explicit text (al-nass al-jali)
C) It was a general wish without binding force
D) It was only known to a few

Key Takeaway
The Imamiyya's entire position on the imamate begins with the claim of a clear, explicit designation of 'Ali, leading them to condemn those who opposed him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Imamiyya took one claim – clear text on 'Ali – and built a theology that condemned the majority of the Prophet's closest Companions. Have you ever built an entire worldview on a single interpretation of a text, only to later realize that your certainty was misplaced? What would it take for you to admit that today?
?
This lesson shows a group that felt compelled to declare others disbelievers over a historical political dispute. Is there anyone in the early Muslim community (or today) whom you have quietly written off as outside the fold of Islam? If so, what is the evidence from the Qur'an and Sunnah that you are following, and are you willing to test it against the consensus of the scholars?
?
The imamate was traced through specific individuals until Ja'far al-Sadiq. Imagine you had to trace your own spiritual lineage back to the Prophet – who would you include? Would your chain be based on bloodline or on adherence to the sunnah? And if you discovered that your chain omitted someone you disliked, would you be willing to add them back?

The Imamiyya Line of Imams After Ja'far al-Sadiq
List of Imamiyya imams after Ja'far al-Sadiq with note on differences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Imamiyya line of twelve imams from Musa al-Kazim to Muhammad al-Hasan (the awaited imam) and the differences among them regarding each succession.

Core Idea
After Ja'far, the Imamiyya settled on a specific line of seven imams ending with the awaited Mahdi.

In the previous lesson, we saw the Imamiyya's claim of a clear text for 'Ali and their line down to Ja'far al-Sadiq. Now we examine the continuation of that line after Ja'far. The author lists the imams they ultimately agreed upon, but notes that there were many disagreements about each succession. This lesson will help you memorize that line and understand the nature of those internal disputes.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of imams
Read the Arabic names from Musa al-Kazim to Muhammad al-Hasan. Note the father-son sequence.
This is the standard Twelver list.
2
Understand 'al-imam al-muntazar'
The last imam, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, is called the awaited Imam (al-imam al-muntazar) – the Mahdi who is in occultation.
3
Note the differences after Ja'far
The passage says they had differences (ikhtilafat) in each rank after Ja'far. This refers to disputes over who the rightful imam was, with some groups following different sons.
These differences are recorded in al-Muhassal by al-Razi.
4
Consider the significance of the twelve
The Imamiyya believe in exactly twelve imams, and this list defines them. This is a core identity marker.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الإمامية فقالوا : بالنص الجلي على إمامة علي وكفروا الصحابة ووقعوا فيهم وساقوا الإمامة إلى جعفر الصادق واختلفوا في المنصوص عليه بعده والذي استقر عليه رأيهم أنه ابنه موسى الكاظم وبعده علي بن موسى الرضاء وبعده محمد بن علي التقي وبعده علي بن محمد التقي وبعده الحسن به علي الزكي وبعده محمد بن الحسن وهو الإمام المنتظر، ولهم في كل من المراتب التي بعد جعفر اختلافات أوردها الإمام في آخر المحصل، وكانت الإمامية أولاً على مذهب أئمتهم حتى
And as for the Imamiyya, they said: there is a clear text (al-nass al-jali) upon the imamate of 'Ali, and they declared the Companions disbelievers and reviled them. They traced the imamate to Ja'far al-Sadiq, and they differed regarding who was designated after him. What their view settled upon is that it is his son Musa al-Kazim, and after him 'Ali ibn Musa al-Rida, and after him Muhammad ibn 'Ali al-Taqi, and after him 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Taqi, and after him al-Hasan ibn 'Ali al-Zaki, and after him Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, who is the awaited Imam (al-imam al-muntazar). They have differences in each of the ranks after Ja'far, which the Imam [al-Razi] mentioned at the end of al-Muhassal. And the Imamiyya were at first upon the school of their imams until...
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage presents the Imamiyya (Twelver Shi'a) doctrine on the imamate. They assert that there is a clear and explicit textual designation (al-nass al-jali) from the Prophet for 'Ali's imamate, and on that basis they declare the early caliphs and other Companions who opposed 'Ali to be disbelievers and they revile them. They trace the line of imams from 'Ali through his sons Hasan and Husayn up to Ja'far al-Sadiq. After Ja'far, there were disagreements among the Imamiyya on who the next imam was, but eventually the settled view became that it was his son Musa al-Kazim, followed by a specific list of seven imams: 'Ali al-Rida, Muhammad al-Taqi, 'Ali al-Taqi, Hasan al-Zaki, and finally Muhammad al-Hasan, who is the awaited Imam (al-Mahdi). The author notes that there were differences concerning each succession after Ja'far, which were recorded by Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi in his work al-Muhassal. The passage cuts off at the word 'until' (hatta), indicating continuation on the next page, possibly describing their later development.

Key Terms
الإمام المنتظر
موسى الكاظم
جعفر الصادق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all Imamiyya agreed on the line of imams without any disagreement.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that there were differences (ikhtilafat) in each succession after Ja'far, indicating internal disputes.

Checkpoint
Who is the final imam in the Imamiyya line according to this passage?
A) Ja'far al-Sadiq
B) Musa al-Kazim
C) Muhammad ibn al-Hasan
D) 'Ali ibn Abi Talib

Key Takeaway
The Imamiyya settled on a line of seven imams after Ja'far al-Sadiq, ending with the awaited Mahdi, but each succession had internal disagreements.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that even within the Imamiyya, there were disagreements at every stage of succession, does this challenge your trust in any single sect's claims to absolute truth? How willing are you to honestly examine the historical disputes within your own tradition, even if it makes you uncomfortable?
?
The Imamiyya eventually settled on a line of seven imams after Ja'far, but the passage notes differences 'for each rank.' This means believers had to make choices amid uncertainty. When you face ambiguity in your own religious beliefs, do you seek clarity through study or cling to comfortable assumptions? What step will you take this week to investigate a point of disagreement you've avoided?
?
The awaited imam is called 'al-Muntazar' — the one who is waited for. In your daily life, is your hope and action oriented toward an eventual manifestation of truth and justice, or have you become complacent? How does the idea of an imam in occultation challenge you to live with active anticipation rather than passive waiting?

The Zaydiyya and the Jarudiyya Sub-Sect
Defines Zaydiyya and details Jarudiyya beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the foundational beliefs of the Jarudiyya, including their view on nass, the status of the Companions, imamate after Hasan and Husayn, and their disagreements about the awaited imam.

Core Idea
The Jarudiyya believed in an implicit designation of Ali and declared the Companions disbelievers for opposing him.

The Zaydiyya trace their name to Zayd ibn Ali. Among their three sub-sects, the Jarudiyya held the most extreme views on the imamate and the Companions. In this lesson, we explore their distinctive doctrines as presented by the author.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the translation. Notice the detailed description of Jarudiyya beliefs.
The passage includes many points; try to identify each one.
2
Identify the key doctrines of the Jarudiyya
List the beliefs mentioned: nass by description, takfir of Companions, imamate as shura among descendants, condition of rising with the sword, and the three opinions on the awaited imam.
3
Reflect on the significance of their views
Consider how these beliefs set the Jarudiyya apart from other Zaydi groups and from Sunni orthodoxy.
This connects to the broader sectarian landscape.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الزيدية وهم المنسوبون إلى زيد بن علي زين العابدين فثلاث فرق : الجارودية : أصحاب أبي الجارود الذي سماه الباقر سرحوباً وفسره بأنه شيطان يسكن البحر وقالوا بالنص من النبي في الإمامة على علي وصفاً لا تسمية والصحابة كفروا بمخالفته وتركهم الاقتداء بعلي بعد النبي والإمامة بعد الحسن والحسين شورى في أولادهما فمن خرج منهم بالسيف وهو عالم شجاع فهو إمام كما مر واختلفوا في الإمام المنتظر أهو محمد بن عبد الله بن الحسين بن علي الذي قتل بالمدينة في أيام المنصور؟ فذهب طائفة منهم إلى ذلك وزعموا أنه لم يقتل أو هو محمد بن القاسم بن علي بن الحسين صاحب طالقان الذي أسر في أيام المعتصم وحمل إليه فحبسه في داره حتى مات فذهب طائفة أخرى إليه وأنكروا موته أو هو يحيى بن عمير صاحب الكوفة من أحفاد زيد بن علي دعا الناس إلى نفسه واجتمع عليه خلق كثير وقتل في أيام المستعين بالله فذهب إليه طائفة ثالثة وأنكروا قتله . السليمانية : هو سليمان بن جرير قالوا : الإمامة شورى فيما بين الخلق وإنما تنعقد برجلين من خيار المسلمين وتصح إمامة المفضول مع وجود الأفضل وأبو بكر وعمر إمامان وإن أخطأ الأمة في البيعة لهما مع وجود علي لكنه خطأ لم ينته إلى درجة الفسق وكفروا عثمان وطلحة والزبير وعائشة البتيرية هو بتير الثومي وافقوا السليمانية إلا أنهم توقفوا في عثمان هذه فرق الزيدية وأكثرهم في زماننا مقلدون يرجعون في الأصول إلى الاعتزال وفي الفروع إلى مذهب أبي حنيفة إلا في مسائل قليلة
As for the Zaydiyya, they are those attributed to Zayd ibn Ali Zayn al-Abidin. They are three sects: al-Jarudiyya: the followers of Abu al-Jarud, whom al-Baqir called Sarhub and interpreted as a devil dwelling in the sea. They said there is explicit designation (nass) from the Prophet for the imamate of 'Ali by description (wasf) not by name (tasmiya). They declared the Companions disbelievers for opposing him and for abandoning following 'Ali after the Prophet. The imamate after al-Hasan and al-Husayn is by consultation (shura) among their descendants; whoever among them rises with the sword, being knowledgeable and brave, is the imam. They differed regarding the awaited imam: is it Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah ibn al-Husayn ibn 'Ali, who was killed in Medina during the days of al-Mansur? One group went to that and claimed he was not killed. Or is it Muhammad ibn al-Qasim ibn 'Ali ibn al-Husayn, the master of Talqan, who was captured in the days of al-Mu'tasim and carried to him, who imprisoned him in his house until he died? Another group went to that and denied his death. Or is it Yahya ibn 'Umayr, the master of Kufa, a descendant of Zayd ibn 'Ali, who called people to himself and many gathered around him, and he was killed in the days of al-Musta'in bi-Allah? A third group went to that and denied his being killed. al-Sulaymaniyya: they are Sulayman ibn Jarir. They said: imamate is consultation among the people, and it is only concluded by two men from the best of Muslims. The imamate of the inferior (mafdul) is valid in the presence of the superior (afdal). Abu Bakr and 'Umar are imams, even if the community erred in giving allegiance to them in the presence of 'Ali, but it is an error that does not reach the degree of sin. They declared 'Uthman, Talha, al-Zubayr, and 'A'isha disbelievers. al-Butriyya: he is Butayr al-Thawmi. They agreed with al-Sulaymaniyya except that they suspended judgment regarding 'Uthman. These are the sects of the Zaydiyya. Most of them in our time are imitators (muqallidun), referring in principles (usul) to Mu'tazilism, and in branches (furu') to the school of Abu Hanifa, except in a few issues.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage defines the Zaydiyya as followers of Zayd ibn Ali, then details three sub-sects: al-Jarudiyya, al-Sulaymaniyya, and al-Butriyya. It begins by naming the subsects and then explains each. For al-Jarudiyya, it mentions their founder's derogatory name from al-Baqir, their belief in implicit designation (nass wasf) of Ali, their takfir of the Companions, their view on imamate after al-Hasan and al-Husayn as a shura among their descendants with the condition of rising with the sword, and their disagreement on the identity of the awaited imam with three different figures. For al-Sulaymaniyya, they hold that imamate is by consultation, valid even if the inferior is chosen, and they consider Abu Bakr and 'Umar as imams but not sinful for preferring them over Ali; they also declare takfir on 'Uthman, Talha, al-Zubayr, and 'A'isha. For al-Butriyya, they mostly agree with al-Sulaymaniyya but suspend judgment on 'Uthman. Finally, it notes that contemporary Zaydis are mostly muqallids, following Mu'tazili theology and Hanafi fiqh except in minor issues.

Key Terms
الزيدية
الجارودية
النص بالوصف
الشورى
الإمام المنتظر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Jarudiyya, what is the basis for the imamate of Ali?
A) Explicit naming (tasmiya) by the Prophet
B) Description (wasf) by the Prophet
C) Consultation among the Companions
D) Military conquest

Key Takeaway
The Jarudiyya sub-sect held that Ali's imamate was divinely designated by description, and they differed among themselves over the identity of the awaited imam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Jarudiyya declared the Companions disbelievers for not following Ali. When you see someone disagreeing with what you believe to be true, is your first reaction to condemn or to understand? What would it take for you to respond with firmness in truth but mercy towards people?
?
The Jarudiyya differed on the identity of the awaited imam, each group insisting on their candidate and denying obvious deaths. Is there any belief you hold so strongly that you ignore clear evidence against it? What would it cost you to honestly reconsider?
?
The condition for imamate among the Jarudiyya was rising with the sword, knowledge, and bravery. What cause in your life are you willing to rise for with full commitment? Can you honestly say you are ready to bear hardship for the truth with courage and learning?

The Sulaymaniyya Sub-Sect
Explains the beliefs of the Sulaymaniyya sub-sect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sulaymaniyya position on imamate by consultation, the validity of the inferior imam, and their declaration of takfir on several prominent Companions.

Core Idea
The Sulaymaniyya viewed imamate as a consultative process and accepted the imamate of the inferior, but declared takfir on Uthman and others.

The second Zaydi sub-sect, the Sulaymaniyya, took a more moderate stance on the imamate of Abu Bakr and Umar while condemning Uthman and his supporters. This lesson unpacks their unique blend of views.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Focus on the key claims: imamate by shura, validity of the inferior, and the list of those declared disbelievers.
Notice the contrast with the Jarudiyya on the status of Abu Bakr and Umar.
2
Analyze the doctrine of imamate
Understand that for the Sulaymaniyya, imamate is a human agreement, not divine designation, and the best person is not required.
3
Identify the targets of takfir
List the four individuals they declared disbelievers: Uthman, Talha, al-Zubayr, and A'isha.
This is a specific point that distinguishes them from other groups.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Sulaymaniyya declared takfir on Uthman and others while considering Abu Bakr and Umar as imams despite an error. When you disagree with someone's actions, do you tend to condemn them entirely or give them the benefit of the doubt? How does this lesson challenge you to examine your own judgments of others' mistakes?
?
They believed an inferior person can be imam even when a better candidate exists, because the error of choosing him is not sinful. Think of a time you, as a group, chose a leader who was not the best. How did you handle that choice? Do you tend to justify it, or do you criticize it as a sin? What does this say about your heart's posture toward authority?
?
The Sulaymaniyya drew a line: they did not declare takfir on Abu Bakr and Umar but did on Uthman and others. Where do you draw lines in your own relationships? Is there someone you have completely written off? What would it take for you to distinguish between an error and outright disbelief in your own heart?

The Butriyya Sub-Sect and Contemporary Zaydis
Describes the Butriyya and summarizes Zaydi practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Butriyya's position on 'Uthman and the overall character of Zaydi practice in later times.

Core Idea
The Butriyya agreed with the Sulaymaniyya but suspended judgment on 'Uthman, and later Zaydis became Mu'tazili in theology and Hanafi in law.

The third Zaydi sub-sect, the Butriyya, differed from the Sulaymaniyya only in their stance on 'Uthman. The passage concludes with an important note on how most Zaydis in the author's time had adopted Mu'tazili theology and Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the concise description of the Butriyya and the final sentence about Zaydi practice.
This lesson is shorter but contains a key summary.
2
Understand the Butriyya's position
They agreed with the Sulaymaniyya except they suspended judgment (tawaqquf) on Uthman, neither affirming nor denying his faith.
3
Analyze the final statement
The author notes that most contemporary Zaydis are muqallidun, relying on Mu'tazilism for usul and Hanafi fiqh for furu'.
This shows the later development of Zaydi thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الزيدية وهم المنسوبون إلى زيد بن علي زين العابدين فثلاث فرق : الجارودية : أصحاب أبي الجارود الذي سماه الباقر سرحوباً وفسره بأنه شيطان يسكن البحر وقالوا بالنص من النبي في الإمامة على علي وصفاً لا تسمية والصحابة كفروا بمخالفته وتركهم الاقتداء بعلي بعد النبي والإمامة بعد الحسن والحسين شورى في أولادهما فمن خرج منهم بالسيف وهو عالم شجاع فهو إمام كما مر واختلفوا في الإمام المنتظر أهو محمد بن عبد الله بن الحسين بن علي الذي قتل بالمدينة في أيام المنصور؟ فذهب طائفة منهم إلى ذلك وزعموا أنه لم يقتل أو هو محمد بن القاسم بن علي بن الحسين صاحب طالقان الذي أسر في أيام المعتصم وحمل إليه فحبسه في داره حتى مات فذهب طائفة أخرى إليه وأنكروا موته أو هو يحيى بن عمير صاحب الكوفة من أحفاد زيد بن علي دعا الناس إلى نفسه واجتمع عليه خلق كثير وقتل في أيام المستعين بالله فذهب إليه طائفة ثالثة وأنكروا قتله . السليمانية : هو سليمان بن جرير قالوا : الإمامة شورى فيما بين الخلق وإنما تنعقد برجلين من خيار المسلمين وتصح إمامة المفضول مع وجود الأفضل وأبو بكر وعمر إمامان وإن أخطأ الأمة في البيعة لهما مع وجود علي لكنه خطأ لم ينته إلى درجة الفسق وكفروا عثمان وطلحة والزبير وعائشة البتيرية هو بتير الثومي وافقوا السليمانية إلا أنهم توقفوا في عثمان هذه فرق الزيدية وأكثرهم في زماننا مقلدون يرجعون في الأصول إلى الاعتزال وفي الفروع إلى مذهب أبي حنيفة إلا في مسائل قليلة
As for the Zaydiyya, they are those attributed to Zayd ibn Ali Zayn al-Abidin. They are three sects: al-Jarudiyya: the followers of Abu al-Jarud, whom al-Baqir called Sarhub and interpreted as a devil dwelling in the sea. They said there is explicit designation (nass) from the Prophet for the imamate of 'Ali by description (wasf) not by name (tasmiya). They declared the Companions disbelievers for opposing him and for abandoning following 'Ali after the Prophet. The imamate after al-Hasan and al-Husayn is by consultation (shura) among their descendants; whoever among them rises with the sword, being knowledgeable and brave, is the imam. They differed regarding the awaited imam: is it Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah ibn al-Husayn ibn 'Ali, who was killed in Medina during the days of al-Mansur? One group went to that and claimed he was not killed. Or is it Muhammad ibn al-Qasim ibn 'Ali ibn al-Husayn, the master of Talqan, who was captured in the days of al-Mu'tasim and carried to him, who imprisoned him in his house until he died? Another group went to that and denied his death. Or is it Yahya ibn 'Umayr, the master of Kufa, a descendant of Zayd ibn 'Ali, who called people to himself and many gathered around him, and he was killed in the days of al-Musta'in bi-Allah? A third group went to that and denied his being killed. al-Sulaymaniyya: they are Sulayman ibn Jarir. They said: imamate is consultation among the people, and it is only concluded by two men from the best of Muslims. The imamate of the inferior (mafdul) is valid in the presence of the superior (afdal). Abu Bakr and 'Umar are imams, even if the community erred in giving allegiance to them in the presence of 'Ali, but it is an error that does not reach the degree of sin. They declared 'Uthman, Talha, al-Zubayr, and 'A'isha disbelievers. al-Butriyya: he is Butayr al-Thawmi. They agreed with al-Sulaymaniyya except that they suspended judgment regarding 'Uthman. These are the sects of the Zaydiyya. Most of them in our time are imitators (muqallidun), referring in principles (usul) to Mu'tazilism, and in branches (furu') to the school of Abu Hanifa, except in a few issues.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage defines the Zaydiyya as followers of Zayd ibn Ali, then details three sub-sects: al-Jarudiyya, al-Sulaymaniyya, and al-Butriyya. It begins by naming the subsects and then explains each. For al-Jarudiyya, it mentions their founder's derogatory name from al-Baqir, their belief in implicit designation (nass wasf) of Ali, their takfir of the Companions, their view on imamate after al-Hasan and al-Husayn as a shura among their descendants with the condition of rising with the sword, and their disagreement on the identity of the awaited imam with three different figures. For al-Sulaymaniyya, they hold that imamate is by consultation, valid even if the inferior is chosen, and they consider Abu Bakr and 'Umar as imams but not sinful for preferring them over Ali; they also declare takfir on 'Uthman, Talha, al-Zubayr, and 'A'isha. For al-Butriyya, they mostly agree with al-Sulaymaniyya but suspend judgment on 'Uthman. Finally, it notes that contemporary Zaydis are mostly muqallids, following Mu'tazili theology and Hanafi fiqh except in minor issues.

المقلدون

الفروع

A) The validity of the inferior imam
B) The status of 'Uthman
C) The concept of shura
D) The imamate of Abu Bakr

Key Takeaway
The Butriyya suspended judgment on 'Uthman, and later Zaydis became Mu'tazili in theology and Hanafi in law.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Butriyya suspended judgment on 'Uthman. In your own life, are there people or issues about which you have rushed to judge without sufficient knowledge? Are you willing to practice tawaqquf—to withhold judgment until you have clarity—even when others demand you take a side?
?
The passage says most Zaydis today are muqallids—followers of schools without independent investigation. How much of your own faith is inherited tradition versus personal conviction? Can you name the source of your beliefs about God and His attributes, or do you simply follow what you were raised with?
?
If you were to examine your own theological and legal practices, would you find yourself more like the early Zaydis who directly engaged with the sources, or like the contemporary muqallids? What is one step you can take this week to move from blind imitation to greater certainty?

The Imamiyya: Doctrine of Nass and Internal Divisions
Describes the Imamiyya's doctrine of nass and their later splits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Imamiyya's core doctrine of explicit designation (nass jali), their line of imams, and their later fragmentation into Mu'tazili, Akhbari, and other subgroups.

Core Idea
The Imamiyya built on nass but eventually splintered into conflicting theological camps.

This passage from al-Iji outlines the Twelver Shia (Imamiyya) and their distinctive belief in an explicit divine designation (nass jali) for Ali's imamate. It then traces the imamate down to Muhammad al-Mahdi and explains how later Imamiyya split into rationalist Mu'tazila, literalist Akhbariyya, and even groups that joined deviant sects. Understanding this helps clarify the internal diversity of Shia theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core doctrine
Read the first part of the passage to see what the Imamiyya believe regarding the imamate of Ali and their attitude toward the Companions.
Note the term 'nass jali' – explicit designation.
2
Trace the line of imams
Follow the sequence from Ali to Muhammad al-Mahdi, noticing where disagreements occurred after Ja'far al-Sadiq.
The settled line includes Musa al-Kazim, Ali al-Rida, etc.
3
Analyze the later splits
Understand how the Imamiyya divided into Mu'tazila (Wa'idiyya and Tafdiliyya) and Akhbariyya (Mushabbiha and Salafiyya).
Also note that some joined deviant sects.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why these internal divisions matter for the history of Islamic theology.
The passage shows that even within a single sect, diversity is present.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الإمامية فقالوا : بالنص الجلي على إمامة علي وكفروا الصحابة ووقعوا فيهم وساقوا الإمامة إلى جعفر الصادق واختلفوا في المنصوص عليه بعده والذي استقر عليه رأيهم أنه ابنه موسى الكاظم وبعده علي بن موسى الرضاء وبعده محمد بن علي التقي وبعده علي بن محمد التقي وبعده الحسن بن علي الزكي وبعده محمد بن الحسن وهو الإمام المنتظر، ولهم في كل من المراتب التي بعد جعفر اختلافات أوردها الإمام في آخر المحصل، وكانت الإمامية أولاً على مذهب أئمتهم حتى تمادی بهم الزمان فاختلفوا وتشعب متأخروهم إلى معتزلة إما وعيدية أو تفضيلية وإلى إخبارية يعتقدون ظاهر ما ورد به الأخبار المتشابهة وهؤلاء ينقسمون إلى مشبهة يجرون المتشابهات على أن المراد بها ظواهرها وسلفية يعتقدون أن ما أورد الله بها حق بلا تشبيه كما عليه السلف وإلى ملتحقة بالفرق الضالة
As for the Imamiyya, they said: there is explicit designation (al-nass al-jali) for the imamate of 'Ali, and they declared the Companions disbelievers and reviled them. They traced the imamate down to Ja'far al-Sadiq and differed regarding who was designated after him. The view that became settled among them is that it is his son Musa al-Kazim, then after him 'Ali ibn Musa al-Rida, then after him Muhammad ibn 'Ali al-Taqi, then after him 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Taqi, then after him al-Hasan ibn 'Ali al-Zaki, then after him Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, who is the awaited imam. For each of the stages after Ja'far they had disagreements which the Imam (al-Razi?) mentioned at the end of al-Muhassal. The Imamiyya were initially upon the madhhab of their imams, until when time prolonged for them they differed, and their later ones split into Mu'tazila, either Wa'idiyya or Tafdiliyya, and into Akhbariyya who believe in the outward meaning of the mutashabihat traditions. And these divide into Mushabbiha who apply the mutashabihat to mean their outward appearances, and Salafiyya who believe that what God has brought is true without tashbih, as was the way of the Salaf. And [some] joined the deviant sects.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage describes the Imamiyya (Twelver Shia) and their core doctrine of explicit designation (nass jali) for 'Ali's imamate, leading to takfir of the Companions. It lists the line of imams from Ali to Muhammad al-Mahdi. It notes that they had disagreements after Ja'far, but settled on Musa al-Kazim. Then it explains the later splits: some became Mu'tazila (either Wa'idiyya emphasizing threat, or Tafdiliyya preferring Ali), some became Akhbariyya (accepting outward of ambiguous hadiths), and within Akhbariyya, some are Mushabbiha (anthropomorphists) and some are Salafiyya (affirming without tashbih). Some also joined deviant sects.

النص الجلي
الإمام المنتظر
الإخبارية
المشبهة
السلفية
الوعيدية
التفضيلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think all Imamiyya are Akhbariyya, believing only in literal hadith.
Correction: The passage shows Imamiyya split into Mu'tazila (rationalists) and Akhbariyya (literalists), among others.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, into which two groups did the Akhbariyya split?
A) Wa'idiyya and Tafdiliyya
B) Mushabbiha and Salafiyya
C) Mu'tazila and Ash'ariyya
D) Jarudiyya and Butriyya

Key Takeaway
The Imamiyya's doctrine of nass jali led to a specific imam line, but later internal divisions produced rationalist and literalist branches.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Imamiyya held that the Companions became disbelievers for not accepting 'Ali's imamate. Do you carry any resentment or negative judgments against any Companions? How would you respond if you discovered your view was based on assumptions rather than evidence? Are you willing to check your heart and correct it even if it requires letting go of a long-held bias?
?
The Imamiyya initially followed the madhhab of their imams, but over time they splintered into groups that adopted rationalism or literalism, some falling into tashbih. Are you blindly following a scholar or a group without verifying their teachings against the Qur'an and Sunnah? What would it take for you to leave a group if you found their beliefs deviated? Could your loyalty to a particular figure be idolatry in disguise?
?
The Akhbariyya among the Imamiyya insisted on the outward meaning of ambiguous hadiths, leading some to anthropomorphism. Do you ever take verses or hadiths about Allah's attributes in a literal sense without considering the understanding of the Salaf? How can you ensure you affirm what Allah has said without falling into tashbih or ta'til? Are you willing to submit to the scholars of the Salaf even if their interpretations are difficult for you?

Al-Muhakkima: The First Khariji Sub-Sect
Description of the Muhakkima sub-sect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the origins and doctrines of the Muhakkima, including their views on imamate and takfir.

Core Idea
The Muhakkima declared 'Ali a disbeliever over arbitration and held that an unjust imam must be removed.

The Khawarij emerged from the arbitration incident at Siffin. The first sub-sect, al-Muhakkima, rejected 'Ali's acceptance of arbitration and declared him a disbeliever. This lesson examines their beliefs, including their definition of imamate and their practice of excommunication.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Muhakkima
Read the Arabic passage describing the Muhakkima and its translation. Note the hadith about their piety but shallow faith.
The hadith is a key insight into their religious devotion despite their extremism.
2
Identify key beliefs
List the doctrines attributed to the Muhakkima: takfir of 'Ali, conditional imamate, non-obligation of having an imam, and takfir of 'Uthman, many Companions, and major sinners.
3
Reflect on imamate
Consider how the Muhakkima's view on imamate differs from mainstream Sunni Islam. They allowed for the possibility of having no imam at all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرقة الثالثة من كبار الفرق الإسلامية الخوارج وهم سبع فرق : المحكمة : وهم الذين خرجوا على علي عند التحكيم وما جرى بين الحكمين، وكفروه وهم اثنا عشر الف رجل كانوا أهل صلاة وصيام وفيهم قال النبي ﷺ يحقر أحدكم صلاته في جنب صلاتهم وصومه في جنب صومهم ولكن لا يجاوز إيمانهم تراقيهم قالوا : من نصب من قريش وغيرهم وعدل فيما بين الناس فهو إمام وإن غير السيرة وجار وجب أن يعزل أو يقتل ولم يوجبوا نصب الإمام بل جوزوا أن لا يكون في العالم إمام وكفروا عثمان وأكثر الصحابة ومرتكب الكبيرة. البيهسية : هو بيهس بن الهيصم بن جابر قالوا : الإيمان هو الإقرار والعلم بالله وبما جاء به الرسول فمن وقع فيما لا يعرف أحلال هو أم حرام فهو كافر لوجوب الفحص عليه حتى يعلم الحق ، وقيل : لا يكفر حتى يرفع أمره إلى الإمام فيحده وكل ما ليس فيه حد فهو مغفور وقيل : لا حرام إلا ما في قوله تعالى : قل لا أجد فيما أوحي إلي محرماً ﴾ [الأنعام : ١٤٥] الآية ، وقيل : إذا كفر الإمام كفرت الرعية حاضراً أو غائباً و قالوا : الأطفال كآبائهم إيماناً وكفراً و قال بعضهم : السكر من شراب حلال لا يؤاخذ صاحبه بما قال وفعل بخلاف السكر من شراب حرام وقيل : هو أي السكر مع الكبيرة كفر ، ووافقوا القدرية في إسناد أفعال العباد إليهم الأزارقة : هو نافع بن الأزرق قالوا كفر علي بالتحكيم وهو الذي أنزل فيه ومن الناس من يعجبك قوله في الحياة الدنيا ويشهد الله على ما في قلبه وهو ألد الخصام ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٠٤ ] ، وابن ملجم محق فيقتله وهو الذي أنزل فيه ومن الناس من يشري نفسه ابتغاء مرضاة الله ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۰۷]، وفيه قال مفتي الخوارج وزاهدها عمران بن حطان : يا ضربة من تقي ما أراد بها إلا ليبلغ من ذي العرش رضوانا إني لأذكره يوماً فأحسبه أوفى البرية عند الله ميزانا وكفرت الصحابة أي عثمان وطلحة والزبير وعائشة وعبد بن عباس وسائر المسلمين معهم وقضوا بتخليدهم في النار ، وكفروا القعدة عن القتال وإن كانوا موافقيهم لهم في الدين وقالوا تحرم التقية في القول والعمل، ويجوز
The third sect of the major Islamic sects: the Khawarij. They are seven sects: al-Muhakkima: they are those who rebelled against 'Ali at the time of arbitration (tahkim) and what transpired between the two arbiters, and they declared him a disbeliever. They were twelve thousand men, people of prayer and fasting, and the Prophet ﷺ said about them: 'One of you would consider his prayer insignificant compared to their prayer, and his fasting compared to their fasting, but their faith does not go beyond their collarbones.' They said: whoever is appointed from Quraysh or others and is just among the people is the imam, even if he changes conduct and is unjust, he must be removed or killed. They did not obligate the appointment of an imam; rather they permitted that there be no imam in the world. They declared 'Uthman and most of the Companions and the committer of a major sin (kabira) disbelievers. al-Bayhasiyya: he is Bayhas ibn al-Haysam ibn Jabir. They said: faith (iman) is affirmation (iqrar) and knowledge of God and what the Messenger brought. Whoever falls into something he does not know whether it is lawful or unlawful is a disbeliever, because it is obligatory upon him to investigate until he knows the truth. And it is said: he is not a disbeliever until his case is raised to the imam who then punishes him; and whatever has no prescribed punishment (hadd) is forgiven. And it is said: there is nothing unlawful except what is in His statement: 'Say: I do not find in what has been revealed to me anything forbidden' (6:145). And it is said: if the imam disbelieves, then the subjects, whether present or absent, disbelieve. And they said: children follow their parents in faith and disbelief. And some of them said: intoxication from a lawful drink does not hold its perpetrator accountable for what he says and does, unlike intoxication from an unlawful drink. And it is said: intoxication along with a major sin is disbelief. And they agreed with the Qadariyya in attributing the actions of servants to themselves. al-Azariqa: he is Nafi' ibn al-Azraq. They said: 'Ali disbelieved by accepting arbitration, and he is the one about whom was revealed: 'And among the people is he whose speech pleases you in worldly life' (2:204). Ibn Muljam was correct in killing him, and he is the one about whom was revealed: 'And among the people is he who sells himself seeking the pleasure of God' (2:207). Concerning him, the mufti of the Khawarij and their ascetic, 'Imran ibn Hittan, said: 'O blow from a pious one, he intended nothing by it except to obtain the pleasure of the Lord of the Throne. I remember him one day and consider him the most righteous of creation in God's balance.' And they declared the Companions disbelievers, i.e., 'Uthman, Talha, al-Zubayr, 'A'isha, 'Abd ibn 'Abbas, and the rest of the Muslims with them, and they judged that they would remain in the Fire forever. And they declared those who sat back from fighting disbelievers, even if they agreed with them in religion. And they said: dissimulation (taqiyya) is forbidden in speech and deed. And it is permissible...
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage introduces the Khawarij as the third major Islamic sect and lists seven sub-sects, detailing three: al-Muhakkima, al-Bayhasiyya, and al-Azariqa. For al-Muhakkima, it describes their origin from the arbitration incident, their religious devotion, the hadith about them, their views on imamate (conditional, non-obligatory), and their takfir of 'Uthman, many Companions, and major sinners. For al-Bayhasiyya, it details their definition of faith as affirmation and knowledge, their strict position on investigating the lawful/unlawful leading to takfir, the possibility of punishment by the imam, the limited scope of haram, the imam's disbelief causing the subjects' disbelief, children following parents in faith, rulings on intoxication, and their agreement with Qadariyya on free will. For al-Azariqa, it mentions their takfir of 'Ali for accepting arbitration, identifying him with a Quranic verse, and praising Ibn Muljam with a verse and poetry; they also declared takfir on the Companions and those who abstain from fighting, and forbidden taqiyya. The passage ends abruptly with 'and it is permissible' indicating a continuation.

Key Terms
الخوارج
المحكمة
التكفير
الإمامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Khawarij were purely violent and lacked religious devotion.
Correction: The hadith shows the Muhakkima were extremely devout in prayer and fasting, but their faith was shallow and misguided.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did the Muhakkima say about the imam who becomes unjust?
A) He must be obeyed
B) He must be removed or killed
C) He can be ignored
D) He is still a believer

Key Takeaway
The Muhakkima represent the earliest Khariji sect, combining intense piety with radical takfir and a conditional, non-obligatory imamate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Muhakkima had tremendous outward devotion—prayer and fasting that would put your own practice to shame—yet the Prophet said their faith barely scratched the surface. Where in your own life is your religious practice deeper than your heart? What will you change today to let your worship reach your soul?
?
They declared 'Uthman and most Companions disbelievers over issues they didn't fully understand. Think of a Muslim you have silently judged as misguided or less of a believer. Does that judgment stem from God's knowledge or your own limited understanding? How can you guard against the same spirit of takfir in your heart?
?
The Muhakkima believed an unjust leader must be removed, even if it means chaos. Reflect on a leader or authority you resent. Is your criticism rooted in a desire for justice or in a lack of trust in God's will? What would it look like to seek justice without arrogating God's judgment to yourself?

Al-Bayhasiyya: A Sub-Sect with Unique Views on Faith and Intoxication
Description of the Bayhasiyya sub-sect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinct doctrines of the Bayhasiyya, including their definition of faith, rulings on the unlawful, and views on intoxication and free will.

Core Idea
The Bayhasiyya defined faith as affirmation and knowledge, and held that ignorance of the lawful/unlawful leads to disbelief.

The Bayhasiyya, named after Bayhas ibn al-Haysam, held several unique positions among the Khawarij. This lesson explores their definition of faith as requiring investigation, their varied rulings on intoxication, and their agreement with the Qadariyya on human agency.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Bayhasiyya
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the chain of narrations (qila) indicating multiple views within the sect.
2
Analyze the definition of faith
The Bayhasiyya said iman is iqrar (affirmation) and 'ilm (knowledge). Failure to investigate the lawful/unlawful results in takfir.
3
Examine their views on intoxication
They distinguished between lawful and unlawful intoxicants, and some held that intoxication plus a major sin is disbelief.
4
Note their agreement with Qadariyya
They attributed actions of servants to themselves, aligning with Qadariyya on free will.

الفرقة الثالثة من كبار الفرق الإسلامية الخوارج وهم سبع فرق : المحكمة : وهم الذين خرجوا على علي عند التحكيم وما جرى بين الحكمين، وكفروه وهم اثنا عشر الف رجل كانوا أهل صلاة وصيام وفيهم قال النبي ﷺ يحقر أحدكم صلاته في جنب صلاتهم وصومه في جنب صومهم ولكن لا يجاوز إيمانهم تراقيهم قالوا : من نصب من قريش وغيرهم وعدل فيما بين الناس فهو إمام وإن غير السيرة وجار وجب أن يعزل أو يقتل ولم يوجبوا نصب الإمام بل جوزوا أن لا يكون في العالم إمام وكفروا عثمان وأكثر الصحابة ومرتكب الكبيرة. البيهسية : هو بيهس بن الهيصم بن جابر قالوا : الإيمان هو الإقرار والعلم بالله وبما جاء به الرسول فمن وقع فيما لا يعرف أحلال هو أم حرام فهو كافر لوجوب الفحص عليه حتى يعلم الحق ، وقيل : لا يكفر حتى يرفع أمره إلى الإمام فيحده وكل ما ليس فيه حد فهو مغفور وقيل : لا حرام إلا ما في قوله تعالى : قل لا أجد فيما أوحي إلي محرماً ﴾ [الأنعام : ١٤٥] الآية ، وقيل : إذا كفر الإمام كفرت الرعية حاضراً أو غائباً و قالوا : الأطفال كآبائهم إيماناً وكفراً و قال بعضهم : السكر من شراب حلال لا يؤاخذ صاحبه بما قال وفعل بخلاف السكر من شراب حرام وقيل : هو أي السكر مع الكبيرة كفر ، ووافقوا القدرية في إسناد أفعال العباد إليهم الأزارقة : هو نافع بن الأزرق قالوا كفر علي بالتحكيم وهو الذي أنزل فيه ومن الناس من يعجبك قوله في الحياة الدنيا ويشهد الله على ما في قلبه وهو ألد الخصام ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٠٤ ] ، وابن ملجم محق فيقتله وهو الذي أنزل فيه ومن الناس من يشري نفسه ابتغاء مرضاة الله ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۰۷]، وفيه قال مفتي الخوارج وزاهدها عمران بن حطان : يا ضربة من تقي ما أراد بها إلا ليبلغ من ذي العرش رضوانا إني لأذكره يوماً فأحسبه أوفى البرية عند الله ميزانا وكفرت الصحابة أي عثمان وطلحة والزبير وعائشة وعبد بن عباس وسائر المسلمين معهم وقضوا بتخليدهم في النار ، وكفروا القعدة عن القتال وإن كانوا موافقيهم لهم في الدين وقالوا تحرم التقية في القول والعمل، ويجوز
The third sect of the major Islamic sects: the Khawarij. They are seven sects: al-Muhakkima: they are those who rebelled against 'Ali at the time of arbitration (tahkim) and what transpired between the two arbiters, and they declared him a disbeliever. They were twelve thousand men, people of prayer and fasting, and the Prophet ﷺ said about them: 'One of you would consider his prayer insignificant compared to their prayer, and his fasting compared to their fasting, but their faith does not go beyond their collarbones.' They said: whoever is appointed from Quraysh or others and is just among the people is the imam, even if he changes conduct and is unjust, he must be removed or killed. They did not obligate the appointment of an imam; rather they permitted that there be no imam in the world. They declared 'Uthman and most of the Companions and the committer of a major sin (kabira) disbelievers. al-Bayhasiyya: he is Bayhas ibn al-Haysam ibn Jabir. They said: faith (iman) is affirmation (iqrar) and knowledge of God and what the Messenger brought. Whoever falls into something he does not know whether it is lawful or unlawful is a disbeliever, because it is obligatory upon him to investigate until he knows the truth. And it is said: he is not a disbeliever until his case is raised to the imam who then punishes him; and whatever has no prescribed punishment (hadd) is forgiven. And it is said: there is nothing unlawful except what is in His statement: 'Say: I do not find in what has been revealed to me anything forbidden' (6:145). And it is said: if the imam disbelieves, then the subjects, whether present or absent, disbelieve. And they said: children follow their parents in faith and disbelief. And some of them said: intoxication from a lawful drink does not hold its perpetrator accountable for what he says and does, unlike intoxication from an unlawful drink. And it is said: intoxication along with a major sin is disbelief. And they agreed with the Qadariyya in attributing the actions of servants to themselves. al-Azariqa: he is Nafi' ibn al-Azraq. They said: 'Ali disbelieved by accepting arbitration, and he is the one about whom was revealed: 'And among the people is he whose speech pleases you in worldly life' (2:204). Ibn Muljam was correct in killing him, and he is the one about whom was revealed: 'And among the people is he who sells himself seeking the pleasure of God' (2:207). Concerning him, the mufti of the Khawarij and their ascetic, 'Imran ibn Hittan, said: 'O blow from a pious one, he intended nothing by it except to obtain the pleasure of the Lord of the Throne. I remember him one day and consider him the most righteous of creation in God's balance.' And they declared the Companions disbelievers, i.e., 'Uthman, Talha, al-Zubayr, 'A'isha, 'Abd ibn 'Abbas, and the rest of the Muslims with them, and they judged that they would remain in the Fire forever. And they declared those who sat back from fighting disbelievers, even if they agreed with them in religion. And they said: dissimulation (taqiyya) is forbidden in speech and deed. And it is permissible...
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage introduces the Khawarij as the third major Islamic sect and lists seven sub-sects, detailing three: al-Muhakkima, al-Bayhasiyya, and al-Azariqa. For al-Muhakkima, it describes their origin from the arbitration incident, their religious devotion, the hadith about them, their views on imamate (conditional, non-obligatory), and their takfir of 'Uthman, many Companions, and major sinners. For al-Bayhasiyya, it details their definition of faith as affirmation and knowledge, their strict position on investigating the lawful/unlawful leading to takfir, the possibility of punishment by the imam, the limited scope of haram, the imam's disbelief causing the subjects' disbelief, children following parents in faith, rulings on intoxication, and their agreement with Qadariyya on free will. For al-Azariqa, it mentions their takfir of 'Ali for accepting arbitration, identifying him with a Quranic verse, and praising Ibn Muljam with a verse and poetry; they also declared takfir on the Companions and those who abstain from fighting, and forbidden taqiyya. The passage ends abruptly with 'and it is permissible' indicating a continuation.

Key Terms
البيهسية
الإيمان
السكر
القدرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Khawarij held the same view on faith and actions.
Correction: The Bayhasiyya had unique, nuanced positions, including a definition of faith as knowledge and affirmation, and a distinction between lawful and unlawful intoxication.

Checkpoint
According to the Bayhasiyya, what happens to a child whose parents are disbelievers?
A) The child is born a believer
B) The child follows the parents in disbelief
C) The child is judged by his own actions
D) The child is not accountable

Key Takeaway
The Bayhasiyya held distinctive doctrines on faith as knowledge, limited haram, children's status, and free will, showing internal diversity among Khawarij.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Bayhasiyya considered ignorance of the lawful or unlawful as disbelief because investigation is obligatory. When was the last time you deliberately avoided learning about a ruling because you knew it would change your behavior? What are you hiding from?
?
Some Bayhasiyya said that intoxication from a lawful drink does not hold one accountable, but from an unlawful drink it does. Do you ever justify your own spiritual negligence by claiming the 'source' is permissible while ignoring the actual state of your heart? How would you feel if Allah held you to the standard you apply to others?
?
They said children follow their parents in faith and disbelief. Have you inherited beliefs or practices from your family without examining them yourself? What would it cost you to truly investigate your own convictions rather than rely on someone else's?

Sects and Disagreements

Al-Azariqa: The Extreme Khariji Sub-Sect
Description of the Azariqa sub-sect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extreme positions of the Azariqa, including their takfir of 'Ali, the Companions, and those who abstain from fighting, and their forbiddance of taqiyya.

Core Idea
The Azariqa declared most Muslims disbelievers, including 'Ali and the Companions, and forbade dissimulation in speech and deed.

The Azariqa, followers of Nafi' ibn al-Azraq, represent the most extreme Khariji sect. They not only declared 'Ali a disbeliever but also excommunicated most Companions and all who did not join their fight. This lesson explores their radical views and their use of Quranic verses to justify their actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Azariqa
Read the Arabic and translation. Note how they quote Quranic verses to support their positions.
2
Identify their takfir targets
They declared 'Ali, 'Uthman, Talha, al-Zubayr, 'A'isha, Ibn 'Abbas, and all who did not fight alongside them as disbelievers, destined for eternal hell.
3
Understand their view on taqiyya
They forbade taqiyya (dissimulation) in both speech and deed, unlike some other sects.
4
Reflect on the poetry about Ibn Muljam
They praised the assassin of 'Ali, considering him a righteous martyr, and used a Quranic verse to support that.

?
Have you ever judged someone's faith based on a single action or disagreement, the way the Azariqa judged 'Ali for accepting arbitration? What does this lesson teach you about the danger of such a mindset?
?

?
The Azariqa not only excommunicated others but also demanded active participation in their cause. Are there any beliefs you hold that you are not willing to act upon? What would it cost you to live out your faith fully, and are you ready to pay that price?

Classification of the Report-Based Group (al-Ikhbariyya)
Passage classifies the Ikhbariyya into three subgroups.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three subgroups of the Ikhbariyya and their different approaches to ambiguous scriptural texts.

Core Idea
Not all who affirm ambiguous texts are anthropomorphists; the Salafiyya affirm without comparison.

This passage from al-Ījī's Mawāqif introduces a subgroup called the Ikhbāriyya—those who base their theology on the outward meaning of ambiguous reports. Within this group, there are important distinctions in how they handle such texts. The author classifies them into three types, revealing a spectrum from literal anthropomorphism to a more reserved affirmation that avoids likening God to creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the author's own wording. Notice the key terms: Ikhbāriyya, Mushabbiha, Salafiyya, and mutashābihāt.
The passage is very concise; each term carries significant theological weight.
2
Identify the three subgroups
The passage divides the Ikhbāriyya into three categories. Find each one and note how they differ in their approach to ambiguous verses.
The third category is only briefly mentioned as those who join deviant sects.
3
Compare Mushabbiha and Salafiyya
The Mushabbiha take ambiguous texts literally, leading to anthropomorphism. The Salafiyya affirm the texts as true but without engaging in tashbīh (comparison). Why is this distinction important?
This contrast shows that affirming the outward meaning does not necessarily imply anthropomorphism.
4
Reflect on the third category
Consider the third group: those who join deviant sects. Why do you think the author includes them in this classification? What does it suggest about the boundaries of orthodoxy?
This category may refer to groups like the Karrāmiyya or others who went beyond affirmation to heretical beliefs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإلى إخبارية يعتقدون ظاهر ما ورد به الأخبار المتشابهة وهؤلاء ينقسمون إلى مشبهة يجرون المتشابهات على أن المراد بها ظواهرها وسلفية يعتقدون أن ما أورد الله بها حق بلا تشبيه كما عليه السلف وإلى ملتحقة بالفرق الضالة.
And to the report-based (Ikhbāriyya) who believe in the outward meaning of what came in the ambiguous reports, and these are divided into the anthropomorphists (Mushabbiha) who apply the ambiguous verses to their outward meanings, and the Salafīs who believe that what God brought in them is true without comparison, as followed by the predecessors, and to those who join the deviant sects.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage classifies a subgroup called the Ikhbāriyya (report-based group) within a larger sect. It divides them into three types: first, the Mushabbiha, who take ambiguous scriptural texts literally and thus fall into anthropomorphism; second, the Salafiyya, who affirm those texts as true but without engaging in comparison (tashbīh), following the way of the early Muslims; and third, those who affiliate themselves with deviant sects. The passage shows the spectrum of approaches to ambiguous texts among those who claim to follow the reports.

Key Terms
إخبارية
مشبهة
سلفية
متشابهات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All who affirm the literal meaning of ambiguous verses are anthropomorphists.
Correction: The passage distinguishes the Mushabbiha, who take literalism to the point of tashbīh, from the Salafiyya, who affirm the same texts as true without comparing God to creation.

Checkpoint
How does the Salafiyya approach the ambiguous reports (mutashābihāt) according to this passage?
A) They interpret them allegorically.
B) They believe they are true without likening God to creation.
C) They reject them as fabricated.
D) They follow the Mushabbiha in taking them literally.

Key Takeaway
The Ikhbāriyya are not a monolithic group; they include anthropomorphists, the Salafiyya who affirm without comparison, and those who join deviant sects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter an ambiguous verse about Allah's attributes, is your first reaction to accept it as true without trying to imagine 'how'? Or do you unconsciously form a mental image? What does that reveal about your heart's reliance on Allah's revelation?
?
The Salafiyya affirm what Allah has revealed without comparison. Is your belief in Allah's attributes built on the same humble submission, or do you find yourself leaning toward either extreme—either rejecting the texts or anthropomorphizing? Which tendency do you need to correct today?
?
The passage warns against joining deviant sects. Have you ever uncritically adopted a view about Allah's attributes because it was popular in your circle, without checking if it aligns with the way of the Salaf? What step will you take to ensure your 'aqīdah is grounded in the Qur’an and Sunnah as understood by the early Muslims?

The Khawarij and the Muhakkima Sub-Sect
Introduces the Khawarij and describes the Muhakkima sub-sect with origin and prophetic critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand who the Khawarij are, their division into seven sects, and the origin and characteristics of the Muhakkima sub-sect.

Core Idea
The Khawarij are a major sect; the Muhakkima are those who rejected arbitration and declared Ali a disbeliever.

This lesson begins our study of the third major Islamic sect: the Khawarij. We will first meet the Khawarij as a group, then zoom in on the first sub-sect, al-Muhakkima. You will learn about their dramatic break with Ali during the arbitration, their surprising piety, and even a prophetic hadith that warns about their shallow faith despite impressive worship.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic slowly, noting key terms like الخوارج and المحكمة. Then read the English translation.
The passage is short but dense; take time to absorb each clause.
2
Identify the three parts
Notice that the passage first states the Khawarij are seven sects, then defines the Muhakkima sub-sect by their origin, and finally describes their piety and the Prophet’s warning.
The hadith is a powerful critique – they are extremely devout but their faith is superficial.
3
Reflect on the hadith
Ask yourself: why would the Prophet mention their great worship? What does ‘faith not reaching beyond collarbones’ mean?
This shows that outward piety without correct creed and action can be worthless.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرقة الثالثة من كبار الفرق الإسلامية الخوارج وهم سبع فرق المحكمة وهم الذين خرجوا على علي عند التحكيم وما جرى بين الحكمين وكفروه وهم اثنا عشر ألف رجل كانوا أهل صلاة وصيام وفيهم قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يحقر أحدكم صلاته في جنب صلاتهم وصومه في جنب صومهم ولكن لا يجاوز إيمانهم تراقيهم قالوا من نصب من قريش وغيرهم وعدل فيما بين الناس فهو إمام وإن غير السيرة وجار وجب أن يعزل أو يقتل ولم يوجبوا نصب الإمام بل جوزوا أن لا يكون في العالم إمام وكفروا عثمان وأكثر الصحابة ومرتكب الكبيرة.
The third sect among the major Islamic sects is the Khawārij, and they are seven sects: al-Muḥakkima – they are those who rebelled against ʿAlī at the time of arbitration and what occurred between the two arbiters, and they declared him a disbeliever. They were twelve thousand men who were people of prayer and fasting, and among them the Prophet ﷺ said, 'One of you would regard his prayer as insignificant compared to their prayer, and his fasting as insignificant compared to their fasting, but their faith does not go beyond their collarbones.' They said: Whoever is appointed from Quraysh or others and is just among the people is an imam, and if he deviates from the sunna and acts tyrannically, he must be removed or killed. They did not consider the appointment of an imam obligatory, but permitted that there be no imam in the world. They declared ʿUthmān, most of the Companions, and the committer of grave sins to be disbelievers.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage opens the discussion of the Khawarij, identifying them as the third major Islamic sect and listing their seven subsects. It then focuses on the first subsect, al-Muḥakkima, explaining their origin from the arbitration conflict between ʿAlī and Muʿāwiya, which led them to declare ʿAlī a disbeliever. Despite their piety (twelve thousand devoted worshippers), the Prophet ﷺ criticized their faith as shallow. Their political doctrines include: the imam must be from Quraysh and just, and if he deviates he must be removed or killed; they did not require an imam to be appointed. In terms of takfir, they condemned ʿUthmān, most Companions, and all grave sinners.

Key Terms
الخوارج
المحكمة
التحكيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Because the Prophet praised their worship, their actions are acceptable and they are true believers.
Correction: The Prophet's praise of their worship is followed by a critique: their faith is shallow and does not reach the heart. Outward piety without correct creed is worthless.

Checkpoint
How did the Muhakkima originate?
A) They were a tribe that rejected Islam
B) They rebelled against Ali at the time of arbitration between him and Muawiya
C) They were followers of a false prophet
D) They were Companions who refused to fight

Key Takeaway
The Muhakkima sub-sect of the Khawarij are characterized by extreme piety but shallow faith, as warned by the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you rely on your acts of worship as proof of your faith, while neglecting the condition of your heart? What if your prayer and fasting are accepted only outwardly—would you know?
?
How often do you judge others as disbelievers because they disagree with you on a matter of religion? What does the Prophet's warning about the Khawarij say about that attitude?
?
The Prophet said that the Khawarij's faith does not go beyond their collarbones. If the Prophet ﷺ examined your heart, what depth of faith would he find? What can you do today to ensure your faith penetrates your soul?

The Beliefs of al-Muhakkima: Politics and Takfir
Details the political and takfiri doctrines of al-Muhakkima.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the political doctrine of al-Muhakkima regarding the imam and their practice of takfir against Uthman, most Companions, and grave sinners.

Core Idea
Al-Muhakkima held that an unjust imam must be removed or killed, and they declared many early Muslims as disbelievers.

Having learned who the Muhakkima are, we now turn to their specific beliefs. This passage reveals two major aspects of their ideology: a radical political theory about the imamate and a broad application of takfir that included Uthman, the majority of the Companions, and anyone who commits a grave sin. These positions set them apart from mainstream Sunni Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the two parts: political doctrine (imamate) and takfir (who they declared disbelievers).
Notice the phrase 'قالوا' introduces their statements.
2
Analyze the political doctrine
They say the imam must be from Quraysh (or anyone) if just; if he deviates, he must be removed or killed. They also do not consider an imam obligatory. Compare this with Sunni consensus.
Their view is radical: they permit anarchy if no just imam exists.
3
Examine the takfir list
They declare Uthman, most Companions, and the committer of grave sins as disbelievers. This shows their extremism in excommunication.
This was a major reason for their conflict with the mainstream community.

Source Text

?

?

?

The Bayhasiyya: Faith, Children, and Intoxication
Passage defines the Bayhasiyya sect's doctrines on faith, ignorance, children's status, and agreement with Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key doctrines of the Bayhasiyya, including their definition of faith, rulings on investigation, children's status, and intoxication.

Core Idea
The Bayhasiyya defined faith as knowledge and confession, and held that ignorance of the law is disbelief.

The Bayhasiyya, a Kharijite sub-sect, held extreme views on faith and legal responsibility. They required exhaustive investigation (faḥṣ) to determine the lawful and unlawful, and considered failure to do so as disbelief. Their doctrines extended to children inheriting their parents' faith status and to intoxication rulings that distinguished between lawful and unlawful drinks. This passage outlines their distinctive positions, including their alignment with the Qadariyya on free will.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of faith
The Bayhasiyya said faith is both inner confession and knowledge of God and the Prophet. Note that this excludes mere verbal profession without understanding.
They emphasized knowledge (ʿilm) as essential.
2
Explore the duty of investigation
Whoever falls into something unknown regarding its lawfulness must investigate until he knows the truth; if he does not, he is a disbeliever. Alternative opinions exist within the sect.
This is an extreme legal obligation.
3
Examine views on children and intoxication
Children are like their parents in faith and disbelief. Intoxication from a lawful drink does not incur liability, but from an unlawful drink combined with a grave sin is disbelief.
These rulings reflect their rigid legalism.
4
Identify agreement with Qadariyya
They attributed actions of servants to themselves, aligning with the Qadariyya on free will.
This contrasts with the predestinarian views of other Kharijites.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البيهسية هو بيهس بن الهيصم بن جابر قالوا الإيمان هو الإقرار والعلم بالله وبما جاء به الرسول فمن وقع فيما لا يعرف أحلال هو أم حرام فهو كافر لوجوب الفحص عليه حتى يعلم الحق وقيل لا يكفر حتى يرفع أمره إلى الإمام فيحده وكل ما ليس فيه حد فهو مغفور وقيل لا حرام إلا ما في قوله تعالى قل لا أجد فيما أوحي إلي محرما الآية وقيل إذا كفر الإمام كفرت الرعية حاضراً أو غائباً وقالوا الأطفال كآبائهم إيماناً وكفراً وقال بعضهم السكر من شراب حلال لا يؤاخذ صاحبه بما قال وفعل بخلاف السكر من شراب حرام وقيل هو أي السكر مع الكبيرة كفر ووافقوا القدرية في إسناد أفعال العباد إليهم.
The Bayhasiyya – its founder was Bayhas ibn al-Haysam ibn Jābir. They said: Faith is confession and knowledge of God and of what the Messenger brought. Whoever falls into something of which he does not know whether it is lawful or unlawful is a disbeliever, because he must investigate until he knows the truth. And it was said: He is not a disbeliever until his case is referred to the imam, who then punishes him, and everything for which there is no prescribed punishment is forgiven. And it was said: There is no unlawful except what is in His statement, 'Say: I do not find in what has been revealed to me anything forbidden' (Q 6:145) – the verse. And it was said: When the imam becomes a disbeliever, the subjects become disbelievers, whether present or absent. And they said: Children are like their parents in faith and disbelief. And some of them said: Intoxication from a lawful drink does not hold the person accountable for what he says or does, unlike intoxication from an unlawful drink. And it was said: It – i.e., intoxication along with a grave sin – is disbelief. And they agreed with the Qadariyya in attributing the actions of servants to themselves.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage details the doctrines of the Bayhasiyya, a Kharijite sub-sect founded by Bayhas ibn al-Haysam. They defined faith as both inner confession (iqrār) and knowledge (ʿilm) of God and the Prophet. Consequently, anyone who fails to ascertain whether an act is lawful or unlawful is deemed a disbeliever for not fulfilling the duty of examination (faḥṣ). However, alternative opinions within the sect held that punishment awaits only after the imam's judgment, or that only sins explicitly forbidden in the Qur’an (citing Q 6:145) are unlawful. They also held the imam's disbelief implicates all subjects, that children inherit their parents' faith status, and that intoxication from lawful drinks does not incur liability, while intoxication from unlawful drinks combined with a grave sin constitutes disbelief. Finally, they agreed with the Qadariyya on the issue of human free will, attributing actions to the servants themselves.

Key Terms
البيهسية
بيهس بن الهيصم
الإقرار
العلم
الفحص
القدرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Bayhasiyya believed that children inherit faith by birth.
Correction: The passage says children are like their parents in faith and disbelief, meaning they follow the legal status of their parents in this worldly life, not that faith is biologically inherited. It reflects their rigid legalism.

Checkpoint
What is the status of intoxication according to some of the Bayhasiyya?
A) It is always a grave sin.
B) It is allowed if from a lawful drink.
C) Intoxication from a lawful drink does not incur liability, but from an unlawful drink combined with a grave sin is disbelief.
D) All intoxication is forgiven.

Key Takeaway
The Bayhasiyya held an extremely legalistic view of faith that demanded exhaustive investigation, and they extended their logic to children and intoxication while aligning with Qadariyya on free will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What if you were required to investigate every religious ruling before acting on it? Would your daily practice change? Would you be willing to do that, or do you rely on what you've always been told?
?
If your children's faith and disbelief depended entirely on your own, how would that reshape your responsibilities as a parent? Are you living in a way that would lead them to faith or disbelief?
?
The Bayhasiyya distinguished between intoxication from lawful and unlawful drinks. What 'lawful' comforts or escapes do you use that may cloud your judgment? Do you hold yourself accountable for words and deeds said under their influence?
