The Core Doctrines of the 'Ajarda Sect
Definition of 'Ajarda and its core doctrine of mandatory disavowal of children.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the defining beliefs of the 'Ajarda sect, especially their obligation to disavow children until they accept Islam after puberty and their judgment that children of polytheists go to Hell.

Core Idea
'Ajarda made disavowal of children mandatory and placed all polytheist children in the Fire.

The 'Ajarda, the seventh group of Khawarij, built on the Najdiyya but added a unique stance on children. They required believers to disavow children who have not yet professed Islam after reaching puberty, and they held that the children of polytheists are destined for Hell. This passage introduces these core doctrines before listing their ten sub-sects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on 'Ajarda's foundation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the main belief: obligatory disavowal of children until they profess Islam after puberty, and the fiery fate of polytheist children.
Notice the phrase 'وجوب البراءة عن الطفل'—this is the central tenet.
2
Identify the two doctrines
The passage presents two specific doctrines: (1) the obligation to disavow children and call them to Islam after puberty, and (2) that children of polytheists are in Hell. Make sure you can state each.
3
Reflect on the context
Consider how these doctrines relate to the broader Khawarij position on radical disavowal (bara'a) and judgment based on belief. How does this differ from mainstream Islam?
This passage sets the stage for the sub-sects that follow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العجاردة: هو عبد الرحمن بن عجرد وهم آخر السبع من فرق الخوارج زادوا على النجدات بعد أن وافقوهم في مذهبهم وجوب البراءة عن الطفل أي يجب أن يتبرأ عنه حتى يدعي الإسلام بعد البلوغ ويجب دعاؤه إليه أي إلى الإسلام إذا بلغ، وأطفال المشركين في النار. وهم عشر فرق: الأولى: الميمونية: هو ميمون بن عمران قالوا بالقدر أي إسناد الأفعال إلى قدر العباد، ويكون الاستطاعة قبل الفعل، وأن الله يريد الخير دون الشر ولا يريد المعاصي كما هو مذهب المعتزلة، قالوا: وأطفال الكفار في الجنة، ويروى عنهم تجويز نكاح البنات للبنين وللبنات ولأولاد الإخوة والأخوات أي جوزوا نكاح بنات البنين وبنات البنات وبنات أولاد الإخوة والأخوات، وإنكار سورة يوسف فإنهم زعموا أنها قصة من القصص ولا يجوز أن تكون قصة الفسق قرآناً. الثانية: من فرق العجاردة والحمزية: هو حمزة بن أدرك، وافقوهم أي الميمونية فيما ذهبوا إليه من البدع إلا أنهم قالوا أطفال الكفار في النار. الثالثة منهم: الشعيبية: هو شعيب بن محمد وهم كالميمونية في بدعهم إلا في القدر. الرابعة: الحازمية هو حازم بن عاصم وافقوا الشعيبية ويحكى عنهم أنهم يتوقفون في أمر علي ولا يصرحون بالبراءة عنه كما يصرحون بالبراءة عن غيره. الخامسة: الخلفية: أصحاب خلف الخارجي وهم خوارج كرمان ومكران أضافوا القدر خيره وشره إلى الله وحكموا بأن أطفال المشركين في النار بلا عمل وشرك. السادسة: الأطرافية هم على مذهب حمزة ورئيسهم رجل من سجستان يقال له غالب إلا أنهم عذروا أهل الأطراف فيما لم يعرفوه من الشريعة إذا أتوا بما يعرف
'Ajarda: He is 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Ajrad. They are the last of the seven sects of the Khawarij. They added to the Najdiyya after agreeing with their school the obligation of disavowal (bara'a) of the child: i.e., one must disavow him until he professes Islam after puberty, and it is obligatory to call him to it, i.e., to Islam, when he reaches puberty. And the children of polytheists are in the Fire. They are ten sects: First: the Maymuniyya: He is Maymun ibn 'Imran. They held qadar (divine predestination), i.e., attributing actions to the power of servants, and that capability is before the act, and that Allah wills good not evil and does not will sins, as is the school of the Mu'tazila. They said: The children of disbelievers are in Paradise. It is narrated from them the permissibility of marrying daughters to sons, and to daughters, and to children of brothers and sisters, i.e., they permitted marriage of granddaughters and daughters of nieces/nephews, and the denial of Sura Yusuf, for they claimed it is a story from stories and it is not permissible for a story of lewdness to be Quran. Second: from the sub-sects of 'Ajarda is the Hamziyya: He is Hamza ibn Adrak. They agreed with the Maymuniyya in the innovations they adopted, except that they said the children of disbelievers are in the Fire. Third: the Shu'aybiyya: He is Shu'ayb ibn Muhammad, and they are like the Maymuniyya in their innovations except regarding qadar. Fourth: the Hazimiyya: He is Hazim ibn 'Asim. They agreed with the Shu'aybiyya, and it is narrated that they hesitated regarding 'Ali and did not explicitly declare disavowal of him as they declared disavowal of others. Fifth: the Khalafiyya: Followers of Khalaf al-Khariji, and they are the Khawarij of Kirman and Makran. They attributed qadar, its good and evil, to Allah, and judged that the children of polytheists are in the Fire without work or shirk. Sixth: the Atrafiyya: They follow the school of Hamza, and their leader is a man from Sijistan called Ghalib, except that they excused the people of the peripheries (atraf) for what they did not know of the Shari'a if they act according to what they know.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage describes the 'Ajarda sect, the seventh group of Khawarij. They emphasized disavowal of children until they profess Islam after puberty. They had ten sub-sects; six are detailed here. The Maymuniyya held Mu'tazili-like qadar, that children of disbelievers are in Paradise, permitted certain incestuous marriages, and denied Sura Yusuf. The Hamziyya agreed except they placed children of disbelievers in Hell. The Shu'aybiyya were like Maymuniyya except on qadar. The Hazimiyya hesitated on disavowing 'Ali. The Khalafiyya attributed all qadar to Allah and placed polytheist children in Hell. The Atrafiyya excused ignorance on the peripheries.

Key Terms
العجاردة
البراءة عن الطفل
أطفال المشركين في النار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the 'Ajarda, when must a child be disavowed?
A) From birth until he professes Islam after puberty
B) Only if he refuses Islam at puberty
C) Only if his parents are polytheists
D) Never, because children are innocent

Key Takeaway
The 'Ajarda sect required disavowal of children until they profess Islam after puberty and held that children of polytheists go to Hell.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear of a child from a non-Muslim family passing away, does your heart immediately lean toward assuming their damnation? How does this lesson’s specific statement about polytheist children challenge your inner assumptions, and what will you do to align your thoughts with God’s mercy?
?
The ʿAjarda made it an obligation to disavow children until they professed Islam. In your life, is there any person you have ‘disavowed’—held at a distance—because they have not yet embraced Islam? How will you replace that disavowal with the patient compassion of the Prophet (peace be upon him)?
?
Do you find it easy to pass absolute judgments about God’s treatment of others, like the ʿAjarda did? Identify one judgment you have made about someone’s destiny and repent from it today by acknowledging that only God knows the final state of any soul.

The Six Sub-Sects of the 'Ajarda
Enumeration of six 'Ajarda sub-sects with their distinctive doctrines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the six sub-sects of the 'Ajarda based on their specific doctrines regarding qadar, the fate of polytheist children, marriage, and other issues.

Core Idea
Maymuniyya, Hamziyya, Shu'aybiyya, Hazimiyya, Khalafiyya, and Atrafiyya each held distinct positions within the 'Ajarda framework.

The 'Ajarda split into ten sub-sects; this passage details six of them. Each sub-sect takes a different stance on qadar (divine predestination), the destiny of polytheist children, and other matters such as marriage and the denial of a Quranic sura. The Hamziyya, for example, agreed with the Maymuniyya except on the fate of children, while the Shu'aybiyya differed on qadar. Let's examine each one.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage listing the six sub-sects
Read the Arabic and translation carefully, focusing on the names of the sub-sects and the distinctive belief mentioned for each.
The passage begins with 'الأولى: الميمونية' and ends with 'السادسة: الأطرافية'.
2
Create a mental table of differences
For each sub-sect, note its position on qadar, the fate of polytheist children, and any unique doctrine (e.g., marriage, denial of Sura Yusuf, hesitancy about 'Ali).
The Maymuniyya and Shu'aybiyya differ on qadar; Hamziyya and Maymuniyya differ on children's fate.
3
Identify which sub-sect held which view on qadar
The Maymuniyya had a Mu'tazili-like qadar (actions from servants), the Shu'aybiyya did not hold that view, and the Khalafiyya attributed all qadar to Allah. Understand these distinctions.
4
Reflect on the variety within the 'Ajarda
Consider how these sub-sects demonstrate internal diversity despite common origins. This helps understand the complex history of the Khawarij.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العجاردة: هو عبد الرحمن بن عجرد وهم آخر السبع من فرق الخوارج زادوا على النجدات بعد أن وافقوهم في مذهبهم وجوب البراءة عن الطفل أي يجب أن يتبرأ عنه حتى يدعي الإسلام بعد البلوغ ويجب دعاؤه إليه أي إلى الإسلام إذا بلغ، وأطفال المشركين في النار. وهم عشر فرق: الأولى: الميمونية: هو ميمون بن عمران قالوا بالقدر أي إسناد الأفعال إلى قدر العباد، ويكون الاستطاعة قبل الفعل، وأن الله يريد الخير دون الشر ولا يريد المعاصي كما هو مذهب المعتزلة، قالوا: وأطفال الكفار في الجنة، ويروى عنهم تجويز نكاح البنات للبنين وللبنات ولأولاد الإخوة والأخوات أي جوزوا نكاح بنات البنين وبنات البنات وبنات أولاد الإخوة والأخوات، وإنكار سورة يوسف فإنهم زعموا أنها قصة من القصص ولا يجوز أن تكون قصة الفسق قرآناً. الثانية: من فرق العجاردة والحمزية: هو حمزة بن أدرك، وافقوهم أي الميمونية فيما ذهبوا إليه من البدع إلا أنهم قالوا أطفال الكفار في النار. الثالثة منهم: الشعيبية: هو شعيب بن محمد وهم كالميمونية في بدعهم إلا في القدر. الرابعة: الحازمية هو حازم بن عاصم وافقوا الشعيبية ويحكى عنهم أنهم يتوقفون في أمر علي ولا يصرحون بالبراءة عنه كما يصرحون بالبراءة عن غيره. الخامسة: الخلفية: أصحاب خلف الخارجي وهم خوارج كرمان ومكران أضافوا القدر خيره وشره إلى الله وحكموا بأن أطفال المشركين في النار بلا عمل وشرك. السادسة: الأطرافية هم على مذهب حمزة ورئيسهم رجل من سجستان يقال له غالب إلا أنهم عذروا أهل الأطراف فيما لم يعرفوه من الشريعة إذا أتوا بما يعرف
'Ajarda: He is 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Ajrad. They are the last of the seven sects of the Khawarij. They added to the Najdiyya after agreeing with their school the obligation of disavowal (bara'a) of the child: i.e., one must disavow him until he professes Islam after puberty, and it is obligatory to call him to it, i.e., to Islam, when he reaches puberty. And the children of polytheists are in the Fire. They are ten sects: First: the Maymuniyya: He is Maymun ibn 'Imran. They held qadar (divine predestination), i.e., attributing actions to the power of servants, and that capability is before the act, and that Allah wills good not evil and does not will sins, as is the school of the Mu'tazila. They said: The children of disbelievers are in Paradise. It is narrated from them the permissibility of marrying daughters to sons, and to daughters, and to children of brothers and sisters, i.e., they permitted marriage of granddaughters and daughters of nieces/nephews, and the denial of Sura Yusuf, for they claimed it is a story from stories and it is not permissible for a story of lewdness to be Quran. Second: from the sub-sects of 'Ajarda is the Hamziyya: He is Hamza ibn Adrak. They agreed with the Maymuniyya in the innovations they adopted, except that they said the children of disbelievers are in the Fire. Third: the Shu'aybiyya: He is Shu'ayb ibn Muhammad, and they are like the Maymuniyya in their innovations except regarding qadar. Fourth: the Hazimiyya: He is Hazim ibn 'Asim. They agreed with the Shu'aybiyya, and it is narrated that they hesitated regarding 'Ali and did not explicitly declare disavowal of him as they declared disavowal of others. Fifth: the Khalafiyya: Followers of Khalaf al-Khariji, and they are the Khawarij of Kirman and Makran. They attributed qadar, its good and evil, to Allah, and judged that the children of polytheists are in the Fire without work or shirk. Sixth: the Atrafiyya: They follow the school of Hamza, and their leader is a man from Sijistan called Ghalib, except that they excused the people of the peripheries (atraf) for what they did not know of the Shari'a if they act according to what they know.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage describes the 'Ajarda sect, the seventh group of Khawarij. They emphasized disavowal of children until they profess Islam after puberty. They had ten sub-sects; six are detailed here. The Maymuniyya held Mu'tazili-like qadar, that children of disbelievers are in Paradise, permitted certain incestuous marriages, and denied Sura Yusuf. The Hamziyya agreed except they placed children of disbelievers in Hell. The Shu'aybiyya were like Maymuniyya except on qadar. The Hazimiyya hesitated on disavowing 'Ali. The Khalafiyya attributed all qadar to Allah and placed polytheist children in Hell. The Atrafiyya excused ignorance on the peripheries.

الحمزية
الشعيبية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All 'Ajarda sub-sects agreed on the doctrine of qadar (attributing actions to human power).
Correction: The Shu'aybiyya differed on qadar: they did not hold the same view as the Maymuniyya and others. The Khalafiyya also attributed qadar to Allah, not humans.

A) Paradise
B) Hell
C) They are not judged
D) Limbo

Key Takeaway
The 'Ajarda sub-sects differed on qadar, the fate of polytheist children, and other doctrines, showing internal diversity within the sect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Maymuniyya denied Sura Yusuf because they thought it contained a story of lewdness. Is there any part of the Quran that you find difficult to accept or that you are tempted to reinterpret because it conflicts with your preferences? What does this tell you about the condition of your heart towards Allah's revelation?
?
The 'Ajarda sub-sects held strong views about the fate of children of disbelievers. Do you ever find yourself making judgments about people's eternal destiny based on your own assumptions rather than relying on clear texts? How can you cultivate humility in matters where Allah has not given you certainty?
?
The Atrafiyya excused people on the peripheries for their ignorance of the Shari'a. Are there areas of your own religious practice where you remain deliberately ignorant or accept shortcuts because 'you didn't know'? Will you commit today to seeking knowledge about one aspect of your faith that you have neglected?

The Four Early Kharijite Sub-Sects
Lists the four Kharijite sub-sects after the Ibadiyya with their distinctive beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinctive beliefs of the four early Kharijite sub-sects that split from the Ibadiyya.

Core Idea
The Kharijites fragmented into four sub-sects with divergent views on faith, predestination, and future prophethood.

After the initial Kharijite split, the Ibadiyya still produced sub-sects. This passage enumerates four that differed on key theological issues such as the nature of faith, the role of miracles, predestination, and the possibility of future prophethood. Understanding these sects clarifies the breadth of Kharijite thought and its internal disagreements.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall structure.
Notice the editorial parentheses in the Arabic – they are part of the scholarly formatting.
2
Identify the four sub-sects and their names
The passage lists four sects: al-Ḥafṣiyya, al-Yazīdiyya, al-Ḥārithiyya, and a fourth unnamed group. Note the founder or key figure associated with each.
3
For each sect, note the specific belief that distinguishes them
Each sect added or opposed a specific doctrine to the Ibadiyya: for al-Ḥafṣiyya it is the intermediate state of knowledge of God; for al-Yazīdiyya it is the future prophet and the view that all sins are polytheism; for al-Ḥārithiyya it is predestination and capacity; for the fourth, it is the definition of obedience.
Pay attention to the phrasing: 'zādū ʿalā al-ibāḍiyya' or 'khālafū al-ibāḍiyya'.
4
Reflect on the significance of these divergent views
Consider why these differences matter in Islamic theology. They show that early Kharijites were not monolithic but debated issues like the relationship between faith and works, the nature of prophethood, and human free will.
This connects to the misconception that all Kharijites held identical views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
توقفوا ( في النفاق أهو شرك ) أم لا، (و) في ( جواز بعثة رسول بلا دليل) ومعجزة ) وتكليف أتباعه ) فيما يوحى إليه أي ترددوا أن ذلك جائز أو لا ) وكفروا علياً وأكثر ، الصحابة وافترقوا) فرقا أربعا . ( الأولى الحفصية : هو أبو حفص بن أبي المقدام زادوا على الأباضية ( أن بين الإيمان والشرك معرفة الله تعالى ) فإنها خصلة متوسطة بينهما ( فمن عرف الله وكفر بما سواه من رسول أو جنة أو نار ) أو بارتكاب كبيرة فكافر لا مشرك . ( الثانية : اليزيدية : أصحاب يزيد بن أنيسة زادوا على الأباضية أن ( قالوا سيبعث نبي من العجم بكتاب يكتب في السماء ويترك عليه جملة واحدة ) ويترك شريعة محمد إلى ملة الصابئة ) المذكورة في القرآن (و) قالوا : ( أصحاب الحدود مشركون وكل ذنب شرك ) كبيرة كانت أو صغيرة ( الثالثة : الحارثية أصحاب أبي الحارث الأباضي. خالفوا الأباضية في القدر أي كون أفعال العباد مخلوقة لله تعالى ( وفي ) كون ( الاستطاعة قبل الفعل . الرابعة : القائلون بطاعة لا يراد بها الله ) أي زعموا أن العبد إذا أتى بما أمر به ولم يقصد الله كان ذلك طاعة .
They hesitated (regarding hypocrisy: is it polytheism) or not, and (regarding) the permissibility of sending a messenger without a miracle, and the obligation of his followers to believe in what is revealed to him, meaning they doubted whether that is permissible or not, and they declared 'Ali and most of the Companions as disbelievers, and they split into four sects. (First: al-Ḥafṣiyya: he is Abū Ḥafṣ ibn Abī al-Miqdām. They added to the Ibāḍiyya that between faith and polytheism is knowledge of God, for it is an intermediate trait between them. So whoever knows God and disbelieves in anything other than Him, whether a messenger or Paradise or Hell, or by committing a major sin, is a disbeliever, not a polytheist. (Second: al-Yazīdiyya: followers of Yazīd ibn Anīsa. They added to the Ibāḍiyya that they said a prophet will be sent from the non-Arabs with a book written in the sky and left as a single whole, and he will abandon the law of Muḥammad for the religion of the Ṣābi'ūn mentioned in the Qur'an. And they said: the people of the prescribed punishments are polytheists, and every sin is polytheism, whether major or minor. (Third: al-Ḥārithiyya: followers of Abū al-Ḥārith al-Ibāḍī. They opposed the Ibāḍiyya regarding predestination, i.e., that the actions of servants are created by God, and regarding the capacity being before the act. (Fourth: those who say obedience not intended for God, i.e., they claimed that if a servant does what he is commanded without intending God, that is obedience.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the first four sub-sects that emerged from the original Kharijite split after the Ibāḍiyya. The author begins by noting the issues that caused the split: hesitation over whether hypocrisy is polytheism, whether a messenger can be sent without a miracle, and whether followers must accept revelations without evidence. They declared 'Ali and most Companions disbelievers and split into four groups. The first, al-Ḥafṣiyya, added that knowledge of God is an intermediate state between faith and polytheism, so whoever knows God but disbelieves in anything else is a disbeliever but not a polytheist. The second, al-Yazīdiyya, claimed a future prophet from the non-Arabs would bring a book written in heaven and abrogate Muḥammad's law for the religion of the Ṣābi'ūn; they also held that all sins are polytheism. The third, al-Ḥārithiyya, opposed the Ibāḍiyya on predestination (that God creates actions) and that capacity exists before the act. The fourth held that obedience performed without intending God is still obedience. Each sect is defined by its distinctive addition or opposition to the Ibāḍiyya.

الحفصية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Kharijites held identical views on faith and practice.
Correction: This passage shows internal diversity: on faith (al-Hafsiyya's intermediate state), on sin (al-Yazidiyya's view of all sins as polytheism), on predestination (al-Harithiyya), and on intention (fourth group). The Kharijites were not monolithic.

Checkpoint
Which of the four sub-sects taught that there is an intermediate state between faith and polytheism?
A) al-Yazīdiyya
B) al-Ḥafṣiyya

Key Takeaway
The early Kharijites fragmented into four sub-sects with distinct theological positions on faith, sin, predestination, and the definition of obedience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Hafsiyya said that knowing God but disbelieving in anything else makes you a disbeliever, not a polytheist. When you sin, do you treat that sin as a lesser offense than shirk, or do you excuse yourself by saying 'at least I know God'? Could that excuse be a veil hiding the reality of your disobedience?
?
The Yazidiyya believed every sin — even a small one — is polytheism. Think about a sin you committed recently, one you considered minor. If you truly believed it was shirk, would you still have done it? How would your attitude toward that sin change if you saw it as a form of associating partners with Allah?
?
The fourth sect said obedience without intention to please God is still obedience. Reflect on a good deed you performed recently: was your motive purely for Allah, or was there a trace of showing off or habit? Are you comfortable with the idea that your deeds might be accepted even if you didn't mean them for Him? What does that comfort — or discomfort — reveal about your heart?

The 'Ajārida Parent and First Three Sub-Sects
Introduces the 'Ajārida parent sect and enumerates the first three sub-sects (Maymūniyya, Hamziyya, Shu'aybiyya) with their key doctrines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the foundational doctrines of the 'Ajārida sect and how the first three sub-sects diverged on issues of predestination and the fate of children.

Core Idea
The 'Ajārida split began with disagreements over predestination and children's afterlife.

The 'Ajārida are the last of the seven Kharijite groups, emerging from the Najdāt. Their distinctive doctrine was the obligation to disavow children until they reach puberty and embrace Islam. From this parent sect branched ten sub-sects, each with its own variations. This lesson introduces the parent sect and the first three sub-sects: al-Maymūniyya, al-Ḥamziyya, and al-Shu'aybiyya.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the parent sect
Note the definition of 'Ajārida and their core doctrine on children.
2
Identify the first sub-sect: al-Maymūniyya
See how they affirmed predestination in a Qadari sense, and held children of disbelievers in Paradise.
Also note their denial of Sūrat Yūsuf.
3
Compare the second and third sub-sects
Al-Ḥamziyya agreed except they put children in Hell. Al-Shu'aybiyya agreed except on predestination.
Observe how small changes create new sects.

al-'Ajārida: he is 'Abd al-Raḥmān ibn 'Ajrad, and they are the last of the seven (groups) of the Kharijite sects. They added to al-Najdāt, after agreeing with them in their doctrine, the obligation of disavowal of the child, i.e., one must disavow him until he claims Islam after reaching puberty, and it is obligatory to call him to it, i.e., to Islam, when he reaches puberty. And the children of the polytheists are in the Fire. And they are ten sects: First: al-Maymūniyya: he is Maymūn ibn 'Imrān. They affirmed predestination, i.e., attributing actions to the capacity of servants, and that capacity is before the act, and that God wills good not evil and does not will sins, as is the doctrine of the Mu'tazila. They said: the children of disbelievers are in Paradise, and it is related from them permitting marriage of daughters to sons and to daughters and to children of brothers and sisters, i.e., they permitted marriage of granddaughters and great-granddaughters and children of siblings. And they denied Sūrat Yūsuf, for they claimed it is a story of stories and it is not permissible for a story of immorality to be Qur'an. (Second: from the sects of al-'Ajārida) al-Ḥamziyya: he is Ḥamza ibn Adrak. They agreed with them, i.e., al-Maymūniyya, in the innovations they held, except that they said the children of disbelievers are in the Fire. (Third) among them: al-Shu'aybiyya: he is Shu'ayb ibn Muḥammad, and they are like al-Maymūniyya in their innovations except regarding predestination. (Fourth: al-Ḥāzimiyya: he is Ḥāzim ibn 'Āṣim. They agreed with al-Shu'aybiyya, and it is narrated from them that they suspend judgment concerning 'Alī and do not declare disavowal of him explicitly as they declare disavowal of others. (Fifth: al-Khalafiyya: followers of Khalaf al-Khārijī, and they are the Kharijites of Kirmān and Makrān. They attributed predestination, its good and evil, to God, and ruled that the children of polytheists are in the Fire without work or polytheism. (Sixth: al-Aṭrāfiyya: they follow the doctrine of Ḥamza, and their leader is a man from Sijistān called Ghālib, except that they excused the people of the frontiers for what they did not know of the law if they did what they knew to be necessary by reason. And they agreed with the Ahl al-Sunna in their principles and in negating predestination, i.e., attributing actions to the capacity of the servant, and in some copies 'negating power', i.e., negating effective power from servants. (Seventh: al-Ma'lūmiyya: they are like al-Ḥāzimiyya except that the believer according to them is one who knows God by all His names and attributes, and whoever does not know Him thus is ignorant, not a believer, and the action of the servant is created by God. (Eighth: al-Majhūliyya: their doctrine is like the doctrine of al-Ḥāzimiyya also, except that they said: knowledge of Him is sufficient by some of His names, so whoever knows Him thus is a knower of Him, a believer, and the action of the servant is created by God. (Ninth: al-Ṣaltiyya: he is 'Uthmān ibn Abī al-Ṣalt, and it is said ibn al-Ṣāmit. They are like al-'Ajārida, but they said: whoever becomes Muslim and seeks our protection, we befriend him and disavow his children until they reach puberty and are called to Islam and accept. And it is related from some of them that children, whether of Muslims or polytheists, have no friendship nor enmity until they reach puberty and are called to Islam and accept or reject. (Tenth: from the sects of al-'Ajārida) al-Tha'āliba: he is Tha'lab ibn 'Āmir. They affirmed friendship with children, young or old, until denial of the truth appears from them after puberty. And it is also transmitted from them that children have no ruling of friendship or enmity until they mature. And they hold taking zakāt from slaves if they become wealthy and giving it to them if they become poor.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage classifies the 'Ajārida, a major Kharijite branch that split from al-Najdāt, and enumerates its ten sub-sects. The author first defines the parent sect: they are the last of the seven Kharijite groups, and they added to al-Najdāt the obligation of disavowing children until they reach puberty and embrace Islam, and they held that polytheists' children are in Hell. Then he lists ten sub-sects: (1) al-Maymūniyya affirmed predestination and capacity before the act, denied that God wills evil, held children of disbelievers in Paradise, permitted certain marriages, and denied Sūrat Yūsuf. (2) al-Ḥamziyya agreed except they put children of disbelievers in Hell. (3) al-Shu'aybiyya agreed with al-Maymūniyya except on predestination. (4) al-Ḥāzimiyya agreed with al-Shu'aybiyya but suspended judgment on 'Alī. (5) al-Khalafiyya attributed predestination entirely to God and held children of polytheists in Hell. (6) al-Aṭrāfiyya followed Ḥamza but excused ignorance in frontier regions and agreed with Ahl al-Sunna on principles and denying human power. (7) al-Ma'lūmiyya required knowledge of all God's names for faith, and held actions created. (8) al-Majhūliyya required knowledge of only some names. (9) al-Ṣaltiyya disavowed children until they accept Islam, with some saying children have no status until maturity. (10) al-Tha'āliba affirmed friendship with children until they reject truth, and had rules on zakāt for slaves. Each sub-sect is defined by its specific addition or variation on these core issues.

Key Terms

الميمونية
الحمزية
الشعيبية
القدر
الاستطاعة
أطفال الكفار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All 'Ajārida sub-sects agreed on the fate of children.
Correction: The first three sub-sects already show disagreement: al-Maymūniyya said children of disbelievers are in Paradise, al-Ḥamziyya said they are in Hell, and al-Shu'aybiyya may have a different view.

Checkpoint
Which sub-sect of the 'Ajārida held that the children of disbelievers are in Paradise?
A) al-Ḥamziyya
B) al-Maymūniyya
C) al-Khalafiyya
D) al-Ṣaltiyya

Key Takeaway
The first three sub-sects of the 'Ajārida diverged mainly on predestination and the fate of children, illustrating how minor differences create new sects.

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate

Sub-Sects 4–6: Hāzimiyya, Khalafiyya, and Aṭrāfiyya
Enumerates the fourth to sixth sub-sects of the 'Ajārida (Hāzimiyya, Khalafiyya, Aṭrāfiyya) with their distinctive doctrines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinctive doctrines of the fourth to sixth 'Ajārida sub-sects, especially regarding judgment on 'Ali, predestination, and excuse for ignorance.

Core Idea
The 'Ajārida branches further diverge on 'Ali, predestination extremes, and frontier excuse.

After the first three sub-sects focused on children and predestination, the next three introduce new issues: al-Ḥāzimiyya suspends judgment on 'Ali, al-Khalafiyya attributes all predestination to God, and al-Aṭrāfiyya excuses ignorance of the law on the frontiers. This lesson examines these three sub-sects in detail.

Guided Path
1
Read about al-Ḥāzimiyya
Note their agreement with al-Shu'aybiyya and their unique position on 'Ali: they suspend judgment and do not explicitly disavow him.
2
Read about al-Khalafiyya
They attributed all predestination (good and evil) to God and held children of polytheists in Hell without work or polytheism.
This is a different predestination stance.
3
Read about al-Aṭrāfiyya
They followed Ḥamza's doctrine but excused people on the frontiers for ignorance of the law, and agreed with Ahl al-Sunna in negating predestination (attributing actions to the servant).
Note the textual variant 'negating power'.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(السابعة : المعلومية هم كالحازمية إلا أن المؤمن عندهم من عرف الله بجميع أسمائه وصفاته، ومن لم يعرفه كذلك فهو جاهل لا مؤمن ( وفعل العبد مخلوق لله تعالى . الثامنة : المجهولية : مذهبهم كمذهب الحازمية أيضاً إلا أنهم ( قالوا : يكفي معرفته تعالى ببعض أسمائه فمن علمه كذلك فهو عارف به مؤمن وفعل العبد مخلوق لله تعالى . al-'Ajārida: he is 'Abd al-Raḥmān ibn 'Ajrad, and they are the last of the seven (groups) of the Kharijite sects. They added to al-Najdāt, after agreeing with them in their doctrine, the obligation of disavowal of the child, i.e., one must disavow him until he claims Islam after reaching puberty, and it is obligatory to call him to it, i.e., to Islam, when he reaches puberty. Which sub-sect suspended judgment on 'Alī and did not explicitly disavow him?

Key Takeaway
The fourth to sixth sub-sects introduce new themes: suspension of judgment on 'Alī, total predestination, and excusing legal ignorance on frontiers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter someone you disagree with on religious matters, do you immediately disavow them, or do you exercise suspension of judgment as the Hāzimiyya did regarding 'Alī? What would it cost you to hold back a verdict on their faith?
?
The Khalafiyya believed children of polytheists are condemned without having done anything. Does this trouble your sense of justice? How do you reconcile God's mercy with this doctrine, and how does it affect the way you view non-Muslim families?
?
The Aṭrāfiyya excused ignorance of the law for frontier people. Are there areas of your own religious practice where you plead ignorance rather than seeking knowledge? What 'frontier' in your life have you been using as an excuse to remain complacent?

Sub-Sects 7–8: Ma'lūmiyya and Majhūliyya on Knowledge of God
Enumerates the seventh and eighth 'Ajārida sub-sects (Ma'lūmiyya, Majhūliyya) focusing on knowledge of God's names and action creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the contrasting views of the seventh and eighth 'Ajārida sub-sects on the extent of knowledge required for faith.

Core Idea
Faith hinges on knowing all or some of God's names, according to these two sub-sects.

The seventh and eighth sub-sects of the 'Ajārida, al-Ma'lūmiyya and al-Majhūliyya, focus on the knowledge of God's names and attributes. Al-Ma'lūmiyya requires knowledge of all names and attributes for one to be considered a believer, while al-Majhūliyya deems knowledge of only some names sufficient. Both hold that actions are created by God.

Guided Path
1
Read about al-Ma'lūmiyya
Note that they require full knowledge of God's names for faith, otherwise one is ignorant, not a believer. Also they believe actions are created.
2
Read about al-Majhūliyya
They require only partial knowledge; knowing some names suffices for faith. They also believe actions are created by God.
Contrast with al-Ma'lūmiyya.

Source Text

And the children of the polytheists are in the Fire. And they are ten sects: First: al-Maymūniyya: he is Maymūn ibn 'Imrān. They affirmed predestination, i.e., attributing actions to the capacity of servants, and that capacity is before the act, and that God wills good not evil and does not will sins, as is the doctrine of the Mu'tazila. They said: the children of disbelievers are in Paradise, and it is related from them permitting marriage of daughters to sons and to daughters and to children of brothers and sisters, i.e., they permitted marriage of granddaughters and great-granddaughters and children of siblings. And they denied Sūrat Yūsuf, for they claimed it is a story of stories and it is not permissible for a story of immorality to be Qur'an. (Second: from the sects of al-'Ajārida) al-Ḥamziyya: he is Ḥamza ibn Adrak. They agreed with them, i.e., al-Maymūniyya, in the innovations they held, except that they said the children of disbelievers are in the Fire. (Third) among them: al-Shu'aybiyya: he is Shu'ayb ibn Muḥammad, and they are like al-Maymūniyya in their innovations except regarding predestination. (Fourth: al-Ḥāzimiyya: he is Ḥāzim ibn 'Āṣim. They agreed with al-Shu'aybiyya, and it is narrated from them that they suspend judgment concerning 'Alī and do not declare disavowal of him explicitly as they declare disavowal of others. (Fifth: al-Khalafiyya: followers of Khalaf al-Khārijī, and they are the Kharijites of Kirmān and Makrān. They attributed predestination, its good and evil, to God, and ruled that the children of polytheists are in the Fire without work or polytheism. (Sixth: al-Aṭrāfiyya: they follow the doctrine of Ḥamza, and their leader is a man from Sijistān called Ghālib, except that they excused the people of the frontiers for what they did not know of the law if they did what they knew to be necessary by reason. And they agreed with the Ahl al-Sunna in their principles and in negating predestination, i.e., attributing actions to the capacity of the servant, and in some copies 'negating power', i.e., negating effective power from servants. (Seventh: al-Ma'lūmiyya: they are like al-Ḥāzimiyya except that the believer according to them is one who knows God by all His names and attributes, and whoever does not know Him thus is ignorant, not a believer, and the action of the servant is created by God. (Eighth: al-Majhūliyya: their doctrine is like the doctrine of al-Ḥāzimiyya also, except that they said: knowledge of Him is sufficient by some of His names, so whoever knows Him thus is a knower of Him, a believer, and the action of the servant is created by God. (Ninth: al-Ṣaltiyya: he is 'Uthmān ibn Abī al-Ṣalt, and it is said ibn al-Ṣāmit. They are like al-'Ajārida, but they said: whoever becomes Muslim and seeks our protection, we befriend him and disavow his children until they reach puberty and are called to Islam and accept. And it is related from some of them that children, whether of Muslims or polytheists, have no friendship nor enmity until they reach puberty and are called to Islam and accept or reject. (Tenth: from the sects of al-'Ajārida) al-Tha'āliba: he is Tha'lab ibn 'Āmir. They affirmed friendship with children, young or old, until denial of the truth appears from them after puberty. And it is also transmitted from them that children have no ruling of friendship or enmity until they mature. And they hold taking zakāt from slaves if they become wealthy and giving it to them if they become poor.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage classifies the 'Ajārida, a major Kharijite branch that split from al-Najdāt, and enumerates its ten sub-sects. The author first defines the parent sect: they are the last of the seven Kharijite groups, and they added to al-Najdāt the obligation of disavowing children until they reach puberty and embrace Islam, and they held that polytheists' children are in Hell. Then he lists ten sub-sects: (1) al-Maymūniyya affirmed predestination and capacity before the act, denied that God wills evil, held children of disbelievers in Paradise, permitted certain marriages, and denied Sūrat Yūsuf. (2) al-Ḥamziyya agreed except they put children of disbelievers in Hell. (3) al-Shu'aybiyya agreed with al-Maymūniyya except on predestination. (4) al-Ḥāzimiyya agreed with al-Shu'aybiyya but suspended judgment on 'Alī. (5) al-Khalafiyya attributed predestination entirely to God and held children of polytheists in Hell. (6) al-Aṭrāfiyya followed Ḥamza but excused ignorance in frontier regions and agreed with Ahl al-Sunna on principles and denying human power. (7) al-Ma'lūmiyya required knowledge of all God's names for faith, and held actions created. (8) al-Majhūliyya required knowledge of only some names. (9) al-Ṣaltiyya disavowed children until they accept Islam, with some saying children have no status until maturity. (10) al-Tha'āliba affirmed friendship with children until they reject truth, and had rules on zakāt for slaves. Each sub-sect is defined by its specific addition or variation on these core issues.

Key Terms
المعلومية
المجهولية
أسماء الله
فعل العبد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All 'Ajārida sub-sects believe the same about faith and knowledge.
Correction: Al-Ma'lūmiyya and al-Majhūliyya have opposite requirements: one demands full knowledge, the other partial.

Checkpoint
What distinguishes al-Ma'lūmiyya from al-Majhūliyya?
A) Al-Ma'lūmiyya says actions are not created by God
B) Al-Majhūliyya requires knowledge of all names
C) Al-Ma'lūmiyya requires knowledge of all names for faith
D) They are identical

Key Takeaway
Al-Ma'lūmiyya and al-Majhūliyya illustrate the diversity within the 'Ajārida on the criterion of faith regarding divine knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Ma'lūmiyya says that if you do not know God by all His names and attributes, you are not a believer. Honestly examine yourself: do you know even the most common names of God deeply? What steps will you take to grow in this knowledge?
?
Al-Majhūliyya takes a more lenient view: knowledge of some names is sufficient. But are you content with superficial recognition of a few names, or do you long to know God more intimately through His attributes? What would change in your life if you truly knew Him by His names?
?
Both sects agree that your every action is created by God, not by you. How does that truth affect your view of your own achievements and failures? Will you let it drive you to humility and reliance on God, or to passivity? What will you do differently today because of this?

Sub-Sects 9–10: Ṣaltiyya and Tha'āliba on Children and Zakāt
Enumerates the ninth and tenth 'Ajārida sub-sects (Ṣaltiyya, Tha'āliba) with doctrines on children and zakāt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the positions of the final two 'Ajārida sub-sects on the status of children and the rules of zakāt for slaves.

Core Idea
The last two sub-sects differ on whether children have legal status before maturity and on zakāt obligations for slaves.

The ninth and tenth sub-sects, al-Ṣaltiyya and al-Tha'āliba, focus on the status of children (whether they can be befriended or disavowed before puberty) and on the payment of zakāt by slaves. These issues show the ongoing Kharijite concern with communal boundaries and ritual obligations.

Guided Path
1
Read about al-Ṣaltiyya
They disavow children until they accept Islam at puberty, with some saying children have no friendship/enmity until maturity.
2
Read about al-Tha'āliba
They befriend children until they reject truth after puberty, but also report that children have no ruling. They also hold that zakāt is taken from wealthy slaves and given to poor slaves.
Note the variation within the sub-sect.

Checkpoint
What unique practice is attributed to al-Tha'āliba?
A) Denying Sūrat Yūsuf
B) Taking zakāt from wealthy slaves and giving it to poor slaves
C) Suspending judgment on 'Alī
D) Excusing ignorance on frontiers

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you condition your acceptance of others—especially the young—on their religious performance, or do you extend friendship from the start as the Tha'āliba did? How would your community change if you adopted their approach?
?
The Ṣaltiyya disavowed children until they accepted Islam. In your own life, are you quick to sever ties with someone who has not yet openly embraced faith? What would it mean to wait patiently as they mature?
?
The Tha'āliba gave zakāt to poor slaves. Who are the 'slaves' or marginalized in your society that you overlook in your charity? How can you proactively seek out those in need, even if they are not within your usual circle?

Sects and Disagreements
beginner

Four Sub-Sects of al-Tha'āliba and Total Kharijite Count
Lists four sub-sects of al-Tha'āliba and sums total Kharijite groups to twenty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinctive beliefs of four sub-sects branching from al-Tha'āliba (al-Akhunsiyya, al-Ma'bidiyya, al-Shaybāniyya, al-Mukramiyya) and how the total number of Kharijite groups reaches twenty, along with a methodological note on counting.

Core Idea
The Kharijite sects multiplied into twenty, but counting is debated.

In this passage, the author completes his survey of Kharijite divisions by detailing four sub-sects that emerged from the Tha'āliba branch. Each sub-sect held distinct positions on issues like judging believers, marriage, predestination, and the status of major sinners. He then sums the previous groups to arrive at a total of twenty, while noting a scholarly objection about counting the parent group itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the four sub-sects
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its translation. Locate the names of the four sub-sects: al-Akhunsiyya, al-Ma'bidiyya, al-Shaybāniyya, and al-Mukramiyya.
These are all branches of al-Tha'āliba.
2
Note the distinctive doctrine of each sub-sect
For each sub-sect, write down one key belief that sets it apart. For example, al-Akhunsiyya suspended judgment on those in the abode of dissimulation; al-Ma'bidiyya opposed them on marriage; al-Shaybāniyya affirmed predestination; al-Mukramiyya declared major sinners disbelievers due to ignorance of God.
Some beliefs are shared with parent groups.
3
Understand the total count and methodological issue
The author adds the four sub-sects to previous groups to reach twenty. Notice his remark that there is discussion because the divided category (al-Tha'āliba itself) should not be counted among its divisions, so the actual count may be less.
This shows careful attention to classification principles.
4
Reflect on the significance of these divisions
Consider why theologians recorded such detailed sectarian splits. These distinctions mattered for determining who is considered a believer or disbeliever, and for understanding the diversity within early Islamic thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( وتفرقوا ) أي الثعالبة أربع فرق : الأولى : الأخنسية : أصحاب أخنس بن قيس هم كالثعالبة إلا أنهم ) امتازوا عنهم بأن ( توقفوا فيمن هو في دار (التقية من أهل القبلة فلم يحكموا عليه بإيمان ولا كفر ( إِلا ممن علم حاله ) من إيمانه أو كفره ( وحرموا الاغتيال بالقتل لمخالفيهم ( والسرقة) من أموالهم ( ونقل عنهم ) أنه يجوز (تزويج المسلمات من مشركي قومهم ( الثانية المعبدية : هو معبد بن عبد الرحمن خالفوهم) أي الأخنسية (في التزويج ) أي تزويج المسلمات ) من المشركين وخالفوا الثعالبة في زكاة العبيد ) أي أخذها منهم ودفعها إليهم . ( الثالثة : الشيبانية: هو شيبان بن سلمة، قالوا بالجبر ونفي القدرة الحادثة الرابعة : المكرمية: هو مكرم بن العجلي، قالوا : تارك الصلاة (كافر لا لترك الصلاة بل ( لجهله بالله ) فإن من علم أنه مطلع على سره وعلنه ومجازيه على طاعته ومعصيته لا يتصور منه الإقدام على ترك الصلاة، ( وكذا كل كبيرة ) فإن مرتكبها كافر لجهله بالله لما ذكرناه ( وموالاة الله ومعاداته لعباده باعتباره العاقبة وما هم صائرون إليه عند موافاة الموت إلا باعتبار أعمالهم التي هم فيها، إذ هي غير موثوق بدوامها ( وكذا نحن فمن وصل إلى حالة الموت فإن كان مؤمناً في تلك الحالة واليناه وإن كان كافراً عاديناه، ( فإذن فرق الخوارج عشر فرق نضمها إلى الست السابقة تصير ست عشرة وتتشعب من الثعالبة والأباضية أربع فرق أخرى فالمجموع عشرون، وفيه بحث لأن المقسم لا يعد من أقسامه فلا تعتبر
And they split, i.e., al-Tha'āliba, into four sects: First: al-Akhunsiyya: followers of Ukhnus ibn Qays. They are like al-Tha'āliba except that they distinguished themselves by suspending judgment concerning one who is in the abode of dissimulation among the people of the qibla, so they do not judge him as believer or disbeliever except one whose state he knows from his faith or disbelief. And they prohibited assassination by killing of their opponents and theft from their wealth. And it is transmitted from them that it is permissible to marry Muslim women to polytheists of their people. (Second: al-Ma'bidiyya: he is Ma'bad ibn 'Abd al-Raḥmān. They opposed them, i.e., al-Akhunsiyya, regarding marriage, i.e., marriage of Muslim women to polytheists, and opposed al-Tha'āliba regarding zakāt of slaves, i.e., taking it from them and giving it to them. (Third: al-Shaybāniyya: he is Shaybān ibn Salama. They affirmed predestination (jabr) and negated originated power. (Fourth: al-Mukramiyya: he is Mukram ibn al-'Ajalī. They said: the one who abandons prayer is a disbeliever, not for abandoning prayer, but for his ignorance of God. For whoever knows that He is aware of his secret and public and will reward him for his obedience and punish him for his disobedience, it is not conceivable that he would proceed to abandon prayer. And likewise every major sin, for its committer is a disbeliever due to his ignorance of God for what we mentioned. And the friendship of God and enmity towards His servants are considered according to the end and what they will become at the time of death, not according to their present deeds, for they are not reliable for their continuance. And likewise we: so whoever reaches the state of death, if he is a believer in that state we befriend him, and if he is a disbeliever we declare enmity towards him. (Therefore, the Kharijite sects are ten sects; we add them to the previous six, so they become sixteen, and from al-Tha'āliba and al-Ibāḍiyya branch four other sects, so the total is twenty. But there is discussion because the divided category is not counted among its divisions, so it is not considered.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage concludes the survey of Kharijite sects by listing four additional sub-sects that branched from al-Tha'āliba and then giving a total count. The author begins by stating that al-Tha'āliba themselves split into four. (1) al-Akhunsiyya suspended judgment on those in the abode of dissimulation, only determining faith or disbelief based on known state; they prohibited killing opponents and theft from them, but permitted marriage of Muslim women to polytheists. (2) al-Ma'bidiyya opposed al-Akhunsiyya on that marriage and opposed al-Tha'āliba on zakāt of slaves. (3) al-Shaybāniyya affirmed predestination (jabr) and denied originated power. (4) al-Mukramiyya held that abandoning prayer and other major sins constitute disbelief due to ignorance of God, because one who truly knows God would not commit such acts. They also held that God's friendship and enmity are based on one's state at death, not on present deeds. Finally, the author summarizes: the Kharijite sects proper are ten; adding to the previous six makes sixteen, and the branches from al-Tha'āliba and al-Ibāḍiyya add four more, totaling twenty. However, he notes a scholarly discussion: the main category (e.g., al-Tha'āliba itself) should not be counted among its own divisions, so the count is disputed.

الجبر
القدرة الحادثة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the total count of twenty Kharijite groups is definitive and undisputed.
Correction: The author explicitly notes a methodological issue: the divided category (e.g., al-Tha'āliba) is not counted among its own divisions, so the actual number of sub-sects is less than twenty.

Checkpoint
According to the author, how many total Kharijite groups are listed after adding the four branches from al-Tha'āliba and al-Ibāḍiyya?
A) ten
B) sixteen
C) twenty
D) twenty-four

Key Takeaway
The Kharijites fragmented into at least twenty sub-sects, but the precise count depends on whether the parent group is included among its own divisions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Mukramiyya believed that one who truly knows God would never abandon prayer. Look at your own prayer: when you miss a prayer, what does that reveal about your current knowledge of God? Are you willing to take one concrete step today to deepen that knowledge so your actions align?
?
The Kharijites splintered over differences like marriage with polytheists and zakāt of slaves. Think of a disagreement you have with a fellow Muslim: is it over a core belief or a secondary issue? How might focusing on the final state at death change how you interact with that person?
?
Al-Akhunsiyya suspended judgment on people in taqiyya, recognizing they could not know another's true state. When have you judged someone's faith based on their outward actions? What if you left that judgment to God and instead examined your own heart?

al-Ma'lumiyya and al-Majhuliyya: Defining Faith by Knowledge of Allah
Enumeration of two related Khawarij sub-sects with doctrinal definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ma'lumiyya and al-Majhuliyya differed in defining faith based on the extent of knowledge of Allah's names and attributes.

Core Idea
Two sects, one threshold: faith requires knowledge – but how much?

Among the Khawarij, even those sharing a common root can diverge on a single point. Al-Ma'lumiyya and al-Majhuliyya both follow the general line of al-Hazimiyya, but they disagree on the quantity of divine knowledge needed for true faith. This lesson examines that subtle but significant difference.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for both sects
Read the Arabic and translation describing al-Ma'lumiyya and al-Majhuliyya. Notice the key difference: one requires all names and attributes, the other accepts some.
2
Compare the two definitions of faith
For al-Ma'lumiyya, ignoring even one attribute makes one ignorant, not a believer. For al-Majhuliyya, partial knowledge suffices. Reflect on how this affects who is considered a believer.
Both still reject those who do not have the required knowledge.
3
Consider the shared premise
Both sects agree that human acts are created by Allah, a doctrine they hold in common with other Khawarij groups. This shows their theological continuity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابعة : المعلومية هم كالحازمية إلا أن المؤمن عندهم من عرف الله بجميع أسمائه وصفاته، ومن لم يعرفه كذلك فهو جاهل لا مؤمن، وفعل العبد مخلوق لله تعالى . الثامنة : المجهولية : مذهبهم كمذهب الحازمية أيضاً إلا أنهم قالوا : يكفي معرفته تعالى ببعض أسمائه فمن علمه كذلك فهو عارف به مؤمن، وفعل العبد مخلوق لله تعالى . التاسعة : الصلتية : هو عثمان بن أبي الصلت وقيل: بن الصامت هم كالعجاردة، لكن قالوا من أسلم واستجار بنا توليناه وبرئنا من أطفاله حتى يبلغوا فيدعوا إلى الإسلام فيقبلوا، وروي عن بعضهم أن الأطفال سواء كانوا للمسلمين أو المشركين لا ولاية لهم ولا عداوة حتى يبلغوا فيدعوا إلى الإسلام ويقبلوا أو ينكروا . العاشرة : من فرق العجاردة الثعالبة : هو ثعلب بن عامر قالوا بولاية الأطفال صغاراً كانوا أو كباراً حتى يظهر منهم إنكار الحق بعد البلوغ، وقد نقل عنهم أيضاً أن الأطفال لا حكم لهم من ولاية أو عداوة إلى أن يدركوا، ويرون أخذ الزكاة من العبيد إذا استغنوا وإعطاءها لهم إذا افتقروا . وتفرقوا أي الثعالبة أربع فرق : الأولى : الأخنسية : أصحاب أخنس بن قيس هم كالثعالبة إلا أنهم امتازوا عنهم بأن توقفوا فيمن هو في دار التقية من أهل القبلة فلم يحكموا عليه بإيمان ولا كفر إلا ممن علم حاله من إيمانه أو كفره، وحرموا الاغتيال بالقتل لمخالفيهم والسرقة من أموالهم، ونقل عنهم أنه يجوز تزويج المسلمات من مشركي قومهم . الثانية المعبدية : هو معبد بن عبد الرحمن خالفوهم أي الأخنسية في التزويج أي تزويج المسلمات من المشركين وخالفوا الثعالبة في زكاة العبيد أي أخذها منهم ودفعها إليهم . الثالثة : الشيبانية: هو شيبان بن سلمة، قالوا بالجبر ونفي القدرة الحادثة . الرابعة : المكرمية: هو مكرم بن العجلي، قالوا : تارك الصلاة كافر لا لترك الصلاة بل لجهله بالله، فإن من علم أنه مطلع على سره وعلنه ومجازيه على طاعته ومعصيته لا يتصور منه الإقدام على ترك الصلاة، وكذا كل كبيرة فإن مرتكبها كافر لجهله بالله لما ذكرناه، وموالاة الله ومعاداته لعباده باعتباره العاقبة وما هم صائرون إليه عند موافاة الموت لا باعتبار أعمالهم التي هم فيها، إذ هي غير موثوق بدوامها، وكذا نحن فمن وصل إلى حالة الموت فإن كان مؤمناً في تلك الحالة واليناه وإن كان كافراً عاديناه.
The seventh: al-Ma'lumiyya: they are like al-Hazimiyya except that the believer according to them is the one who knows Allah with all His names and attributes, and whoever does not know Him thus is ignorant, not a believer, and the act of the slave is created by Allah Almighty. The eighth: al-Majhuliyya: their doctrine is like the doctrine of al-Hazimiyya also except that they said: knowledge of Him Almighty with some of His names suffices; so whoever knows Him thus is a knower of Him, a believer, and the act of the slave is created by Allah Almighty. The ninth: al-Saltiyya: he is Uthman ibn Abi al-Salt, and it is said ibn al-Samit; they are like al-'Ajārida, but they said: whoever becomes Muslim and seeks protection with us, we befriend him and disavow his children until they reach maturity and are called to Islam and accept. And it is narrated from some of them that children, whether of Muslims or polytheists, have no alliance and no enmity until they reach maturity and are called to Islam and accept or reject. The tenth: among the sects of al-'Ajārida, al-Tha'āliba: he is Tha'lab ibn 'Amir; they said regarding the allegiance of children, whether young or old, until denial of the truth appears from them after puberty, and it has been transmitted from them also that children have no ruling of alliance or enmity until they mature; and they hold taking zakat from slaves if they are wealthy and giving it to them if they are poor. And they—i.e., al-Tha'āliba—split into four sects: the first: al-Akhunsiyya: the companions of Akhnas ibn Qays; they are like al-Tha'āliba except that they distinguished themselves from them by suspending judgment concerning whoever is in the abode of dissimulation among the people of the qibla, so they do not judge him with faith or disbelief except for one whose state they know, whether his faith or disbelief; and they prohibited assassination by killing their opponents and stealing from their wealth; and it is narrated from them that it is permissible to marry Muslim women to polytheists of their people. The second: al-Ma'bidiyya: he is Ma'bad ibn 'Abd al-Rahman; they opposed them—i.e., al-Akhunsiyya—regarding marriage, i.e., marrying Muslim women to polytheists; and they opposed al-Tha'āliba regarding zakat of slaves, i.e., taking it from them and giving it to them. The third: al-Shaybaniyya: he is Shayban ibn Salama; they said with coercion and negation of originated power. The fourth: al-Mukramiyya: he is Mukram ibn al-'Ajli; they said: the abandoner of prayer is an unbeliever not because of abandoning prayer but because of his ignorance of Allah, for whoever knows that He is aware of his secret and public and will recompense him for his obedience and disobedience, it is not conceivable that he would proceed to abandon prayer; and likewise every major sin, for its committer is an unbeliever due to his ignorance of Allah, for the reason we mentioned; and the friendship of Allah and enmity towards His servants is based on the outcome and what they are destined for at the time of death, not based on their deeds that they are in, for they are not guaranteed to continue; and likewise we: whoever reaches the state of death, if he is a believer in that state, we befriend him, and if he is an unbeliever, we take enmity towards him.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of four specific Khawarij sub-sects belonging to the 'Ajārida branch, each with its distinctive doctrinal positions. The author first describes al-Ma'lumiyya: they define faith as knowing Allah with all His names and attributes; failure to do so results in ignorance, not faith. They also affirm that human acts are created by Allah. Next, al-Majhuliyya hold a similar position but relax the requirement: knowing Allah with only some of His names is sufficient for faith. Then al-Saltiyya, attributed to Uthman ibn Abi al-Salt, follow the 'Ajārida in general but add specific rulings on children: they only befriend converts and disavow their children until they reach maturity and accept Islam; some narrations extend this to all children, Muslim or polytheist, with no alliance or enmity until maturity. Finally, al-Tha'āliba, founded by Tha'lab ibn 'Amir, affirm the allegiance of children until they explicitly reject truth after puberty; they also hold that children have no legal status until maturity, and they have unique rulings on zakat for slaves. The Tha'āliba then split into four sub-sects: al-Akhunsiyya, who suspend judgment on people in the abode of dissimulation (taqiyya) regarding faith, prohibit assassination and theft from opponents, and permit marrying Muslim women to polytheists of their own people. Al-Ma'bidiyya oppose al-Akhunsiyya on marriage and oppose al-Tha'āliba on slave zakat. Al-Shaybaniyya advocate coercion (jabr) and deny originated power. Al-Mukramiyya consider the abandoner of prayer an unbeliever due to ignorance of Allah, extending this to all major sins; they base divine friendship and enmity on one's final state at death, not on current deeds, since those are not guaranteed to persist.

Key Terms
المعلومية
المجهولية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What distinguishes al-Ma'lumiyya from al-Majhuliyya?
A) al-Ma'lumiyya require knowing all of Allah's names and attributes; al-Majhuliyya require only some.
B) al-Ma'lumiyya believe human acts are not created; al-Majhuliyya believe they are.
C) al-Ma'lumiyya reject al-Hazimiyya; al-Majhuliyya follow them.
D) al-Ma'lumiyya consider children believers; al-Majhuliyya do not.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ma'lumiyya and al-Majhuliyya differ in the extent of divine knowledge required for faith, but both insist that faith depends on such knowledge and affirm that human acts are created by Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to be judged by the standard of al-Ma'lumiyya—requiring knowledge of all of Allah's names and attributes—would you be considered a believer? How does that feel, and what does it reveal about your own diligence in seeking knowledge of Him?
?
Al-Majhuliyya settled for knowing 'some' of Allah's names. Do you ever settle for a superficial knowledge of Allah, content with just enough to feel safe? What would it cost you to truly strive to know Him more?

al-Saltiyya: Rulings on Converts and Their Children
Definition of the Saltiyya sub-sect and its rulings on children.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the unique position of al-Saltiyya regarding the status of children of converts and the suspension of judgment until maturity.

Core Idea
Allegiance and disavowal depend on personal acceptance of Islam, not birth.

Among the Khawarij, al-Saltiyya stands out for its rulings on children. While following the general 'Ajārida doctrine, they introduce a suspension of judgment: a child of a convert is not automatically considered a believer or disbeliever until they reach maturity and make their own choice. This lesson explores that distinctive view.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on al-Saltiyya
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the two reported opinions: one restricts the ruling to children of those who seek protection, the other extends it to all children.
2
Identify the key principle
The central principle is that children have no religious status until they are old enough to understand and accept or reject Islam. This contrasts with other Khawarij who might automatically assign status based on parentage.
3
Reflect on the implications
Why might a sect adopt this view? It emphasizes personal responsibility and the rejection of inherited faith. Consider how this aligns with Khawarij emphasis on individual judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

al-Tha'āliba: The Status of Children and Zakat on Slaves
Definition of the Tha'āliba sub-sect and its doctrines on children and zakat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the dual positions of al-Tha'āliba regarding children (allegiance until rejection) and zakat obligations for slaves.

Core Idea
Children start as believers until they deny the truth; slaves can give and receive zakat.

Al-Tha'āliba, another 'Ajārida sub-sect, takes a nuanced stance on children: unlike al-Saltiyya, they initially affirm allegiance to children until they explicitly reject truth after puberty. They also have a distinctive view on zakat, allowing its collection from slaves and distribution to them. This lesson unpacks these positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on al-Tha'āliba
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two reported views on children: one says they are under allegiance until they reject truth after puberty; another says they have no ruling until maturity.
2
Analyze the zakat ruling
Al-Tha'āliba permits taking zakat from slaves if they are wealthy and giving it to them if they are poor. This contrasts with mainstream views that generally exclude slaves from zakat obligations or benefits.
3
Compare with earlier sects
How does al-Tha'āliba's position on children differ from al-Saltiyya's? Al-Tha'āliba leans toward initial inclusion (allegiance) until rejection, whereas al-Saltiyya suspends judgment entirely until maturity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابعة : المعلومية هم كالحازمية إلا أن المؤمن عندهم من عرف الله بجميع أسمائه وصفاته، ومن لم يعرفه كذلك فهو جاهل لا مؤمن، وفعل العبد مخلوق لله تعالى . الثامنة : المجهولية : مذهبهم كمذهب الحازمية أيضاً إلا أنهم قالوا : يكفي معرفته تعالى ببعض أسمائه فمن علمه كذلك فهو عارف به مؤمن، وفعل العبد مخلوق لله تعالى . التاسعة : الصلتية : هو عثمان بن أبي الصلت وقيل: بن الصامت هم كالعجاردة، لكن قالوا من أسلم واستجار بنا توليناه وبرئنا من أطفاله حتى يبلغوا فيدعوا إلى الإسلام فيقبلوا، وروي عن بعضهم أن الأطفال سواء كانوا للمسلمين أو المشركين لا ولاية لهم ولا عداوة حتى يبلغوا فيدعوا إلى الإسلام ويقبلوا أو ينكروا . العاشرة : من فرق العجاردة الثعالبة : هو ثعلب بن عامر قالوا بولاية الأطفال صغاراً كانوا أو كباراً حتى يظهر منهم إنكار الحق بعد البلوغ، وقد نقل عنهم أيضاً أن الأطفال لا حكم لهم من ولاية أو عداوة إلى أن يدركوا، ويرون أخذ الزكاة من العبيد إذا استغنوا وإعطاءها لهم إذا افتقروا . وتفرقوا أي الثعالبة أربع فرق : الأولى : الأخنسية : أصحاب أخنس بن قيس هم كالثعالبة إلا أنهم امتازوا عنهم بأن توقفوا فيمن هو في دار التقية من أهل القبلة فلم يحكموا عليه بإيمان ولا كفر إلا ممن علم حاله من إيمانه أو كفره، وحرموا الاغتيال بالقتل لمخالفيهم والسرقة من أموالهم، ونقل عنهم أنه يجوز تزويج المسلمات من مشركي قومهم . الثانية المعبدية : هو معبد بن عبد الرحمن خالفوهم أي الأخنسية في التزويج أي تزويج المسلمات من المشركين وخالفوا الثعالبة في زكاة العبيد أي أخذها منهم ودفعها إليهم . الثالثة : الشيبانية: هو شيبان بن سلمة، قالوا بالجبر ونفي القدرة الحادثة . الرابعة : المكرمية: هو مكرم بن العجلي، قالوا : تارك الصلاة كافر لا لترك الصلاة بل لجهله بالله، فإن من علم أنه مطلع على سره وعلنه ومجازيه على طاعته ومعصيته لا يتصور منه الإقدام على ترك الصلاة، وكذا كل كبيرة فإن مرتكبها كافر لجهله بالله لما ذكرناه، وموالاة الله ومعاداته لعباده باعتباره العاقبة وما هم صائرون إليه عند موافاة الموت لا باعتبار أعمالهم التي هم فيها، إذ هي غير موثوق بدوامها، وكذا نحن فمن وصل إلى حالة الموت فإن كان مؤمناً في تلك الحالة واليناه وإن كان كافراً عاديناه.
The seventh: al-Ma'lumiyya: they are like al-Hazimiyya except that the believer according to them is the one who knows Allah with all His names and attributes, and whoever does not know Him thus is ignorant, not a believer, and the act of the slave is created by Allah Almighty. The eighth: al-Majhuliyya: their doctrine is like the doctrine of al-Hazimiyya also except that they said: knowledge of Him Almighty with some of His names suffices; so whoever knows Him thus is a knower of Him, a believer, and the act of the slave is created by Allah Almighty. The ninth: al-Saltiyya: he is Uthman ibn Abi al-Salt, and it is said ibn al-Samit; they are like al-'Ajārida, but they said: whoever becomes Muslim and seeks protection with us, we befriend him and disavow his children until they reach maturity and are called to Islam and accept. And it is narrated from some of them that children, whether of Muslims or polytheists, have no alliance and no enmity until they reach maturity and are called to Islam and accept or reject. The tenth: among the sects of al-'Ajārida, al-Tha'āliba: he is Tha'lab ibn 'Amir; they said regarding the allegiance of children, whether young or old, until denial of the truth appears from them after puberty, and it has been transmitted from them also that children have no ruling of alliance or enmity until they mature; and they hold taking zakat from slaves if they are wealthy and giving it to them if they are poor. And they—i.e., al-Tha'āliba—split into four sects: the first: al-Akhunsiyya: the companions of Akhnas ibn Qays; they are like al-Tha'āliba except that they distinguished themselves from them by suspending judgment concerning whoever is in the abode of dissimulation among the people of the qibla, so they do not judge him with faith or disbelief except for one whose state they know, whether his faith or disbelief; and they prohibited assassination by killing their opponents and stealing from their wealth; and it is narrated from them that it is permissible to marry Muslim women to polytheists of their people. The second: al-Ma'bidiyya: he is Ma'bad ibn 'Abd al-Rahman; they opposed them—i.e., al-Akhunsiyya—regarding marriage, i.e., marrying Muslim women to polytheists; and they opposed al-Tha'āliba regarding zakat of slaves, i.e., taking it from them and giving it to them. The third: al-Shaybaniyya: he is Shayban ibn Salama; they said with coercion and negation of originated power. The fourth: al-Mukramiyya: he is Mukram ibn al-'Ajli; they said: the abandoner of prayer is an unbeliever not because of abandoning prayer but because of his ignorance of Allah, for whoever knows that He is aware of his secret and public and will recompense him for his obedience and disobedience, it is not conceivable that he would proceed to abandon prayer; and likewise every major sin, for its committer is an unbeliever due to his ignorance of Allah, for the reason we mentioned; and the friendship of Allah and enmity towards His servants is based on the outcome and what they are destined for at the time of death, not based on their deeds that they are in, for they are not guaranteed to continue; and likewise we: whoever reaches the state of death, if he is a believer in that state, we befriend him, and if he is an unbeliever, we take enmity towards him.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of four specific Khawarij sub-sects belonging to the 'Ajārida branch, each with its distinctive doctrinal positions. The author first describes al-Ma'lumiyya: they define faith as knowing Allah with all His names and attributes; failure to do so results in ignorance, not faith. They also affirm that human acts are created by Allah. Next, al-Majhuliyya hold a similar position but relax the requirement: knowing Allah with only some of His names is sufficient for faith. Then al-Saltiyya, attributed to Uthman ibn Abi al-Salt, follow the 'Ajārida in general but add specific rulings on children: they only befriend converts and disavow their children until they reach maturity and accept Islam; some narrations extend this to all children, Muslim or polytheist, with no alliance or enmity until maturity. Finally, al-Tha'āliba, founded by Tha'lab ibn 'Amir, affirm the allegiance of children until they explicitly reject truth after puberty; they also hold that children have no legal status until maturity, and they have unique rulings on zakat for slaves. The Tha'āliba then split into four sub-sects: al-Akhunsiyya, who suspend judgment on people in the abode of dissimulation (taqiyya) regarding faith, prohibit assassination and theft from opponents, and permit marrying Muslim women to polytheists of their own people. Al-Ma'bidiyya oppose al-Akhunsiyya on marriage and oppose al-Tha'āliba on slave zakat. Al-Shaybaniyya advocate coercion (jabr) and deny originated power. Al-Mukramiyya consider the abandoner of prayer an unbeliever due to ignorance of Allah, extending this to all major sins; they base divine friendship and enmity on one's final state at death, not on current deeds, since those are not guaranteed to persist.

Key Terms
الثعالبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Tha'āliba, what is one view on children's religious status?
A) Children have no ruling until maturity.
B) Children are automatically disbelievers.
C) Children are considered polytheists.
D) Children who cannot speak are exempt.

Key Takeaway
Al-Tha'āliba held that children are initially under allegiance until they reject truth after puberty, or alternatively have no status until maturity; they also allowed zakat transactions with slaves.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Tha'āliba considered children under allegiance until they denied the truth. Do you default to assuming good faith in others, or are you quick to judge? How would your relationships change if you presumed belief until proven otherwise?
?
They allowed giving zakat to slaves, recognizing their dignity and need. Who in your life is overlooked because of their social status? What specific action can you take this week to serve or support someone who is marginalized?

Sects and Disagreements
advanced
8 min
Four Sub-Sects of the Tha'āliba: al-Akhunsiyya, al-Ma'bidiyya, al-Shaybaniyya, al-Mukramiyya
Enumeration of four sub-sects of al-Tha'āliba with their doctrinal specifics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinctive doctrines of the four sub-sects that emerged from al-Tha'āliba, particularly on taqiyya, marriage, jabr, and the definition of unbelief.

Core Idea
Four branches, four distinctive rulings on judgment, marriage, determinism, and sin.

Al-Tha'āliba did not remain monolithic; they fragmented into four sub-sects, each with its own nuanced positions. From suspending judgment on people in taqiyya to declaring the abandoner of prayer an unbeliever due to ignorance, these groups illustrate the internal diversity of Khawarij thought. This lesson surveys all four.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage on the four sub-sects
Read the Arabic and translation from 'وتفرقوا' to the end. Each sub-sect is introduced by a number: first, second, third, fourth.
2
Identify the key doctrine of each sub-sect
For each: al-Akhunsiyya (suspension of judgment in taqiyya, prohibition of assassination and theft, permissible intermarriage with polytheists); al-Ma'bidiyya (oppose al-Akhunsiyya on marriage, oppose al-Tha'āliba on slave zakat); al-Shaybaniyya (jabr, denial of acquired power); al-Mukramiyya (abandoner of prayer is kafir due to ignorance, final state determines friendship/enmity).
3
Compare with parent sect al-Tha'āliba
Notice how each sub-sect modifies or opposes specific positions of al-Tha'āliba or each other. This shows the dynamic nature of sectarian splits.
4
Reflect on the Mukramiyya position
The Mukramiyya's reasoning is detailed: the abandoner of prayer must be ignorant of Allah, which constitutes kufr. Consider the logical chain and how it differs from other groups that may consider the act itself as kufr.

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of four specific Khawarij sub-sects belonging to the 'Ajārida branch, each with its distinctive doctrinal positions. The author first describes al-Ma'lumiyya: they define faith as knowing Allah with all His names and attributes; failure to do so results in ignorance, not faith. They also affirm that human acts are created by Allah. Next, al-Majhuliyya hold a similar position but relax the requirement: knowing Allah with only some of His names is sufficient for faith. Then al-Saltiyya, attributed to Uthman ibn Abi al-Salt, follow the 'Ajārida in general but add specific rulings on children: they only befriend converts and disavow their children until they reach maturity and accept Islam; some narrations extend this to all children, Muslim or polytheist, with no alliance or enmity until maturity. Finally, al-Tha'āliba, founded by Tha'lab ibn 'Amir, affirm the allegiance of children until they explicitly reject truth after puberty; they also hold that children have no legal status until maturity, and they have unique rulings on zakat for slaves. The Tha'āliba then split into four sub-sects: al-Akhunsiyya, who suspend judgment on people in the abode of dissimulation (taqiyya) regarding faith, prohibit assassination and theft from opponents, and permit marrying Muslim women to polytheists of their own people. Al-Ma'bidiyya oppose al-Akhunsiyya on marriage and oppose al-Tha'āliba on slave zakat. Al-Shaybaniyya advocate coercion (jabr) and deny originated power. Al-Mukramiyya consider the abandoner of prayer an unbeliever due to ignorance of Allah, extending this to all major sins; they base divine friendship and enmity on one's final state at death, not on current deeds, since those are not guaranteed to persist.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Mukramiyya consider the act of abandoning prayer itself as kufr, but they attribute it to ignorance.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that the abandoner of prayer is kafir 'not because of abandoning prayer but because of his ignorance of Allah.'

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Mukramiyya's reason for considering the abandoner of prayer an unbeliever?
A) Because abandoning prayer is a major sin that automatically removes one from Islam.
B) Because the person must be ignorant of Allah, as true knowledge would prevent abandoning prayer.
C) Because they follow the doctrine of jabr and deny free will.
D) Because they reject the obligation of prayer altogether.

Key Takeaway
The four sub-sects of al-Tha'āliba illustrate the extreme internal diversification of Khawarij thought, producing distinct rulings on taqiyya, interfaith marriage, determinism, and the nature of unbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mukramiyya argue that if you truly knew Allah, you would not abandon prayer. When you skip a prayer or commit a sin, do you truly feel the weight of Allah's knowledge and recompense? What does your action reveal about the depth of your knowledge of Him?
?
The text says our friendship and enmity should be based on the final state at death, not on current deeds. Are you treating fellow Muslims as if their current sins define them forever? Does the way you interact with a sinful brother reflect hope for their end or judgment of their present?

Definition and Etymology of the Murji'ah
Definition of the Murji'ah and two etymologies of their name.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the term 'Murji'ah' and the two etymological explanations for their name.

Core Idea
The Murji'ah are named for deferring action after faith, either in rank or in consequence.

The Murji'ah are one of the major early Islamic sects. To understand their distinctive theology, we must first grasp the meaning of their name. The passage explains two possible etymologies and clarifies how the word should be pronounced.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on definition and name
Read the Arabic passage carefully and its translation. Note the two explanations given for the term 'irjā'.
2
Identify the two etymologies
The first etymology relates to deferring action from intention; the second relates to giving hope (rajā'). Understand how each leads to the name.
3
Note the pronunciation rule
The passage states that based on the first etymology, the word should not be pronounced with a hamza. This shows how etymology affects usage.
This subtle point matters for correct reading of the term.
